I Still Shut My Eyes

by kayniiine

Summary

Once upon a time, life was perfect for Agatha and Rio Harkness-Vidal. In their early thirties, they both had thriving careers and a home life that was made immaculate with the arrival of their son, Nicholas.

Four months after his birth and after the recruitment of a nanny, Rio arrives home to an empty house and no trace of her son or the nanny.

What first seemed hopeful carries on for twenty-five very long years until suddenly, the unthinkable happens.

In The Big Apple, a mere car ride away from the Harkness-Vidal home in Newark, a twenty-five year old physical therapist who has always wondered about his mother's avoidance about his other parent decides to take an ancestry test. His girlfriend bought it for him for his birthday and, well, if his mother won't provide answers to his questions, he'll get them on his own.

When his sample flags as a match to a two-and-a-half decade old DNA sample from a missing person's case, he gets far more of them than he ever could have imagined.

Chapter 1: Once I'm Alive Again

April 18th, 2000

Rio.

She had only been ten minutes late.

Rio Harkness-Vidal was never late, but her consult with the representatives of a large commercial banking company that her company would be catering a massive event for had run eight minutes over.

It had taken her two minutes to pee on her way out.

After washing her hands, Rio took a quick survey in the mirror. She was met by rich amber eyes and tousled dark hair that was poorly maintained in a low bun. There was a soft dusting of freckles that seemed to pop whenever her cheeks went rosy. Well, at least she was just going home. She grabbed her phone and shot a text to the nanny that had been taking care of her son, Nicky. Agatha, her wife, had known days ahead of time that on that day in particular, she was going to be home late.

Rio had thought that at some point on her way home, she would get a text back from Wanda with some kind of update. Then again...

Rio grabbed her Blackberry out of the cupholder and did something she knew Agatha would choke her for -- not in the fun way -- and dug through her inbox while she drove. When she pulled up her messages with Wanda, she noticed for the first time that they were rather... empty. Normally the nanny would send her updates on their day or photos of Nicky. If not to her alone, then to the group message the three women occupied for the sake of Nicky's care.

It had been four months since Agatha had given birth to their son and while going back to a normal work schedule had been hard on the both of them, Rio had told herself time and time again that it was simply a fact of life, something they had to perpetuate as adults. The duty of responsibility could be fickle in that way.

The search for a nanny had been tricky, to say the least. While Rio tended to make decisions based on observations, Agatha made them on judgements. Agatha took all that she saw at face value and made a decision on the spot.

Perhaps therein lie the current issue: Agatha had deemed Wanda Maximoff suitable to care for their son pretty quickly, though she had followed up with a thorough vetting after the fact.

And yet, Rio was only ten minutes late and the house was empty.

Oh, and Wanda still hadn't answered her text messages.

Rio checked the time and cursed from her place in the middle of the living room, knowing full well that Agatha was in surgery for at least another hour.

That gave Rio time to figure out what the fuck was going on.

Where the fuck was Wanda?

More importantly, where the fuck was Nicky?

Even though she had done it once upon arriving, Rio searched the house again. Wanda usually took a cab, so the fact that there was no car was of no consequence. Her pace was unhindered as she sped through the house, checking every room.

Den: empty.

Living room: empty.

Office: empty.

Bathroom: empty.

She took the stairs two at a time to check the upper story.

Nicky's room: empty.

Hers and Agatha's room: empty.

Where the fuck was Nicky?

Rio tried calling Wanda again. This time, it didn't even ring and just went straight to voicemail. She tried again, just for good measure, only to be met with the same result. Now, Rio was beginning to panic.

Where the fuck could Wanda have possibly gone and why had she not let Rio know? Agatha, that was understandable because she was in an operating room more hours of the day than she was not, but she always could have messaged Rio, or even called. She wasn't always able to pick up right away, but if she ever saw a missed call, especially from Wanda, she called back immediately.

In her panic, Rio was struggling to figure out the right thing to do. She should sit and wait, maybe Wanda would come back. If she didn't come back, Agatha would surely accost Rio up and down for staying idle and not making more of an effort in the span of an hour. So what the fuck did she do? Where did she even start?

She would go to Wanda's. It wasn't that far and she could probably get there within ten minutes if she gave little regard to the majority of traffic laws.

So that was what Rio did.

When she got there, something akin to dread began to fill her stomach, swirling and churning like she simply knew something was wrong even before she approached the door. The knocking was more of a banging as Rio's fist thudded against the wood.

"Wanda? Wanda, are you in there? Wanda?!" Rio called, thumping her fist to the door again.

She waited, but an answer never came.

With a disregard for Wanda's privacy at that point, Rio tried the door handle.

It opened.

Rio pushed it, revealing more of the interior of the house. What she found inside caused her to throw up onto the hardwood.

Judging by the several missing items and the disheveled state of what was left, Wanda had vacated in a hurry. And it did not look like she planned on coming back.

No. No, this could not be happening. Wanda had simply absconded with their fucking kid?! What the fuck was actually going on?!

Rio tried to call her again. And again. And again and again. Still standing in Wanda's kitchen, Rio had called her 25 times. Every time, she only got Wanda's voicemail. 15 of those times, she left scathing messages where she shouted that Wanda needed to call her as soon as she could and explain what the fuck was going on.

Checking the time once more, Rio's stomach melted into the floor, already void of its contents. Agatha would be finishing work soon and Rio had no idea how to explain this. How did she tell her wife that she had come home to an empty house and Wanda and Nicky were nowhere to be found? How did she explain to Agatha that she had only been ten minutes late, as if that were the reason this had happened in the first place when it clearly was not?

Where did one even look for someone who had no car and wasn't either of the two places she was supposed to be?

Rio bit down on her lip, hard enough that she almost immediately tasted the copper on the tip of her tongue. She stared down at her phone, her indecision nearly crippling her. She needed to text Agatha. She needed to at least tell her wife to call her the moment she could, and they could go from there.

Right?

 

Agatha.

Microsurgical resections were getting easier. At least, they'd gotten to be that way after the fourth one Agatha Harkness-Vidal had performed. It was something she could do with ease, something that felt almost automatic anymore. Sure, every patient could be different, but those processes stayed all the same.

As Agatha stripped herself of her outerwear -- including her gown, gloves and scrub cap that had been maintaining that wild light brown mane of hair, one that couldn't be tamed by the bun she'd thrown it in -- she let her thoughts drift homeward, to what would be awaiting her after an impossibly long day. She was tired and wanted nothing more than to make her way home, shower off the day, and curl up on the couch with her wife and their four-month-old to decompress.

It had been a successful day, but it had been difficult and exhausting in a way that Agatha loved, but still lost energy over. All she needed was leftover stir fry and the love of her family and she would be recharged and ready to take on the following day.

By the time Agatha had been able to retrieve her phone from her locker, nothing had felt amiss. Not until she checked her messages and had 12 from Rio over the span of an hour.

I need you to call me when you see this.

I know you're in surgery right now, but as soon as you see this call me.

Agatha I don't know what to do.

I searched the whole fucking house.

Wanda is gone.

What the fuck did that mean? How could Wanda be gone?

Agatha kept scrolling, watching as Rio's hysteria visibly grew in text.

She's not at the house.

She's not at her house.

She won't answer her phone.

Agatha, I don't know what the fuck to do.

Do I call the police?

Agatha I have no fucking clue what to do.

It was the last message that made every one before it make perfect sense.

She has Nicky. She took Nicky with her.

SHE WHAT?

Agatha's first reaction should have been to call Rio, to get a full briefing of what the fuck was actually going on. She should have checked on her wife, tried to comfort her in some way while they got this figured out.

Instead, Agatha chose to call Wanda.

She was fucking furious when her voicemail picked up immediately. The moment that beep sounded, all hell was unleashed and Agatha did not care who in that hospital heard her.

"Wanda fucking Maximoff, if you do not call one of us back AS SOON AS FUCKING POSSIBLE, I swear to God I will scour this fucking city from top to bottom to find you AND SO HELP ME GOD you will regret whatever the fuck you are thinking by DISAPPEARING WITH MY FUCKING SON! So if you have any GODDAMN SENSE in that fucking head of yours, YOU WILL CALL ONE OF US BACK IMMEDIATELY."

Agatha nearly broke her phone in the act of disconnecting the call, punching the red phone button with hysteric fury.

After grabbing her jacket and nearly sprinting through the hospital, Agatha was in her car and flying toward home before she had enough sense fill her to know she needed to call her wife. She dialed out and put the phone on speaker so she could keep driving. When Rio answered, she sounded frenzied and unrestrained.

"Agatha, I'm --"

"Where are you?!" Agatha snapped, cutting her off. Her head whipped over her shoulder as she changed lanes abruptly, missing the nose of the car behind her by mere inches.

"I'm at Wanda's. The cops are here. I called them a few minutes after the last message I sent you. I... I didn't know what else to do."

Rio sounded so fucking upset and while Agatha understood it, she couldn't relate. Agatha was fucking angry, so angry that she was certain her body temperature had raised at least five degrees.

"I'm on my way there now. It should only be a couple of minutes." Agatha's voice was sharp and cold like the blade of a pristine and new hunting knife, slicing right through the line and consequently, right through her wife.

"I'm sorry, Agatha... I... I was only ten minutes late." Rio's voice started to break over her words and something in Agatha aligned with reality.

Even though it still came out cold, Agatha meant what she had to say. "Rio, she was gone longer than ten minutes. You being on time wouldn't have made a difference."

"I... I know, I just..."

This was what happened when major crises occurred. Rio panicked. Agatha got angry.

In those moments, speeding through the streets of Newark, Agatha was more than just angry. The rage she was feeling that was only amplified by her anxiety and it was overwhelming her. She couldn't break down behind the wheel of a car and she could not wreck it before she got to Wanda's house, but Agatha wanted to scream. She wanted to throw something and hit something and come undone in her fury. She couldn't do that if she died before meeting solid ground again.

How the fuck had this happened? How had she been so convinced that they had found someone trustworthy enough to care for their son and let this unfold as a result? Agatha had been fooled, which was quite a difficult feat to manage, but it left her wondering: How long had this been the plan? Did Wanda just wake up that morning and decide to kidnap a child? Their child?

Perhaps therein lie the root of why this had enraged her: She had pushed for Wanda. She had been so confident that those judgements she'd made were fair and safe. There had been a genuine sense of trust there, and she felt like a fucking idiot. Never could she imagined that the woman would be capable of such insane levels of duplicity and yet, there Agatha sat in that car fighting to not stomp the gas pedal to the floor.

She took a breath at the sound of Rio sniffling on the other end of the line.

"Rio," Agatha voiced, glancing down at her phone where it sat on her knee for the briefest moment before looking back to the road. "This isn't your fault. If anything, it's mind for trusting that stupid bitch."

Rio sniffled again.

"Are you almost here?" Rio asked in a squeak right as Agatha turned the corner onto Wanda's street.

"I'm pulling up now."

 

May 5th, 2000

Rio.

It had been seventeen days since Rio and Agatha had last seen their son the morning they each kissed him on the forehead and bid him a well behaved day for the nanny.

It had been seventeen days since said nanny had disappeared. With him.

If Agatha found Wanda before the cops did, she was surely going to prison because she was going to kill her.

Neither of them had been sleeping, spending hours hunched over laptops and on phone calls with too many detectives to count. It was an all-hands-on-deck affair until Nicky was back in their arms.

What had made it almost impossible was that Wanda had no known vehicle. She had no car to track, no way to visibly gauge where she might be going without having to see her in person. It was frustrating to no end and while Rio did not shed those exasperated tears in front of Agatha, she let them loose in the quiet moments alone, tucked in their downstairs bathroom. She let go of them after Agatha exhausted herself to sleep. Those were the only times Rio could cry those tears.

Agatha on the other hand only cried when she was pissed. It wasn't even that she was crying, it was just that she was so angry and her body temperature had grown feverish to a point that it simply made her eyes water. Her face had been red for weeks and every single moment of her day was spent doing whatever she could to locate their son.

Neither of them had worked a minute in those seventeen days and had devoted every bit of the time they had into the search. It was all that could have occupied their time while their son was somewhere out there without them.

Rio had been afraid. Even though Agatha had made it clear time and time again that it was not Rio's fault, she still felt as though Agatha were just looking for the best reason to blow up on her, to somehow use this as a reason to tear apart everything they had built up to that point. Agatha was angry and she could be irrational in that emotion.

It had yet to come. That was shocking in and of itself, but Rio knew better than to question small miracles. Instead, they had come together to cover every lead they could, track down every small clue they had been given.

It just hadn't been enough.

The police were still doing their due diligence, but Rio could see what was starting to happen.

Everyone else was beginning to give up.

Their friends were still showing up, and Rio's mother Lilia was still losing sleep in her efforts to scour hotels and motels with the hopes that she might be able to at least convince someone to agree that they had spotted someone matching Wanda's description. She had come up empty each and every time.

The people that mattered, they weren't giving up.

The police were slowly losing hope. It had started two days after, but creeping up on three weeks it seemed as though their reserves for giving a shit had been depleted.

That made Rio even angrier than the entire situation did in the first place, which was saying something. It also pissed Agatha off to no end the last two days when every single one of her calls with the cops ended up with her slamming her phone down and screaming out in unending frustration.

This time, on that particular night seventeen nights in, when Agatha was mid-shout at whoever was on the other line and they hung up on her, the cellphone shattered when she smashed it against the desk, the Blackberry falling to too many pieces to count.

"Fucking useless pigs! All of them!" she screamed, swiping the pieces of the phone off of the desk and onto the floor below. The moment that task was completed, Agatha slammed both fists down in a move that Rio heard and was certain had to hurt.

Timidly, Rio paced to the doorway and leaned against the frame, her concerned gaze falling on her wife though she already knew what was happening without being told.

"They're diluting the task force, aren't they?" Rio asked softly.

When Agatha looked up at her from her place behind that desk, those angry tears were burning molten rivers down her bright red cheeks.

"Fuck them. Tax dollars hard at work as they sit on their fucking asses drinking their sludge coffee and finger-fuck their own assholes," Agatha snapped.

Rio didn't take it personally. Honestly, she felt the exact same way but she was a little more reserved in her wording because of the two of them, she tried to be that voice of reason.

There was no reason. Not for what Wanda had done.

"It's getting late," Rio offered, her voice low and quiet. It was nearing on eleven pm and neither of them had slept more than an hour or two per night the last two weeks. "We really should get some sleep. We can pick it up in the morning."

Agatha leaned back in her chair, raising both palms so that she could use the heels to dry her eyes and then her cheeks. Rio was the only person in the world who wasn't afraid of seeing Agatha cry. It was because she knew what it meant. It meant hurt and uncertainty. Agatha didn't get sappy or sad or dejected when she cried. No, it was just pure fury time and time again.

"I'm not ready to give up, not like they are," Agatha argued back, though there was a notable tightness to her tone that felt like a lead weight in Rio's middle.

Slowly, Rio paced into the room to place herself behind Agatha, tender fingertips sinking into the meat of her trap muscles, kneading and pressing lovingly despite the fact that the stress they had been dealing with had made those muscles hard as steel.

"We're never going to give up, my love," Rio assured her, leaning just enough to place a light kiss to the top of Agatha's head. "But we won't have a choice if we die from exhaustion in the process," she added in a soft murmur against her scalp.

"I just don't understand why they don't give a fuck," Agatha voiced through an exhaled sigh. "Now that the hubbub from the breaking news and headlines has died down, it's as if they just don't feel like it's worthy of their time. And I..." Agatha cut herself off, head dropping in defeat as it slipped out from beneath Rio's lips. "Nicky is fucking worth it. He's always been worth it."

"I know, Agatha," Rio soothed, working a little harder at trying to ease some of her tension. "And that's exactly why we're never giving up. Because he is worth it, and we will bring him home."

Rio had meant that statement with every ounce of will in her body.

Sometimes, it didn't matter, though.

Life could be cruel that way.

 

December 18th, 2000

Agatha.

It had been seven months to the day since Nicky had gone missing.

Agatha had never stopped searching.

Both herself and Rio had done everything they could. They checked hospitals and hotels, even ventured into New York to post flyers in hopes that someone might see Wanda and call the number in bold at the bottom of the page.

No call ever came.

Agatha had even hired a private investigator two months in and even that had not brought forth results. Wherever Wanda was, and wherever she had taken their son, she was untraceable. The more the days passed, the more Agatha realized that Wanda was slipping further and further from their reach and as a result, so was Nicky.

Despite the insanity of what the other woman had chosen to do, something in Agatha knew that even if no one knew where she was, Nicky was still okay. Wanda wouldn't have hurt him; if she was going to do that, she wouldn't have taken him and disappeared. Maybe it would have been beneficial to dig deeper, to press on the nearly imperceptible reaction Wanda had when Rio had asked if she had children. She'd said no, but there had been this strange look in her eyes, one that Agatha had mistakenly let go.

Somewhere out there, she now had their little boy and Agatha had no idea what that meant.

It kept her up most nights, even still. She and Rio had fallen into this strange routine where they would lay in bed and talk softly about next plans, about what more they could do, and then they would lie there and both pretend they were asleep when they really weren't. They had started getting a little more sleep when they'd had to return to work, but only due to the sleeping pills Agatha had procured for them and only because they needed to be coherent in their duties.

Agatha, more than Rio, had a duty of care to her patients, to every person who came through her OR that she do what she could to improve their lives. She could not be capable of that if she was depriving her body of what it needed to function. It was why she had taken a little longer in returning; Rio could run on two hours of sleep and four cups of coffee. Agatha could not, not safely anyway.

On that night, seven months without their son, Agatha came home to something unexpected.

When she had opened the front door, she was surprised to see that the majority of the furniture had been pushed aside and in the middle of the living room, Rio had spread out a quilt across the floor. Atop it, she had placed the low table and set up a dinner for them of homemade tamales, along with several different salsas that she had likely prepared herself as well. Between the two plates sat a bottle of red wine with the cork already popped and two awaiting glasses.

"Rio?" she called into the house as she shed her coat and hung it in the foyer closet.

"I'm in the kitchen, just finishing the rice. It took a little longer than I meant," she responded, her voice carrying from her place at the stove. A moment later, she appeared with two small bowls of the rice that she had perfected over the years, the warm orange color depicting just how robust with flavor it was.

"Well hi," Agatha greeted, clearly spent from the day behind her. She met Rio on the quilt at the edge of that low table to take a soft kiss. "What is all this for?"

Rio took the kiss happily, but she was not immediate in her response. Instead, when she pulled back, her bright amber eyes simply tracing over the features of Agatha's face as she sought out her answer.

"I decided that we've been punishing ourselves... and each other far more than we mean to. Not in that we treat each other like shit, but that we haven't much made time for ourselves or our marriage since..." For just a moment, Rio wavered. Her throat trembled noticeably at the forefront of her neck and her lips quivered just barely. Quickly, she cleared her throat and threaded some composure back into her form. "Since everything happened. And I just... I know you know it because you believe me when I say it, but I love you. And I... I know that our lives aren't going to be the same ever again, but I don't ever want to lose what we have in the process."

The longer she spoke, the more Agatha could feel her walls coming down. Sure, she had never once blamed Rio for what had happened. She had been angry, yes, and there were even times that she took it out on Rio because she was the only one within shouting distance (though Rio had gotten her back on a few occasions, mostly as it pertained to the police), but Agatha had never once stopped loving her.

It was in the early morning hours as they sat fully clothed, crying in a bathtub full of cold water as they clung to one another. It was in the weekend afternoons when Rio couldn't stop herself from looking inside the nursery which, more often than not, left her in a heap of tears on the hallway floor before Agatha came along to pick her up. It was in the late evenings when she would close Rio's laptop and request that she come to bed, even if she couldn't sleep.

For as unfair as life had been, Agatha wasn't the only one suffering. She wasn't the only one who was missing Nicky more than words could say, Rio just had a different way of showing it.

She showed it by doing things like this. In the throes of missing Nicky and fighting to find a way to bring him home, Rio had started to separate herself and apparently, it was something she had recognized. This was Rio looking Agatha in the eyes and saying what she was saying with her words, but also saying something more with that look in her eyes: I can't lose you, too.

Both of Agatha's palms raised and cradled Rio's jaw between them. She leaned in, not for a direct kiss, but to place them in several spots over Rio’s face from her cheeks to her forehead and even down to her chin. She could feel the muscles shift, tugging up on the corners of Rio's mouth at the attention Agatha was giving her.

Agatha felt that smile when she finally kissed her wife across those soft lips, too.

"I love you," Agatha whispered, pulling back only to kiss the tip of Rio's nose. "And dinner smells delicious. Let's eat."

 

August 15th, 2003

Rio.

In over a thousand days, there had not been a single one where Rio had not thought about her son.

He would be walking now. Talking. She wondered how many words he would know at that age, and how smart he might be. As much as she hated considering it, there was some part of Rio that hoped, somehow, if Wanda still had him that she'd been good to him through the years. He had been nothing more than a baby and deserved no evil to befall him. He deserved love, and if she had taken that right away from Rio and Agatha, she damn well better have been supplementing with what she could.

Nicky deserved that much.

Something in the passing weeks had changed, though.

Agatha still brought him up a couple of times a week, just to have a quiet or short conversation about him. The way Rio saw it, it was the one thing Agatha could do to make sure they would never forget about him, as if they ever could. In the last two, though, the frequency had lowered. More than that, she seemed a little more discombobulated and scattered. She was forgetting little things, like where she put her wallet or what time Rio would be coming home at night (even though it had been the same for the last year and a half).

They were minimal, really, but something in Rio recognized it as abnormal. She let it play out, though, knowing that if it got too bad and Agatha still hadn't wanted to discuss it, she would take any necessary action.

On a sticky fall evening, they had been out back as Rio worked in the vegetable troughs, clearing them of any of the foliage that had since died after harvest. Agatha had kept her plied with iced tea and a bowl of watermelon while she'd perched in a lawn chair and read. She had been contentedly munching on the fruit, but suddenly, she began to gag.

Rio snapped up, glancing over as Agatha ripped herself from the chair and bolted inside. Taking off her gloves, Rio was quick to follow her straight to the bathroom where she found Agatha kneeling at the toilet, the watermelon coming back up as a smoothie this time.

"My love," Rio voiced softly as she knelt next to Agatha, a hand gently rubbing over her back. Agatha straightened and wiped at her mouth before turning to look at Rio, her eyes wet from the vomiting. "I have been willfully neglecting to bring this up, but something's going on. Are you alright?"

Agatha's lip quivered for a moment and her eyes developed a new shine, one that radiated... fear?

"I don't know," she admitted, her lips twisting while those beautiful blue eyes searched Rio's face in a panic. "I... I've felt like this before but..."

She trailed a little too long and Rio suddenly felt overwhelmed with nerves at the way Agatha was looking at her.

"But?" Rio probed lightly, reaching up to cup Agatha's cheek, brushing it lightly with her thumb.

"But I was hoping it was just a bug... It's just been going on for too long and... And I... I..."

This time, when Agatha's eyes filled with tears, it wasn't because she was angry. It was because she was scared.

"Rio," she whispered, "I think I'm pregnant again."

Hearing those words, Rio wasn't sure if she was going to implode or explode, but either way she was not certain that her atoms were going to maintain corporeal form.

It wasn't something they had talked about, wasn't something they had planned for and while Rio trusted Agatha's instincts, they had to know for certain. Rio's hand had not stopped tending to its pacing up and down Agatha's back as they stared at each other like frightened animals, trapped and unsure where to go.

After a beat too long, Rio finally found the wherewithal to move, leaning toward her wife to brush their lips softly together. She didn't know if Agatha's hunch was right, or even what it meant if it was. What she did know was that there was really only one way to know for sure.

"I'm going to go grab a test, yeah?" she whispered before tilting her head back so that she could place a gentle kiss between Agatha's eyebrows. "Do you want me to grab anything else while I'm at the store?"

A sardonic chuckle passed through Agatha's lips as she leaned back so that she could wipe at her wet cheeks. She sniffled and nodded her head before she formed her answer. "One of those big boxes of caramel truffles for if it's positive and a bottle of Jack Honey if it's negative."

Despite the plethora of emotions that were violently coursing their way through Rio's entire being, she somehow found herself smiling and even breathing a soft laugh at Agatha's request.

"Of course, my love."

That night, they sat in bed eating caramel truffles and amassing a pile of wrappers that was far bigger than it needed to be.

The following Monday, the appointment they attended confirmed that they were, indeed, going to be having a second child.

That brought with it its own twisted and warped set of feelings. They had laid in bed with mostly untouched pasta set aside on their nightstands, wrapped in one another while they went through every inch of track on the rollercoaster of things they were trying to feel and understand.

They were happy, of course. It was another child, another opportunity to pour their love into a being they had created.

Then, they were devastated. It was a replacement of the one they never got to raise, even almost four years later.

No, that wasn't fair.

What happened to Nicky had not been their fault. All of this had happened for a reason.

Next, they were afraid. It had been a lengthy conversation, but Rio had ultimately decided that during Agatha's last trimester, she would either sell or dismantle her catering business and be a stay-at-home mom. She loved what she did and she had poured every drop of blood, sweat or tears into cultivating her own little empire, but this was more important. Having her family would always be the most important thing to Rio and no matter what she had to do to protect it, she absolutely would.

Finally, they were excited.

It had been long enough that while the shadow of what had happened to Nicky would always hang over them with the unanswered question of whether or not he was even still alive being dragged along with it, they had to move forward. A second child was likely the only thing that would have ever been capable of giving them the push they needed.

Rio was not foolish enough to think it would be easy, at least at first. Seeing a new baby and still being able to recall so easily what Nicky had looked like on that last morning, it was going to be emotional and it was going to be something that took effort to work through. Rio knew there would be other hurdles to overcome and she and Agatha had both decided that this new child would absolutely never be left in the care of someone who wasn't one of the two of them.

The talk had ended on a good note, but ten minutes later Agatha began to tremble against Rio's chest, her tears wetting the soft cotton on Rio's torso. 

Rio knew she was scared. Hell, Rio was too. Yes, it had been three years, but that fear had never left them. They both carried a piece of Nicky with them every single day in hopes that he might come back to them. The days that passed never did a thing to crack their resolve that someday, their son would come home.

 

April 18, 2004

Agatha.

Being eight and a half months pregnant was a feat in and of itself. Being eight and a half months pregnant at thirty-six years old was Olympic sport material. 

Agatha was tired. All of the time. 

Since she had stepped away from her duties as a neurosurgeon by way of maternity leave, Agatha's favorite way to pass the time was to nap. She could nap in the late morning, could nap in the early afternoon. Hell, sometimes she even took a nap at 5pm because she wanted to.

With Rio around more as well, -- as she had done as she'd promised and sold off her business for a hefty chunk of change due to the reputation that came with the name -- quite a few of those naps had consisted of cuddles and the lightest kisses as Rio whispered silly musings or quoted movie lines at her until she dozed off.

The exhaustion brought with it other consequences. It had been at least a week since Agatha had been able to muster the energy to leave the house. It wasn't that she didn't want to, but most of the time she wasn't sure how she'd be able to function in a public setting. 

Rio had noticed -- of course she had -- and had instructed Agatha to spend the majority of the afternoon napping so that they could go out for a very low key and low effort meal and stop by Agatha's favorite ice cream spot on the way home. For as tired as Agatha had been as of late, the suggestion actually sounded pretty tantalizing. 

They still had date nights every so often, but they had become fewer and farther between the further along Agatha got in her pregnancy. Rio still made more than enough effort by making copycat versions of Agatha's favorites, bringing home flowers any time she went out, and always drawing a hot bath at the end of the day for Agatha to soak in and alleviate the stress in her muscles.

So Agatha had done as she was told. She had climbed into that big bed and taken a kiss from Rio as she declared that she had a few things left to grab for the nursery's final touches.

Rio had been the one to tackle that project. They could have put the nursery for their baby girl in another room in the house, but Rio had been insistent that it was meant to be that room. It had taken her a couple of days to sort through things and clean out old clothes that Nicky never even got to really wear, but she had done it all the same. Agatha could see that it was getting to her, but she soldiered on and never let Agatha see her shed a tear.

Agatha knew she still shed them anyway.

When she had awoken from her nap, she took a few minutes to fully wake up, noting immediately that Rio had not joined her to rest or if she had, she'd gotten up before Agatha had come-to. When she sat up, she saw the purple lace and fabric maternity dress that Rio had laid out for her and an appreciative smile crossed her lips.

She and Rio had been married for nearly nine years and there really had yet to be a day where Agatha had not felt loved fully and appreciated wholly by her wife. They had been through hell and back together and while it had seemed, even for a moment, that they might not make it through, Rio had stepped up and did every single thing she needed do to ensure that they saw the light of day again. Rio pulled every string she could to prove that they would find happiness once more, and that they would live full lives when they'd resigned to only living half ones.

In the process of getting dressed, Agatha heard the blow dryer turn on in the adjoining bathroom; ah, Rio had been in the shower. 

Agatha had been in the midst of brushing her own wild and sleep-disturbed hair when Rio emerged, drawing Agatha's delighted blue gaze.

With her hair curled slightly in a way that bounced, there stood Rio in a long sleeved, dark green vintage dress that had a black belt with a gold buckle cinched snugly around her middle. There was a pin of the same tint of gold in her hair, keeping the left side clipped over her ear.

Rio was beautiful. Agatha had always known that, but in those moments, it was more than just her looks.

It was the fact that she had gotten dolled up, had let Agatha get dolled up. It was the fact that she had planned this dinner for them that, if Agatha had to guess, was probably a little less casual than she had initially let on -- or so Agatha had thought.

There had been a moment, one where Agatha almost asked if they could just order in. Something felt... off. She couldn't quite put her finger on it, but it felt to her as though her body was trying to tell her something, something she dismissed to embrace the prospect of spending a night out with her wife.

During their drive, the closer Rio got to Arlington Diner, the more suspicious Agatha grew. She did not say anything, at least not until Rio made the turn into the parking lot.

Agatha simply laughed.

Of course Rio had dressed them up to get a sandwich and some fries. Of course she had.

It was the million and eighth reason Agatha found to love her.

Rio got her usual of the portabella wrap and Agatha had opted for the pesto chicken panini, which she had been thoroughly enjoying until she felt the baby shift and press on her bladder.

"I'll be right back," she informed Rio. There had been every intention of just running to the restroom and coming right back to finish their meal, but when Agatha stood up and took only a step, she suddenly found a puddle of water at her feet and Rio staring up at her with impossibly wide and shocked eyes.

"Erm..." Agatha managed, not able to glance down at the proof her water had broken, but not needing it with the look Rio had slapped to her face.

"Maybe we should get you to the hospital... like now?" Rio asked, quickly pushing out of the booth so that she could rush to the counter and pay for their food. The server had been polite enough to ask if they wanted boxes, but Rio had kindly dismissed her with a 'thank you, though' before she turned her attention back to Agatha and getting her out to the car.

"Are you taking me to Clara Maass?" Agatha asked her as Rio carefully helped her slide into the car. When Rio reached down without being told and helped Agatha lower the seat backing to be more comfortable, Agatha could have kissed her. She was always so fucking thoughtful and always knew what to do, even in the face of panic.

"Yeah, it's the closest and... I know they were good to us last time," Rio answered. Before she shut the door to scramble to the driver's side, she leaned in to give Agatha a supportive and encouraging kiss.

And then, they were off.

 

Rio.

She had been there before.

Rio had existed in a delivery room that had looked almost exactly the same. She had stood dutifully by Agatha's bedside, holding her hand and letting Agatha squeeze the ever-loving fuck out of her knuckles, feeling as they bumped and rubbed against one another inside her skin. She had heard that cry, so similar yet so different.

Laying eyes on their little girl for the first time had also been a  familiar feeling and still somehow was so brand new. 

With a weak nod from Agatha who's grip slackened around Rio's fingers, Rio departed her station beside her wife to observe as the nurses cleaned her off, those little tiny wails sounding the entire time. She was beautiful with her dark hair and little ball-tipped nose. She was remarkable with those fat little cheeks and her wrinkled skin.

She was theirs and they would do whatever it took to see to it that she led a good life, one where they loved her every single day of it.

"Do you want to take her to momma for skin-to-skin?" the nurse asked Rio gently as she finished cleaning the newborn. She had finally stopped wailing and was instead making little frustrated coos and grunts.

"I would like that," came Rio's soft response.

As the nurse lifted the baby up and turned to Rio, she said something so innocent. It was so well-intentioned, but it felt like a lance through the heart.

"Just remember to support her head. New parents sometimes need to be reminded."

Rio smiled at her, but she could feel the threat of tears as they pricked at the backs of her eyes and for a moment, she almost stayed quiet. But, something took over her; it was a desire to assert Nicky's memory and remind herself that if he could be there to meet his little sister, he would have been.

"She's our second, but I do appreciate the reminder," Rio voiced, her tone a little pained as she held her hands out to receive all five pounds of their daughter. She cradled her easily as she made the short trek to Agatha's bed, her chest bare and skin ready to flush with the warm and new skin of their little girl.

"I proudly present Miss Danica Inez Harkness-Vidal," Rio announced in a voice that could have barely been constituted as a whisper.

"Hi, my Dani," Agatha greeted as Rio gently laid their daughter on her chest. Agatha's hand raised immediately, the tips of her fingers gracing that ridiculous amount of hair on Dani's head. A quiet chuckle passed through her lips as those tired but bright blue eyes lifted to Rio, the smallest smile on her lips. "All of the heartburn was worth it for this much hair."

Rio couldn't help but laugh. She leaned forward, her forearm steadying her as it pressed to the hospital bed above Agatha's head, her hand landing so that she could gently brush Agatha's hair back away from her still slightly-sweaty face. Her lips pressed softly to her wife's warm forehead and then her eyes dropped to their sweet little baby girl.

She was there. She was healthy. She was perfect.

And every god be damned, Rio would do absolutely anything in the world to ensure that the life Dani got to live was one more in their control than Nicky's had been.

No matter what needed to be done, Rio would do it, even if she died trying.

Perhaps such a sentiment could have seemed overdramatic. 

Not to Rio.

History would not repeat itself. 

Not again.

 

Chapter 2: Hold Together Our Bones

December 25th, 2004

Rio.

It was their very first Christmas as a family.

Nicky had been born on New Year's Day and so, he had just missed Christmas by a week. And then, well... That was something that still got thought about quite often, both for Rio as well as Agatha.

In those first few months with Dani, it was almost impossible not to think about Nicky. It was an unimaginable feat to try and not see the very obvious fact that they had the same tiny dimple in their chins, one that came from Agatha. It was physically not something Rio could do to not recognize that tiny little line in Dani's forehead and immediately picture Nicky's face to match it up.

Part of Nicky was with Dani, and always would be. It didn't matter where he was, he was going to help them take care of her one way or another, even if it was just his memory that would do the guiding. 

Being eight months old, there wasn't a lot to do by ways of gifts; Dani would never remember it anyway. What they could and had decided to do was dress in a matching set of pajamas and take photos. The pants were black, but one could hardly tell with the layers of red stripes and bigger ones of white polar bears that covered the length, the black filling the voids in between. The shirts had one singular polar bear wearing a Santa hat. Dani's, of course, was just a little baby bear onesie that Rio had wiggled the tiny pants over.

They sat on the couch as Agatha grumbled through the entire duration of 'It's A Wonderful Life' while sipping occasionally at her hot chocolate. It was one of Rio's favorite Christmas films, something she insisted on every year, though they had skipped it for the last four because life had not, in fact, been wonderful. Rio knew that this year, Agatha understood why she had pushed for it.

It hadn't been a wonderful life without Nicky.

Maybe it could be one as wonderful as humanly possible with Dani.

Agatha had been sunk back into the cushions of the couch with Dani positioned belly-down on her chest. When Rio went to ask Agatha if she wanted an additional hot chocolate even though it was eleven at night, she turned to see them both fast asleep, Dani's chest moving a little quicker than Agatha's due to her size.

For a moment, on a Christmas Day that Rio had never assumed could come, she felt like things might be okay. As she sat there and traced them both with her gaze, just outlining them in a sketch she could keep in her mind forever, Rio knew that despite the misery that had been brought into their lives, this was the reward they got for not sundering. This was the one thing they could have that would remind them that it was possible to rebuild after disaster.

They would keep building, day after day, for the rest of Dani's life until they were no longer around to do so.

Rio decided to let them sleep and got up to make herself another hot chocolate. Once she returned to the couch, she put on her second favorite Christmas movie, A Muppet Christmas Carol. They had already watched it once that day, but Rio would more than willingly indulge in an extra helping of the sheer chaos that was Rizzo the Rat.

Partway through the movie, when Gonzo caught Rizzo's tail on fire and the rat consequently screamed out "Light the lamp, not the rat! Light the lamp, not the rat!" Rio dissolved into giggles she tried to keep hushed. It didn't matter how many times she'd seen the movie or how old she got, that part was funny every single time without fail.

Unknowingly, she had woken her wife beside her who took a moment to rouse. She nearly scared Rio shitless when she spoke a couple minutes later.

"Seriously?" Agatha grunted sleepily, though she didn't move otherwise. "Again?"

"Oh, let me have my Christmas fun," came Rio's soft murmur. She leaned toward Agatha, placing the lightest kiss to her cheek. When she spoke again, it was both a whisper and warm against Agatha's skin. "Merry Christmas, my love. The best gift has been spending it with the two of you."

Rio could feel immediately the way Agatha's cheeks shifted with her tired smile. Her eyes were still closed but her head lulled to the side, a quiet beckoning for Rio to bring her lips closer and Rio was more than happy to respond in kind. Their mouths were gentle through such a connection, the lightest caress of a kiss before it broke.

"Why don't we head for bed? I think we have gotten the most out of the day that we could manage, hm?" Rio pulled away and shifted forward on the couch to collect their dishes and any wrappers or shreds of giftwrap from the gifts the two of them had exchanged earlier in the evening.

Agatha had gifted Rio with a Polaroid camera for one reason and one reason only: Rio loved to have physical copies of photos but she did not have the patience to go through the process of taking them to be developed. Agatha had decided to cut out the middleman, and it was just an additional bonus that it was an answer to a years long request that had begun before Nicky was even born.

Rio had gone a bit more sentimental. She knew Agatha's penchant for mildly flashy jewelry, as was evident by the ring Rio had placed on her finger those years ago when they'd said their vows, but she also knew that Agatha was a little old world and could appreciate a vintage piece a little more than the next person. When Rio had laid eyes on that locket, she had just... known.

It was a work of art, oval shaped and encircled in a frame of threaded gold, the tiniest loops like little arches all the way around. The small hinge was almost unnoticeable, overshadowed by the purple bubble and the etchings of three muses in white atop it. 

Charm, beauty, creativity. 

They were everything Rio knew Agatha to be capable of and more.

"It's beautiful," Agatha had breathed, her fingertips tracing over the little carvings.

"Open it," Rio urged her, shifting Dani around in her arms a bit.

Agatha listened, gently cracking the locket open. On the left side, there was a photo of Nicky that had been taken minutes after his birth. On the right, there was one in the same vein of Dani. Seeing them side by side was actually insane, almost. They looked so similar in their fresh newness, clearly siblings. Maybe that would change as they both grew -- because gods be damned, Rio knew Nicky was out there growing -- but in those photos that were stowed safely in that locket, they looked just the same.

Those hours later, they put Dani to bed and shuffled to their own room, arms wrapped around waists throughout their trek down the hall. When they split off to venture toward their respective sides of the bed, Rio was a little surprised to watch as Agatha pulled the locket from her pocket and clutched it tightly as she crawled between the sheets.

The moment they landed on their backs next to one another, Rio's head turned to take in the scape of Agatha's profile as she held the locket up to behold it.

"Do you like it?" came Rio's low and quiet question.

Agatha's cheek dropped to the pillow and those vibrant but emotional eyes landed directly into Rio's. 

"I love it, truly," Agatha breathed back at her, scooting over enough that she could steal a soft kiss. "I love you."

"And I love you, Agatha. We'll get past next week and have an entire new year in front of us to make the most of."

Rio meant that with every fiber of her being, and Agatha knew it, too.

 

May 8th, 2008

Agatha.

The years that had rolled on in their lives had, in fact, been bountiful in the experiences and emotions it had brought to the Harkness-Vidal family. They were afforded every single day they had hoped for with their daughter, watching her grow, watching her become the person they hoped for her to be.

Even at four years old, there was absolutely no denying that Dani was Agatha's daughter through and through. She might have favored Rio more in resemblance, but that spitfire attitude and constant need to argue? That was embedded into fifty percent of her DNA, the half that belonged to Agatha.

Dani's expression were Agatha's favorite. She was so positively animated that it was quite hard to understand how a child developed that kind of control over their face, but she never questioned it. That slightly tanned skin was a perfect offset to her beautiful blue eyes. Agatha knew that most babies had blue eyes when they were born and as such, they had expected Dani's to change, but they never had.

No. Dani might have looked so much like Rio in her features and stature, but those blue eyes came straight from Agatha, no questions asked.

On a warm spring afternoon, Agatha was relaxed in a lounger on the back patio, the sun high and bright in the sky as it warmed the occupants of the yard. Not only was that inclusive of Agatha, but Rio and Dani as well. 

The two of them were hunched over, preening off dead leaves from the fruits and vegetables that were beginning to grow. They were clearly having a conversation judging by the grin Rio was wearing as Dani's head bobbed emphatically with whatever she was saying, but Agatha could not hear what they were talking about.

The loudest thing she heard was Rio as she cried out into the air.

"No! It's mine! You better give it back!" She was clearly amused and was still donning that grin, but Dani immediately took off, cradling the smallest strawberry in her palms, one that had not meant to be picked so soon.

Her giggles were wild and bright, but Rio gave her about a four foot head start before taking off after her, chasing her lazily around the yard. Rio's legs were about as tall as Dani was in her entirety, and she could have easily closed the space between them, but she was clearly having the time of her life chasing Dani around trying to get a strawberry that was no good to begin with.

It was silly, but their laughter rang exuberantly in the air of the May afternoon and it made Agatha realize just how lucky she was.

Was the following day another Mother's Day where she wished they could be four instead of three? Of course. That was something she wished for on any momentous day. She wished for it every New Year's Day on Nicky's birthday. She wished for it on Easter when she would pull out the photo of his tiny head sporting the smallest bunny ears. She wished for it on Dani's birthday. She ached for it on Mother's Day and even Father's Day, too. She longed to have him with them in their family costumes on Halloween and in their matching pajamas on Christmas. Never would a single day or occasion pass where Agatha did not wish her son was there to share it with them.

Right then, though, as Agatha watched her wife and their daughter scampered around the yard in the silliest game of chase, she knew she was blessed to have what she did, even if it wasn't all that she yearned for.

Maybe some day, she'd find the ability to stop imaging scenarios that included Nicky, too.

That day was not going to be the one.

 

June 19th, 2020

Rio.

Walking in the side door with a hand full of grocery bags that evening, Rio had not been expecting to arrive in the midst of a warzone. Surprisingly, she hadn't heard the shouting from out in the garage, but it was at full volume by the time she made it into the house.

"Danica Inez, I swear to God, if you step outside that front door with those keys in your hand, I will absolutely ground you into oblivion and you will not see the light of day until you graduate!"

Oh, shit. Agatha was pissed.

"I have my license now! Why would you buy me a car if I can't drive it?!" Dani shrieked back.

As Rio paced further into the house, she could spot them from the kitchen. Agatha was closer to her in her place on one side of the living room and Dani was dangerously close to the front door on the opposite side. Rio couldn't see Agatha's face, but she could see Dani's and it was bright red in a direct contrast to how blue her eyes were in their emotion.

"Just because you have a car does absolutely not mean that you can just come and go as you please. I understand the need for independence, but you at least owe us an explanation of where you're going," Agatha  reminded her, though it was clear she was forcing her energy into the act of not shouting those words across the room.

"If you're that worried, just get that tracking app or whatever," Dani snapped back, and what Rio knew that Dani did not was that she had just unwittingly given Agatha everything she wanted.

The thing was, Rio and Agatha had already discussed that very idea. They had decided to give it time, to let Dani have a bit more freedom as she grew. They had been a little... well, clingy for the majority of her life up to that point for obvious reason, but it was apparent that they couldn't continue to suffocate her the older she got.

For her first ten years of life, there had not been a single day where she had been out of one of their sights. In the house, yes, but never anywhere else. She was not allowed to go to sleepovers, though her friends had always been welcomed with open arms in their home instead. She was not allowed to go on day trip outings with her friends' families unless one of the two of them could tag along as well. Even until she got into middle school, they had chosen to homeschool her.

That had been a prime choice and in many ways, it had helped Dani develop more skills and talents that could only enrich her life moving forward. They had given her the basement as a studio and as such, it was where she could continue to teach herself the many instruments she had sunk her time into -- including violin, cello, guitar and drums -- and on the other side, they'd curated a little lounge area that she could spend time in when her friends would come over.

Isolation, while ideal, had never really been an option. They still found ways to help her socialize and groups for ger to join that would be stimulating and encourage growth and development on a personal level. So while school had not been an explored area of Dani's life, they still wanted her to be a kid and to live life as one.

By eleven, they had allowed her into public school. With the addition of sports, Dani was absolutely thriving and continued to do so in such a vast social setting.

Even when they had resigned to letting her go out during day time hours without them when she turned fourteen, it had been mandated that an adult they met, conversed with, and trusted would be there as well. By fifteen, they had finally budged on letting her stay the night somewhere else, but only because she had a phone and could shoot them a singular emoji to tell them that something was wrong.

The truth was, Dani was an incredible kid. Not only did she have her hobbies and her sports, but when she had time, she indulged in extra curriculars like quiz bowl. It had quickly helped her to develop a strong rapport with different cliques. She had friends in sports, ones in chess club and quiz bowl, and she had the ones that loved music in the way she did.

Excelling in academics had been another of her many feats, something Agatha had told her time and time again that she could relate to. Agatha had graduated high school shortly after her seventeenth birthday and had already taken electives that attributed toward her college courses. When they had gotten the call that Dani was being skipped up a grade -- completely bypassing her sophomore year -- they had celebrated by taking her out to the restaurant of her choice and letting her have whatever it was she wanted.

They were always proud of her accomplishments, but Rio could tell Agatha took that one to heart a little more.

Now that Dani had approached the crisp age of sixteen, she had developed this sense of entitlement that pissed Agatha off to no end. It irritated Rio, sure, but it made Agatha so so mad. Rio was fully aware of the reasoning: Dani acted as stubborn and iron willed over the things she wanted and believed in just as much as Agatha did. They were cut from the same cloth and as such, they butted heads to no avail.

Right then as she tried to square off with her mother, Dani had just handed Agatha every bit of ammunition she would need in the war waged on worrying about her every second of every day that she was not with them.

"Fine," Agatha stated simply. She shifted her weight to her left foot and crossed her arms over her middle. Rio couldn't see it, but the knew the expression Agatha was wearing right then was smug as fuck.

Dani's eyes widened and her jaw hinged. She was always so beautiful with her plump cheeks and lush lips that so clearly came from Rio, but right then she looked the spitting image of her in her state of being truly aghast at what had just happened, and that it had been by her own suggestion.

"That's not what I meant!" she tried to backtrack, but it was too late. Agatha got the permission and hadn't even needed to ask for it.

"Nope. You suggested it, and mom and I have talked about it already but wanted to try and give you some breathing room, so you can have it your way." Rio was just watching Agatha's back, trying her best to imagine what her face looked right then, so rooted in her justified righteousness. "If you wanna come and go, we're always going to know where you are. Period."

"Momma, that's a l --"

"I think she's right," Rio voiced from her place in the kitchen as she stowed boxes of cereal in the cabinet. "You want freedom, and we get that, but it comes with conditions and you know why."

Of course Dani knew why. They all shared in a cupcake to wish Nicky a good year and a happy birthday every single New Year's since Dani was four. She knew that was the reason.

"But --"

Rio had already started to close the gap between where she had been in the kitchen and where Agatha was poised and steeled in her sense of resolve.

"No buts, Danica," Rio cut in softly with a shake of her head. "You can have space, but we will always worry. You're a teenager and for the next year until you graduate and maybe get accepted in Julliard like you hope, you're going to abide by the rules we have. We try to be fair, but there are still hard no's for right now. You running around the city unmonitored is one of them."

"And for this little..." Agatha waved her hand dramatically in a circling gesture to indicate what had just transpired, "tantrum, you're definitely not leaving tonight. We'll discuss if that lasts any longer. But this whole 'I think I'm a big girl now because I have a license' thing you've got going on isn't cutting it. So knock it off."

Dani had grown, yes, and she was fit and limber, but she was still a kid. She was still their kid and until she was an adult -- or until she submitted to a very adult undertaking like college -- they simply couldn't loosen their hold on her too much for fear that if she slipped away, they might never get her back.

"Basement and your room are your options for the night. I think you need some time to consider the way you've been acting lately. We've been letting it slide because you're otherwise composed, but not anymore." Agatha's voice was stern, but Rio could still hear the affection and the need to protect that was woven through her tone.

"Momma, that's not --" she tried to argue, but Rio interjected to stop her.

"Danica," she cut, though she wasn't sharp. "Tonight, it's best to let it be. We can talk again in the morning and maybe find a different solution, but just... let it go. Go downstairs, play your video games or your instruments and work it out. We'll check in later."

Although Rio was being gentle in the tone of her voice, there was a clear instruction in those words, one that Dani knew best to heed. 

"Okay," she grumbled, head hanging as she dropped her keys on the designated hook and trudged her way to the basement stairs before disappearing down them.

"Well," Rio started, stepping directly next to Agatha, a palm landing flat on her back. "That was quite an event to come home to with boxes of cereal and cartons of ice cream."

"Yeah," Agatha agreed with a discouraged sigh. She hadn't turned her head, eyes still fixed on some distant mark across the room. Rio's hand shifted, a light back and forth of support and love.

"She's just... being a sixteen-year-old, unfortunately. We've done our best to respect her for the young adult she is, but she's got a little ways to go in understanding that such respect needs to go both ways," came Rio's musings. She leaned in closer, her lips brushing Agatha's cheek. "We're working on it, all of us. All the time."

"You're right. I know you're right," Agatha finally resigned, her shoulders slumping slightly as her face finally swung around to land before Rio's, their eyes locking.

"Even if she's a miniature version of you, hellfire anger included, she's still a pretty great kid and we did get lucky considering half of her classmates are being suspended for fucking in the bathroom," Rio reminded her with a dry chuckle.

They were thankful that while relationships and the like were on the backburner in regard to Dani's priorities, even if they weren't, they'd long since had the talk that boys were of no interest to her.

Rio had been the one to take the lead there, making her request that if it changed and her attractions shifted elsewhere, they needed to be notified and another talk entirely could be had.

"Can you stop that?" Agatha grumbled, her face scrunching.

"Stop what?" Rio asked back, swiping another quick kiss.

"Being right all the time."

 

April 12th, 2021

Danica.

Every day for the last two weeks, around the same time of day, Dani found herself pacing a rut in the floor of the foyer. She was waiting for that stupid little flap on the door to rattle and for the day's mail to spill onto the floor.

In the throes of her back and forth, her cheeks had grown pink and she'd even tied her hair up to keep from getting any warmer than she needed to be. That was almost impossible right then; she'd been waiting for the letter from Julliard that would tell her what her life was going to be like. She had also applied to NYU, but she absolutely had her heart set on Julliard. 

When she had made the suggestion that she wanted to apply to Berklee, she could tell that while it was still on the same side of the country, the idea of being any further away than New York was not something her parents were going to allow without a fight. Yes, she was attending college a year early, but by all technicalities, she was still not an adult yet and she could understand their caution.

Truthfully, her parents were the living, breathing definition of 'helicopter moms.' She could comprehend what they had been through in their lives that had made them that way, but the older she got, it began to feel a lot like being smothered.

Danica loved her moms with everything she had, and she was grateful for all they had given her. She knew that sometimes, she could be a handful. She was aware that she could make poor choices and do the wrong thing every now and again, but they had never once buckled in their mission to love her. Even when they were angry or upset, they never walked away without expressing that they loved her, even if they didn't know how to handle whatever issue they had encountered.

What that letter meant, if it was an acceptance over a denial, was that she got to have a sliver of independence. She would get to venture into the city every day. Maybe her parents would let her explore so long as she was with someone. Sure, she wouldn't get to live on campus until after she turned eighteen, but even getting to go at all would open her up to an entirely new world. She would meet new people, learn new things. It was the first door to pass through that led her toward the rest of her life, but not the last one by any measure.

Maybe she had just turned seventeen, and there was still an endless list of lessons that life was sure to teach her, but anyone who had ever met Danica Harkness-Vidal would have announced her to be quite the entity. She was pragmatic and funny, but her beauty could have been a weapon. Instead, she used it as a soft and comforting expression that safety could be found in friendship with her.

She'd dated, more in the last year than the previous ones, but she'd been too nervous to bring any of the girls home. It wasn't that she expected Rio or Agatha to be a complete terror, but something about the idea of waving a giant flag in front of their faces that reminded them just how much she had grown up didn't seem like the best course of action, at least not yet.

The thought that they would dismiss her could never be the reasoning; they had raised her to love the way they did. They had raised her to protect her big heart and share it with only those that were worthy. It was simply that it was a forward trajectory in her life that would cause them to realize that by natural progression, she was stepping a little further from them and a little closer to the life she wanted to be living.

Dani had been deep in thought as she continued her back and forth, her brow furrowed in her effort. She had delved so far into her own mind that the sound of another voice caused her to skip a step in a startled jump.

"Still nothing?" Rio asked although she already knew the answer. She came off of the last step, a empty glass in her hand as she made her way to the kitchen to drop it in the sink.

"Mail must be running late," Dani grumbled, her lips twisting nervously, but she had not stopped pacing.

"You know momma's going to make you refinish the hardwood if you don't stop it," came Rio's soft teasing in return. She rinsed the glass out and paced toward the foyer, stilling Dani by wrapping her up in her strong arms. "You gotta stop worrying, Dani girl."

Dani's arms raised and secured snugly around her mom, squeezing her tight as she laid her head atop Rio's shoulder.

"I'm not worried... I just... I want to know," Dani tried to explain, but she knew that it fell short.

"I know, baby. But... It'll be here soon. And we will know for certain one way or another. If the answer is yes, then that's fantastic. If the answer is no, then we wait for the letter from NYU and we can make a plan then." Rio was always so even, so calm in times when Dani felt like she could shake right out of her skin. She'd always had this way about her, this authoritative gentleness that helped guide Dani through any struggle she faced.

Agatha had taught Dani to never take 'no' for an answer.

Rio had taught her that when there was no other answer than 'no,' it was okay to find other avenues to keep progressing.

Almost on cue, the outside flap of the mail slot clanged. Then, the inside one pressed open and about six envelopes spilled through, dropping with the curse of gravity to the floor before the time Dani could untangle herself from Rio and bolt over. She scooped them up and began to feverishly flip through them.

By the time she had moved to tuck the third envelope behind the others, her shockingly blue eyes widened and she dropped the envelope between her fingers to pick up the one she had been waiting for. Rio approached to take the other mail from her, but she dropped it too so that she could immediately rip into the envelope from Julliard.

"Agatha!" Rio shouted over her shoulder, loud enough for Agatha to hear her from her place upstairs. "It's here!"

The sound of heavy footfalls rang overhead as Agatha moved reasonably fast for her age, booking it down the hall and then down the stairs, her hair blowing wildly as she all but ran to where they were in the foyer.

"It's here?! What does it say!?" she questioned a bit breathlessly, skidding to a halt behind Dani, to her left.

The letter was in Dani's hands, still folded into three sections. She took in a deep breath and moved to lift the top portion up, though all she saw was her name and the Julliard letterhead in the opposite corner. She then tucked down the lower portion, her nervous gaze dropping to the text.

"Ms. Danica Harkness-Vidal, it is with great PLEASURE WE INFORM YOU THAT YOU HAVE BEEN ACCEPTED INTO JULLIARD'S BACHELORS OF MUSIC PROGRAM FOR THE CLASS OF 2025!" she was shouting, but her voice was undeniably trembling the longer she went on. She tried to keep it together, but the tears had begun to spill even before she felt the embraces of both her parents as they sandwiched her between them tightly.

They were kissing her cheeks, her temples, her hair at the same time and she was torn between wanting laugh at them or completely sob because she had managed to get into Julliard at the age of seventeen. She knew there had been younger students, but for her, it still felt like an accomplishment.

"Danica," her mom voiced into her hair, placing a couple more kisses there.

On the other side, Agatha had buried her face in Dani's shoulder and her voice sounded immediately after Rio's.

"We are so proud of you."

Dani reached up to the best of her abilities, wiping at her wet cheeks. 

"Thanks, guys. I'm... pretty proud of myself, too."

 

Two weeks ago, March 2025.

Agatha.

Ding!

Agatha was not typically the most popular person after hours, but if there was a text coming in at ten at night, she had an inkling who it would be coming from. When she swiped her phone off of her nightstand and leaned back into the pillows, she couldn't fight the smile at the photo of Dani that popped up alongside the contact name 'Boog.'

There had been about three months when she was thirteen when she had really detested the nickname she'd had since she was a toddler, but she'd found a way to get over it. She knew that it was because she menacingly would pick her nose and chase them around screaming 'BOOG BOOG!' even if there was nothing on her finger.

She was currently in her last year of her Bachelors of Music at Julliard, but she had already been accepted into the Masters program, furthering her education another two years. She had declined a few orchestral offers to do so, but she had been determined to get that elevated degree and Agatha had never been shy about telling her just how proud of her they were.

Dani had moved to the city during her second year in college and while it had been hard to let her go, they knew they would lose that fight with her having turned eighteen. She legally was an adult and no matter how much they wanted to cling to her to be the ones to ensure her safety, they'd found that they needed to trust the lessons they had taught her, the skills she had learned. 

When she had been in her first year, Rio would drive into the city every day to meet Dani at an MMA gym. They both took the lessons and while for Dani, it had been about protection, Agatha certainly hadn't minded the muscle building that had occurred in Rio's form. It had been a way for the two of them to bond and as Rio had disclosed in whispers through the stillness of early morning hours, it made her feel really good to be able to help Dani learn to protect herself.

Right then, Dani needed protecting from herself. 

Not actually, but the little bit of the message Agatha could see before she unlocked her phone read 'Quick, I'm at Pioneer and need the recipe for...'

Agatha chuckled as the text window popped up in its entirety.

Boog: Quick! I'm at Pioneer and need the
recipe for your Creme Brulée. It's an
emergency.

Me: It's ten at night, why are you at
the grocery store?

Boog: I told you, it's an emergency!

Me: Oooo, are you trying to woo
a new lady friend? Do you even
own a blow torch?

Boog: ...yes, actually, I do, momma.

Me: You're a musician. I should
have expected nothing less.

Boog: I'm 21 momma. If the worst 
thing I'm doing as a senior in
college is smoking weed and
making Creme Brulée at 11pm,
I'd say I'm doing okay.

Agatha had to laugh at that one. 

It was fair, and Dani had a point: If the worst thing she was doing was getting high and cooking in her own kitchen in the middle of the night, perhaps they'd done a rather decent job in handling her upbringing.

Me: What do you already have?

Boog: Heavy cream and sugar.

Me: Okay, so vanilla bean, salt, and 
4 eggs should be all you need.

The entire time she had been typing out the recipe, she had watched as the bubble that indicated Dani was typing appeared and disappeared about six times. Agatha knew damn well she was going to give her a hard time about the length of the message, but she would then remember what she had asked for in the first place.

Her attention span could be a little limited in that manner.

Boog: ...you are insane and I love
you with everything I am. And also...
probably right. Guess I will just
have to hang out with her tomorrow
too.

Me: Atta girl. Get your stuff and go

Me: She has gone for one of her night

Me: Oh, and have fun with your friend!

Boog: I'm muting this convo til morning.

Me: You almost done, beautiful?

She locked the phone and set it on her lap so that she could grab the remote to turn the volume on the television up a bit. As she was setting it back down, her phone dinged in her lap again.

Wife: Yeah I am a block away and 
should make it in Jesus f****** christ

That one chaotic text message was almost as funny as the entire exchange she had shared with Dani.

A little bit later and after she had received a text from Dani that she had made it home, Rio had returned home and showered and crawled into bed smelling of Palo Santo and peonies, something that made Agatha snuggle into her immediately. 

Agatha had propped her phone up on Rio's stomach as she scrolled through the interaction with Dani to show her. Rio had lightly dug a thumb into Agatha's ribs when they got to the bit about Rio burning the pasta sauce, playfully acting like she was biting Agatha's head as she did so.

"You are both absolute terrors," Rio had breathed with a laugh, her arm tightening in its grip around Agatha.

"You would have it no other way, my love."

 

Nikolai Malikov.

The only thing Nik Malikov already wanted to do when he got off later on in the day was get home, shower, order something in and enjoy a quiet evening in with his girlfriend, Gabriela. Work hadn't been hard as of late, but on that day of all days, he hadn't wanted to go in. It was his birthday. His twenty-fifth birthday, to be exact. He had woken up to a 'Happy Birthday' text from his mother and an empty bed that had left him confused.

After a few slow early morning breaths, he could smell coffee. And... Bacon? It was six in the morning.

He pulled himself out of bed and slipped into a pair of boxers, shuffling down the hallway to the bathroom to begin his morning routine.

Flipping on the light, he found himself staring at his reflection, those eyes so dark green they were almost brown studious as they scoped out his own face, looking for any flaw or blemish that might have appeared since the day before. 

His dark brown and slightly wavy hair was a tousled mess atop his head, but nothing a comb couldn't fix. His jawline was as strong as ever, chiseled and angled perfectly. Gabi had been trying to convince him for weeks to let her pluck his unruly eyebrows, but he had yet to cave to that request. So far.

After brushing his teeth and combing his hair, he made his way back to their bedroom to change into his scrubs, suited in his armor for another day in the oh-so-glamorous life of a physical therapist. Nik loved his job, but he had been feeling a bit stagnant as of late. He had been trying to pull himself out of it and he and Gabi had spent too many hours in early mornings looking at ridiculous career paths he could change to. It never went anywhere but it was fun to imagine. 

Once he finished dressing himself, Nik headed for the kitchen, finding Gabi at the stove as she fried up a couple of eggs. There was a toasted bagel sitting in the popped toaster and an untoasted one sitting on the counter next to it. 

"Good morning, gorgeous," he greeted warmly as he slid up behind her so that he could crane his head over her shoulder to press a kiss to her cheek. She jumped slightly as his hands found her hips, but hummed softly at the feeling of his lips just beneath her eye.

"Happy birthday, handsome," she responded. She reached forward and shut off the burner before she turned around in his grasp, hands landing easily on his chest as she peered up at him, that bright grin on her face.

Gabriela Mendoza was, without a doubt, the most beautiful person that Nik had ever laid eyes on in his entire life. It wasn't just the thin and pointed slope of her nose, or the perfectly sculpted cheekbones. It wasn't only that dazzling smile, her silky black hair, or the way those dark eyes shimmered when she was truly pleased or thrilled with something. Gabi was beautiful because her heart was pure, she spent time volunteering for different causes, and she loved Nik with everything she had.
