She'd loved him like that since they met his freshman year at NYU.

He dropped his head, gracing his lips softly against hers in a show of appreciation.

"Thank you. And I see you have been hard at work on birthday breakfast. Bacon, egg, and cheese bagels?" he questioned with a soft chuckle, glancing over her shoulder to inspect her work. 

"Your favorite. Of course. But I know you have to get going, so I poured you a mug of coffee already and I'll build and wrap this for you so you can be off."

That was why Nik loved his girlfriend and why he had been heavily considering the possibility of proposing, but he knew he needed to put a little more thought into it before he made any big plans.

They had been together since they were eighteen and Gabi had been the first person that Nik had ever felt truly comfortable enough with to even consider talking about his mother.

Alisa Malikov was... a sort-of good person. She always looked disheveled with her blonde hair and bright green eyes, constantly seeming like she needed to be looking over her shoulder. It had been a lot worse when he had been younger; she had moved them almost like clockwork once a year. He'd lived in a few southern states, the Midwest, even as far as C'ouer D'Alene. Sometimes, he wondered if she would have moved them out of the country if she could.

Being steady and planted was not something he had ever known, just as he had never known what it was like to have two parents like so many of the kids he grew up with. What was more was that for almost fifteen years, his mother had deflected almost every single he had hurled at her in relation to who the other half of him actually was.

She had never been bad to him, but it wasn't like she had been striving to win any Mom-of-the-Year awards. She took care of him, she did love him, but Nik had felt quite often like maybe there were more important things on her mind the majority of the time. 

When he had informed her that he was applying for NYU his senior year of high school in Chicago, she had been furious. She had told him that he couldn't leave, that he couldn't go that far. She had been even more upset when he had applied anyway and got in on a full baseball scholarship. 

Perhaps something in him should have found it strange that once he had informed her that he was leaving, with no chance for her to sway him, she had found a house in Upstate New York to replant her roots for the 900th time in his life. He had wanted to argue, beg her to give him a bit of breathing room, but he knew it would have collapsed their relationship in that house-of-cards stability it had been maintaining since he had announced his departure.

Nevertheless, his life had gone on, he had met someone he was convinced was the love of his life, and he had a career he was thriving in, even if he was growing a bit bored in the process.

Nik released Gabi's hips and gave her another peck before he slid over to the toaster and changed out the bagels, setting his on the wax paper so that he could side it over to her. 

After she had assembled and wrapped his sandwich, he had left her with one more kiss before he departed for the day, leaving her to her homebound day filled with ad building for her own job. She worked in advertising for a world-renowned technolgical supplier and she, too, loved what she did. As far as Nik was aware, though, Gabi stayed enthralled with her work load.

His day at work had been abnormally long; he had an inkling that it was solely because it was his birthday. The other employees at the rehabilitation facility he had worked for had gotten him a cake, one that had a picture of Old Gregg screened to the top of it, something that he'd gotten a good chuckle over.

They had even supplied him with lunch from his favorite deli a few blocks over, both of which he had taken photos of to send to Gabi who had gushed that he had the sweetest coworkers. She hadn't been wrong. When he informed her the cake was almond, she had asserted immediately that any leftovers should get to come home with him -- almond cake was her favorite.

So, he had left the facility a few minutes early and made his way back to their apartment. When he walked in, there were candles lit around the main and dining areas even though there was still an hour or so left of daylight. On the dining room table sat a bag from his favorite Indian restaurant and in front of it was a small wrapped box. 

Slipping out from under the nylon strap of his messenger bag, Nik hung it on the door and lifted his head to scan the apartment again.

"Babe?" he called, moving further into the apartment.

"In the bedroom!" she called back, causing a small smile to tug on the corners of his lips.

When he discovered her where she said she would be, she was an absolute vision. Her tanned, warm skin was visible on her arms, shoulders and chest with the velvet black dress she had pulled onto her form. Around her neck was a thin silver chain that sported the diamond necklace he had gotten her a couple of Christmases ago.

"Babe, you look..." Nik managed, though his mouth felt dry as he surveyed the wonder she was. "You got this dressed up to eat Tikka Masala and Butter Chicken in our dining room?"

Her expression softened and she closed the rest of the space between them, bringing her hands up to cradle either side of his face.

"Of course I did, handsome. It's your birthday. And just because you didn't want to be out and about doesn't mean we can't still celebrate appropriately." Her low tones were so convincing, so able to talk him out of the idea that it would be silly to put on a button-down and pair of slacks to sit in his own apartment.

So, he had chosen to do just that without giving it further thought.

After they had enjoyed their meals and drained their wine glasses, Gabi had pushed the little wrapped present across the table to him.

"Go on," she urged, those dark eyes flickering down to it before lifting back toward his face. "Open it."

He eyed her for just a moment but the smile he wore in the next second said that he knew he needn't be skeptical of her.

His fingers were precise as they worked the paper free, tearing it only when he had to. Once finished, he flipped the box over in his palms so that he could properly survey it.

On it, in very clean letters that were fashioned into the very familiar logo read:

Ancestry.com

His eyes widened and then lifted to his grinning, gorgeous girlfriend as she sat across the table from him looking thrilled with the thought she had put into such a gift. When she realized he was looking at her and not the box anymore, she knew she should probably offer some kind of explanation.

"I just thought... I guess I just thought that if your mom is never going to give you answers, you have a right to get them for yourself. And... in the seven years I've known you, she's evaded the topic damn near every time. So... let us get them for you instead." The explanation was stout, pointed and very, very clear. Gabi loved him enough that if she could help him know more about who he was, she was going to without skipping a beat.

Nik scooted his chair back from the table a bit, leaving the box on the table as he cocked his head to beckon her over. She was still grinning as she got to her feet and padded over to him, placing herself in his lap as her arms draped around his neck and she beamed down at him.

"No matter what that test says you are," she began softly, clearly needing to inform him of something very important as she leaned in to press their foreheads together, "I will love you always. There will only ever be one Nikolai Malikov. And he's mine."

That giggle that escaped her right as she gave him a soft kiss sent his heart soaring cleanly into outer space. Their lips parted and he found himself grinning, the gentlest whisper leaving his lips.

"Always yours."

 

Chapter 3: A Little Destiny to Tell You What You Know

Present Day, Early April, 2025

Danica.

Walking out of March and into April, Dani felt like she was stepping off the safety of solid ground and onto a rocket that was going to shoot through the next couple of months with ferocity. There was an endless list of things that would need attending or celebrating, including both her birthday and her graduation.

Maybe two days after her birthday, she could use the excuse of the 'holiday' to convince her parents to smoke weed with her. It was a long shot, but they would likely crave a distraction and what better one could there be than getting high, eating excessive amounts of popcorn and potato chips, and watching over-the-top comedies?

In the grand scheme of things, she knew this year was likely going to be harder for her moms than the previous ones. She knew that because it had been twenty five very long years since they had last seen Nicky; a quarter of their lives. So much had gone on and the way time had passed had brought them so much in life, but they'd never forgotten about him. Not any of them, even Dani. She might not have ever gotten the chance to meet him, but she still remembered the idea of what he could have been.

She still had the idea of what he was to her.

Other kids had imaginary friends. Dani had her imaginary Nicky. 

He trounced through creek waters with her, digging up hidden treasures and crawdads. He built a dirt and plywood ramp with her when she was twelve. When she broke her arm launching her bike off it, she insisted she'd done it alone. She even drew him in chalk on the brick wall in the backyard, throwing a softball at his poorly drawn gloved hand.

Dani had never met Nicky, but he had always been there, real or not.

That night, a Friday at the beginning of April, the Harkness-Vidals were set to attend an award ceremony at the hospital Agatha had been working at for the last twenty-seven years. There were a variety of categories and recognitions to be handed out to a plethora of medical professionals, but the one Agatha was set to receive was a career recognition award. It was to honor the countless hours she had poured into her work and into that hospital, to boast about her passion and her unyielding ferocity. It was the biggest 'thank you' they knew they could offer. 

A gala meant that Dani got to take the train to Newark and turn up on the doorstep of their family home with a bag over her shoulder after her classes ended in the early afternoon. It meant that when she opened the door, she was immediately hit with the smell of sugar cookies that were in the oven.

A grin filled her face, pushing up those still somehow cherubic cheeks as she dropped her bag, shed her shoes and all but sprinted to the kitchen where she found Rio, trading one sheet pan of baked cookies for a pan of raw ones.

"Mom!" she chirped, waiting until the moment the oven door was shut to bound up behind Rio, her arms wrapping firmly around her middle.

"Well hello, my daughter!" came Rio's delighted greeting, broken by her laughter.

"I missed you," Dani informed her, cheek still pressed to Rio's shoulder as she hugged her from behind. She gave Rio another hearty squeeze before she continued. "And don't give me 'It's only been two weeks' because I don't wanna hear it."

A pleased chuckle passed through Rio's lips as she gave Dani's arm a soft pat.

"I missed you too, boog. You ready to get dressed up all fancy and drink pricey champagne?" Rio questioned. She already knew Dani wasn't drinking; she'd agreed to drive so the two of them could celebrate accordingly, but Dani felt it wasn't worth it to remind her. Instead, Rio gave Dani's arms a light squeeze to request that she loosen her hold and she obliged easily, letting her mom go so that she could turn around to face her. The moment she did, RIo's warm palms found her cheeks with ease and she smushed them together.

"Ack, mom! Stop it!" Dani squealed, reaching up for Rio's wrists while she simultaneously ducked her head away from the touch. "You're gonna get cookie gunk in my hair an I already showered today," she tried to scold, but the grin that was on her lips extended to sparkle in her eyes as she regarded her mother. 

Yes, it had been two weeks since she had been home for a visit, but it felt like so much longer than that. Each time Dani saw her parents, she could see as the days were beginning to wear on them. 

Time was the very reason for their convening that evening. The award Agatha was receiving was a way to honor the time she had spent in the hospital's walls, but it was likely also the last of its kind in the span of Agatha's career. 

Agatha was nearing retirement and while Dani was of the opinion that she would have to find some kind of job to busy herself and not go insane, she also realized that after the life she had lived to that point, Agatha deserved a bit of a break to just spend weeks or months at home with her wife and make occasional trips into the city to go shopping or grab a bite with her not-so-little girl.

"But yes, I actually brought my royal blue dress, the one with the corset bodice and the leg slit. Classy and not slutty enough to shame the family," Dani offered, her mischievous grin wide and bright at the slight widening of Rio's eyes. Before she could speak or give protest, Dani was posing an inquiry to change the subject. "What are you both wearing?" 

Rio's eyes narrowed slightly, as if to call Dani out for being downright rotten without having to say a word, but then relaxed as she considered her daughter's question.

"I, myself, am wearing my black dress with the studded sleeves. As of this morning before she left for work, momma hasn't made a decision on whether or not she's wearing a suit or a dress. She has selected one of each but can't choose between the two." Rio took a step back and leaned against the counter, regarding Dani as those blue eyes flickered with the sparks of an idea.

"So what if I pick for her?" she suggested with a grin. "If someone doesn't make a decision, she's going to come home and spent an hour going over fifty reasons why each one would be right for this specific occasion. I can guess almost all of them, so I'll just choose for her." The way Dani said it, it was like it was the most obvious option available. It was as if nothing else could have ever worked.

She could tell by the look on her mom's face that she might have been onto something. 

Rio jaw shifted and her tongue pressed to the inside of her cheek as a smirk bloomed on her lips. "I think that's actually a great idea. And would mean the world to her, honestly."

"Go on then, she'll be home in about a half an hour depending on traffic," Rio urged her with a light shooing gesture. 

To Dani, it felt close to impossible to wipe that grin off of her face, even as she leaned in to place a kiss to Rio's cheek before she skipped up the stairs and down the hall to her parents' bedroom. 

Unsurprisingly, it was tidy and well kept; the bed was made as though it were some high-class hotel room, only missing the chocolates on the pillows. Atop the duvet, two very different outfits were laid out in Agatha's indecision, shoes included on the floor at the foot of the bed. 

The dress on the left was black, likely to match Rio's. It had a tilted neckline that looped around the outside of the shoulder. It was a sleek piece, one that Dani had seen her wear plenty of times before to schmoozy and uppity events.

Next to it was a black suit that had larger-than-normal pinstripes that were almost white, but had the softest tinge of pink. It was classic, in Dani's personal opinion, and she knew Agatha would look phenomenal in it. 

Truthfully, Dani got the dilemma. She understood why Agatha couldn't choose.

Thankfully, Dani was not Agatha.

She picked the dress up and walked back into the closet, sliding it onto a hanger to place it back where it belonged. Once finished, she tossed the shoes in as well and wound her way back down the stairs to join Rio in the kitchen.

Pulling the door to the refrigerator open for something to drink, Dani grimaced. "La Croix? God, you guys are really showing your age. Drinking that stuff is like sipping on television static while someone shouts the name of a fruit from another room."

Rio's laughter from in front of the oven happened in the next breath and was bright and amused, nearly folding her.

"Where the fuck do you come up with this stuff?" Rio asked her, lifting her head to take in that insanely imaginative young woman she had raised. 

"I think," Dani replied as she tucked a bottle of water under her arm before reaching back inside for something else, "that it might be," she continued, pulling her hand back with something clearly clutched in it. She bumped the door shut with her shoulder and used her empty hand to snatch a cheese cube from the other one, tossing it in her mouth. "The unmedicated ADHD. Maybe. Probably."

Rio knew she was right. They had tried the medication dance, but Dani hated it. It had helped in some regard when it came to studying and trying to actually take in information, but she had been very vocal about the part where it had stunted her creative process. She had the relief when she needed it, but by choice, she preferred to let the chaos reign and ride the waves as they rolled in. 

"Didn't your parents ever teach you it's rude to talk with your mouth full?" Rio asked her, glancing into the oven again to check on the last batch of cookies.

"They might have, but I enjoy being a wild heathen instead," Dani replied sarcastically with a grin before tossing another cheese cube into her mouth.

"Oh, right. Your mother did say you've been smoking the electric lettuce," Rio teased, knowing it would draw a reaction out of Dani, and it did in the form of her howled laughter.

"You said it like that on purpose!" Dani gasped between bursts of her humored wailing. "You do not fucking think of weed like that! You're not ancient!"

Her entire jovial demeanor and the way the joke tickled her just so was something that clearly pleased Rio; there had once been a time where she had considered the idea that she would never know the joys of a visit from an adult child, but right then, she couldn't have been more thankful that it was an ever-present facet of her life.

"You're right, but this was totally worth saying it like I'm ninety," Rio assured her. She straightened and backed up, lowering the oven door so that she could remove the pan of cookies before placing it on the cooling rack and returning to the oven to shut it off. "And it goes without saying, but leave the cookies for after the awards?"

Dani's grin was toothy and ornery, the lights of mischief dancing in those beautiful blue eyes that looked so much like her mother's.

"Did you count them? Because if you did, whatever the total was, it's actually less. I can tell just by looking at them," the younger woman informed Rio with a self-assured tip of her head. Dani's humor had always been a beautiful thing and she was fully aware that both of her parents were happy with the fact that it was not something she had grown out of.

Rio rolled her eyes, her delight with Dani's antics still clear on her face. "I counted them. Twice. It's a treat to celebrate. When we come home drunk, we can make ice cream sandwiches with them," she explained as she began to clean up the few odds and ends that had been left out from her little cookie foray. "So I mean it, Danica, there has to be an even number."

Rotten as she was, Dani's smirk was Cheshire in appearance. "So what I'm hearing is: eat two cookies."

Rio took the couple of steps needed to close the space between them and lifted a hand, palming Dani's face. "What you are now hearing is: Go get ready for the gala, your momma should be home any minute."

"Bbt thn shldnt ah waitta shay 'ello?" Dani blubbered, stifled by Rio's hand against her face. Rio's fingers shifted and split so Dani's eye was visible, scowling as she spoke again.

"I'm kind of mad that I understood exactly what that meant," Rio informed her, detaching her grip from her daughter's face. 

"Am I not correct?" Dani challenged in jest, the giggles working their way up her throat.

"You are, you're just really annoying ab --" Rio had started, but the sound of the front door opening cut her off as Agatha came striding in, still clad in those navy blue scrubs with her hair pinned tight at the base of her skull.

"Momma?!" Dani called excitedly from the kitchen as she hurried around the island to greet Agatha.

"Is that my little gremlin?!" Agatha snickered as she slid off her shoes, meeting Dani in the dining room with a tight and warm hug, one that seemed to communicate just how much Agatha had missed her in her absence. 

Maybe Dani's teenage years had been a little bumpy in regard to how clingy and concerned her parents had always been, but now that she had grown and learned various ways to protect herself, they had gotten the chance to witness the kind of woman she could become on her own. Her romantic life was one flaming hot disaster after another, but she had yet to call it quits. Plus, the sex was mostly good, but that was not something that needed to be common knowledge.

"How did your Creme Brulée turn out?" Agatha questioned as she placed a kiss to the side of Dani's head and pulled back to gauge her expression for an answer.

"It was..." Dani started, though the smirk that was fighting its way onto her lips was difficult to ignore. "Pretty good." The smirk won out and Agatha's natural response was to roll those eyes that were almost a mirror image of her daughter's.

Dani stepped aside as Agatha released her so that Rio could step up as the next in line for a greeting from her wife after a day apart.

Rio went through these periods where she would pick up odd jobs for short periods of time to keep herself busy once Dani had left the house, but overall, she seemed to enjoy the role of keeping the fort held down. She cooked and cleaned, sunk time into crafts and hobbies she enjoyed like gardening and kayaking when the weather was right. Being able to work when she wanted was a nice facet to the dynamic of their marriage, one Dani actually found admiration in.

Her parents were powerhouses in their own rights, but as the couple they had become, she looked at them and saw a relationship that would likely never crack under time or pressure. What they had was the epitome of true love and Dani would have insisted so until she was blue in the face.

"Hi, my love," Rio greeted as she stepped into Agatha's waiting arm, planting a gentle kiss of hello to her lips. "Happy awards day."

"They made me work for it, today," Agatha murmured before she took another kiss. Despite breaking their lips apart, she did not let Rio go. He deduction came gently, her delight apparent by the light curl of her lips. "Smells like you've been up to trouble." Her eyes lifted to Dani, smile widening. "Were you a co-conspirator?"

Dani's hands flew up, palms out to prove her innocence. "Hey! I just got here. I was actually trying to convince her she can't count and that she's saying there are two more cookies there than there actually are."

That softened but knowing look as it crossed Agatha's face warmed something in Dani's chest. It was that silent acknowledgement that she knew one of the cookies would have been for her and that Dani bore more of Agatha's cunning and humor than most people saw. When she was home, when she was comfortable, it truly came out and she could tell both of her parents enjoyed seeing it.

"Well," Rio stated, hands raising to rub lovingly at Agatha's biceps as she stole one last kiss. "I am going to put the cookies away. You should both go get ready and I will be up to join."

Dani tauntingly snapped her ankles together and whipped a flattened hand to her eyebrow. "Sir, yes sir!" she barked, though the last word hitched right before she began to laugh.

"You're so annoying," Rio sighed, feigning exasperation.

"She gets that from you!" Agatha informed her quickly, ducking in to place a kiss to Rio's cheek before untangling herself to follow Dani up the stairs. "Do hurry, my love!" Agatha called behind her.

From higher up, Dani's own shout echoed down the hall and stairs. 

"We're on a time crunch! No banging in the shower!"

 

Nikolai.

"Just text them and tell them we're running a little late!" Nik called toward the bedroom as his girlfriend tore through it in a search for her wallet. The hunt had started about twenty minutes prior and thus far had been entirely unsuccessful. Every five minutes that passed without Gabi locating it, her frustration seemed to grow. "I'm almost finished shaving. Give me two more minutes and I will help you."

"I just don't understand where it could have gone!" Gabi griped, clearly aggravated. "I don't even remember taking it out of my bag!"

Nik considered for a moment, making one final swipe of the razor along his jaw. As he dropped it to rinse it in the sink, his brow pinched in consideration. "Do you think you might have left it in the center console in the car?" he asked. Fingers grasped tightly onto a hand towel as he pulled it from the rack and paced into their bedroom, drying his jaw and neck. 

"I mean..." she started as her feet planted to search her recollection for any instance where that might be a possibility. "I can always check. Are the keys --"

Before Gabi could complete her question, there was a sharp rapping on the front door, heavy and commanding in its call for attention. Nik watched her expression tighten as she glanced over his shoulder in the direction of the front door. 

"You get dressed, I'll get it." She looked a vision as she headed toward him in that white blouse and high-waisted navy trousers, kissing him on the cheek as she passed. They were just meeting friends for dinner, but Gabi never missed an opportunity to knock the breath right out of him with how stunning she could be, even dressed so simply and cleanly.

He had heeded her request, disappearing into the closet to find a button-down and slacks of his own. From where he was tucked inside the walk-in, he could not hear who their guest might have been. In fact, he hadn't heard a thing until Gabi blew back into the room.

"Hey, um, the police are here," she informed him with no other courtesy to break the tension. His confused frown pinched tight, lips turning down heavily at the corners. What the hell were the police doing there? Before he could ask as much, she took it upon herself to inform him. "They won't tell me why they're here. They said it has to be you."

He finished buttoning up his shirt, still not understanding what was happening.  "I haven't done anything," he tried to reason. "I've gone to work and come home and gone out with you. That's it."

"Hey," she tried to soothe, reaching to place a firm hand on his shoulder despite the fact that he was more than a couple inches taller than her. "They did say you aren't in trouble, but that there's something they need to discuss with you."

Nik's lips worried against one another and an uncertain huff of a sigh left his nostrils in a gesture that did nothing to soothe the sudden anxiety was sparking its way through his nervous system. What could this possibly be about? Why were the cops turning up at his door on a random Friday when he knew for a fact that he had done nothing wrong?

His eyes dropped, watching as Gabi held out an encouraging hand, one he would always take without a second thought. He followed her into the living room, taking in the sight of the two detectives standing by the door. One of them was considerably older, dark eyebrows that did not match the white beard on his jawline or the decent amount of white hair atop his head. His skin had started to sag in places, like this was a job that had been wearing on him for some time.

The detective next to him was younger by at least a decade, bright and eager blue eyes that were in direct opposition to the mildly somber expression on his chiseled face. 

"Good evening, gentlemen," Nik offered, stepping further into the living room but still cautious enough to keep space between them. "How may I help you?"

The older detective stepped forward, close enough that Nik could see the badge that he had to offer. 

DET. GREGORY STRAUSS.

There was something peculiar about his actual credentials, though.

CITY OF NEWARK POLICE DEPARTMENT.

"This is my partner Detective Kingston. We just have a few questions."

Why were police from New Jersey in the city, in his apartment?

"Perhaps you might like to sit," the detective suggested, gesturing to the couch behind them. 

"No, we're alright," Nik assured him. "What's this about?" As he surveyed them further, he realized that the younger detective was clutching a folder with something of relevance obviously inside. His gaze snapped back to Detective Strauss.  

The older man's expression softened, as if he were trying to be convincing. He seemed to know that whatever can of worms he was about to open would likely call for a sitting position, but Nik could not begin to fathom what could possibly be so serious.

"Before we go any further, may I ask you to confirm that you submitted a DNA sample to the testing site Ancestry.com a little less than two weeks ago?" the gentleman asked.

Both Nik and Gabi glanced at one another, a mirrored confusion happening in the same knitting of their brows before they turned their attention to the detectives.

"I did. Is there... Did I do something wrong?" he asked. He could feel Gabi shift at his side, her arm lacing through his so she could fasten her hand into his, squeezing it tightly.

"You didn't, no," Detective Strauss assured him. He glanced over at the couch again, seeming a little more insistent that Nik sit. This time, that slight shift in the man's expression sent a painful chill racing up Nik's spine. 

He swallowed down the lump in his throat and tugged Gabi toward the bigger sofa, waving a hand toward the smaller loveseat as he tucked his chin over his shoulder toward the detectives before he spun to sit.

"Please, sit," he indicated. Immediately, he was on the edge of the couch, Gabi's hand still clutched tightly in his larger one.

"The reason we are here is because we received an alert from Ancestry that your sample raised a flag in the system," Detective Strauss began. Before either of them could supplement that they had no idea what it could be about, he held his hand out for the folder Detective Kingston had been holding onto. "It matched to a sample that was collected twenty five years ago, back in Newark, in relation to a missing persons case."

Nik was listening, or at least he was trying to. His DNA had.. flagged? What did that even mean? When the detective had continued, Nik balked, his jaw dropping open.

"Missing persons?" he parroted back stupidly, gripping tightly at Gabi's hand in his stupor.

"Yes, we..." Detective Strauss began, glancing toward his person. "We would like for you to join us at the station in Newark for an official sample."

"Newark? I've never been to Newark in my entire life and I am clearly not missing," he argued back, not capable of deducing what was going on without them providing him with more information.

Detective Strauss opened the folder and picked up something that looked like a very old news clipping. He stared at it for a long few moments before his gaze lifted to land right in Nik's, his mouth in a tight line before he began to speak. The moment the words fell from his lips, he looked like he wanted to be saying anything else, if at all humanly possible.

"We have reason to believe that in April of 2000, you were taken from your home and away from your parents when you were four months old. Your birth name, if that truly was your DNA sample, is Nicholas Harkness-Vidal." There was something about the expression the detective was wearing that was shouting his need to say more, to keep going, but he stopped himself. Soundlessly, he lowered the news clipping to the coffee table and pushed it toward Nik.

Nik didn't move, not at first. His eyes dropped, barely scanning the paper before they landed on the men again, probing, daring them to admit this was nothing more than a prank someone had paid them to pull on him.

"You're trying to tell me that my mother... Isn't my mother?" he asked, the incredulity and disbelief in his words heavy and thick.

His mother was a lot of things, but she wasn't a fucking criminal. She didn't just run around stealing children. It had always just been the two of them, no matter how unsettled they had always been. 

Detective Strauss just glanced at the clipping on the table. 

Finally, Nik picked it up with the hand that wasn't clutching at Gabi's. The headline was bold and unmissable.

NANNY KIDNAPS INFANT: HARKNESS-VIDAL FAMILY SEEKING ANSWERS.

His gaze dropped, scanning over the few paragraphs of information. The women, Agatha and Rio Harkness-Vidal, had arrived home to their son and nanny missing. The article itself was dated a week and a half into the search but in that time there had been no leads. They had even posted a reward of five thousand dollars for any credible information in relation to the kidnapping.

He read over it again, and one more time for good measure.

"But..." he voiced, tone strangled in the swell of emotions that were threatening to overwhelm him. "This says it happened in April and that the baby was four months old. I... I was born a week before April. I couldn't have been four months old. I... I've seen my birth certificate," he argued back, doing all he could to poke holes in such a ridiculous story.

"There are explanations for things like that, but I don't feel as though we should be offering them until we know for certain that this is all true. Which..." The man's stubbled lips twisted for a moment before the gentle pleading that followed. "Which is why we would greatly appreciate it if you would join us in Newark. Once we confirm the DNA, we will be able to answer more of your questions and act accordingly."

Nik was just staring, eyes flicking from one detective to the other, as if waiting for one of them to admit that this was all a mistake, that they had gotten the samples confused. This could not be happening to him of all people. Maybe it had been annoying to have to move cities every year and maybe there were certain things his mother had done through the years that had felt abnormal or off, but he had simply written them off as quirks. Alisa was harmless, if not just a bit strange.

There they sat, doing their damnedest to convince him that she was a kidnapper. More than that, they were trying to hell him that she wasn't even his mother. That couldn't be true. He... kind of looked like her, didn't he? Maybe his hair wasn't the same color, and even though his eyes held a semblance of green in the right light, they were far darker than hers. His cheekbones were far sharper and his jaw was more angled, but it was why he'd had questions about the other portion of his paternity, questions she would never answer.

Could this really be why?

"Nik, baby," Gabi urged beside him, gripping tighter at his hand in an attempt to bring him back into the moment. 

Very slowly, his head turned and he was able to tear his eyes away from the detectives. Somehow, he was hoping he might be able to find an answer in her beautiful brown eyes. All he saw there were pools of nerves that she was trying to bury beneath encouragement.

"I think we should go," she told him in a quiet murmur, those dark eyes searching his expression for a response before it actually hit.

"But... Gabs, this is insane. This... It... It can't be true," he returned lowly, waving the newspaper clipping that was still in his grasp around in the air. "I mean... It's sad they lost their kid... But that's not me. It can't be me." The panic was sleeping into his tone more and more as he tried to rationalize the information that had been given to him, his eyes glassing over the longer he talked.

Soothingly, Gabi's palm landed on his cheek, her thumb brushing below his eye in nothing more than pure comfort.

"I know, Nik. But if we go, they swab your cheek, we wait around, and then we know for sure one way or another. After that... Well, after that you and I will figure out where we go depending on what we find out. Either way, we do it together." Her voice was still quiet in a way that left the two other men mumbling between themselves to try and offer a moment of privacy when they could not realistically leave the room.

Nik heard her, though. He knew that she was right. They had to know. It wasn't like the cops would have shown up on just a hunch, but the theory they were floating to him was going to completely crumble his entire life if it was true. His agreement only came because deep within himself, he was certain they were wrong. His mother might have been many things, and she might have been capable of some unhinged behavior when it came to protecting him, but this? Kidnapping and keeping him away from any biological family he might have had for his entire life? It just seemed insane.

Finally, his attention turned back to the policemen. 

"Okay, we'll go."

 

Rio.

A couple of times a year, events like this rolled around where Rio felt truly proud of the woman she had fallen in love with over thirty years ago. She loved that the three of them were given an excuse to put on extravagant outfits and do their makeup. She loved that they got to venture out into the world as a unit, boastful over Agatha's accomplishments.

Watching the way Dani regarded Agatha in her suit with her hair tamed but still slightly unkempt as it flowed down her back stole Rio's breath away before she could even consider an actual reaction. 

That look in Dani's eyes as she watched her mother slide on a few decorative rings was everything; Dani looked at Agatha like she was the only person in the world who had ever been capable of placing the moon and the stars in the night sky. Dani looked at Agatha like she could very well be the sun, herself, if she got any brighter.

They had been nothing but a cacophony of giggles as they emerged from the house and loaded into the Escalade that frequently hauled them around, as well as any company they might have kept at other times. Dani plugged in the address Agatha had given her into the GPS and departed, headed right toward what was sure to be an evening they would never forget.

Oh, how impossibly true that had been and how impossible for any one of them in that car to have had any idea.

Rio felt light, almost like she could have floated away as the three of them walked into the banquet hall of the hotel where the ceremony was being held. They looked like a million dollars, a pure showing up absolute class as Agatha, the incredible neurosurgeon she was, marched in with her wife and daughter, sandwiched between them in a chain of clasped hands.

It was not their first event of that nature, but Rio was all too aware that it was likely one of their last. Agatha knew it, too, but she had been dismissive of actually acknowledging it as fact. She was happy to reach the end of her career and spend the rest of her time relaxing on a beach somewhere warm with her wife, but she had also spent nearly three decades learning and growing and serving and teaching in that hospital. 

That hospital had been a second home to Agatha over the years and ultimately, it was going to be hard to walk out those doors and know she was not going to be walking back into them. She had not officially set a date, but knowing that it was on the horizon clearly had her feeling certain things that she was not ready to discuss. Right then, sitting at that table as they shared in the meal provided and drank their champagne, she was happy.

Rio was proud. This was an accomplishment, something that an entire room for of people were going to understand. Agatha's dedication knew no limits; she had lost sleep, hours with her family, days of her life to the walls of those operating rooms but she had saved more lives than she had been able to count. There had been losses a long the way, but that number was far, far lower than that of her successes. 

With the dinner plates collected, the evening rolled on into the awards portion. There were a couple of different presenters that cycled through the different categories with Agatha's being the very last. There had been a couple of instances where Rio had caught, out of the corner of her eye, as Agatha's phone lit up on the table below her, just out of Agatha's eyeline. 

After the fourth time, Rio casually reached over and flipped the phone, leaving the screen pressed to the top of the table right as the current presenter called Agatha's name. The room erupted into applause as Agatha got to her feet, not hesitating to kiss her wife and squeeze her daughter's shoulder before making her way to the stage to accept the honor and say a few words.

Rio had tried to pay attention, but something else was drawing it away. She could hear the faint buzzing of Agatha's phone from its place on the table as it rang. It stopped for all of twenty seconds and started vibrating again, ringing over and over.

Who the fuck was calling Agatha so insistently?

Not only was it after nine in the evening but it was clear that she was indisposed and not able to answer. Rio's phone was stowed in her clutch and as such, she didn't consider the idea of checking it, too. 

Instead, she tuned in for the last bit of Agatha's speech before she sealed it with her gratitude and departed the stage to Rio and Dani who were whooping and hollering in their endless pride. 

With hers being the last award given, the ceremony was set to wrap the moment she sat back down and had started the process when Rio leaned in, first to kiss her cheek and then to whisper in her ear. 

"Someone is desperately trying to get in touch with you. I haven't checked to see who it is," Rio informed her. She leaned back into her own seat, lifting a hand to grab her champagne flute so she could drain it of its contents. At the same time, Agatha was quick to grab her phone up, checking her calls and messages.

"Hey," she voiced suddenly, her empty hand flying out to land on Rio's forearm.

Rio and Dani both pinned Agatha with confused glances, having noted the panic that was constricting her tone. 

"We should go," she said, not even having looked up from her phone. She was still clutching at Rio's arm and for the first time, Rio realized that not only was Agatha's hand trembling in her grasp, but her throat was quaking with emotion.

Rio's gaze shifted, landing on their daughter. For the briefest moment, a silent conversation was had where they both decided it was best to get outside, away from prying ears and eyes, and talk out there. 

"Okay," Rio agreed easily, though it was so quiet that surely only Agatha could hear. 

After collecting their things, the three of them spilled into the night air, Agatha's attention still nearly locked in on that phone screen. 

"Who's been trying to call you, Agatha?" Rio questioned, an arm sliding around the small of Agatha's back as they began the trek toward the parking lot. 

"Detective Strauss..." she answered, punching in the command for her voicemail. "I haven't heard from him in a few years..."

After putting it on speaker, the phone rang once before the automated system kicked on and voiced that it was going to play the message. The man's voice was familiar in some ways, but Rio had hoped she might never have to hear it again. 

"Dr. Harkness-Vidal, this is Detective Strauss. If you could please get in touch with me at your earliest convenience, that would be greatly appreciated. Feel free to call this number back at any time."

The automatron kicked on again, but Agatha disconnected the call so that she could locate the phone number in her call log to immediately call it back, though they had not stopped walking in the direction of the car. Dani was silent, Rio was silent, both understanding what that message could possibly mean.

Sure, he had been vague. But... There was something there. Something more.

On speaker again, the phone rang three times, then the line clicked before the man's familiar voice picked up.

"Dr. Harkness-Vidal, thank you so much for calling me back. I did not mean to disrupt anything," he apologized sincerely. The had reached the edge of the parking lot by the time he continued on. "If you're available, I know it's late, but... Do you think that you and your wife might be able to come into the station?"

They were twenty feet from the car, but Agatha halted in place, staring down at the phone in her hand. 

"Gregory," Agatha clipped coldly. "You tell me right now that you've found him."

Maybe it shouldn't have made sense, but as Rio took in the sight of her wife, still as a statue as she stared at that phone -- silence on the other end of the line for a little too long -- Rio knew it, too. 

Dani stepped up to Rio's side, grabbing her hand tightly as they both stared at Agatha who was still zeroed in on the source of that phone call.

"We found him," Detective Strauss affirmed.

It was a good thing that for Rio, she didn't actually understand what it was he was agreeing to. Agatha did, though, and before she would let herself revel in the fact, she needed another answer first.

"Tell me the next part. Is he..." she hesitated. This time, Rio knew the reason she wasn't looking up at the two of them was because she was going to find them with nervous tears streaking their cheeks. That would be a sight she couldn't handle if the man offered an unsatisfactory answer.

Then, Detective Strauss said the words Rio and Agatha had been waiting twenty-five years to hear.

"He's alive."

 

Chapter 4: Burn The Candle At Both Ends

Nikolai.

"It shouldn't be taking this long," Nik grunted as he paced the length of the steel table that was located in the center of the room they were currently occupying. 

Gabi had been the one to drive them to Newark and for that, Nik had been infinitely thankful. The truth was, his hands had not stopped shaking since the moment he had touched that newspaper clipping. Even more, he was pretty sure that he nothing in his body had stopped shaking since that moment. 

For every bit of resolve and sense that had been seeping out of him, Gabriela seemed to be absorbing it, taking it in, holding it until he was ready to take it on once more. She was fortified in her mission to see it all out and get it handled, which Nik surely would have appreciated with a deeper sense of gratitude if his head had not been spinning as he watched the lights of the city grow fewer and fewer until the transition was made and they found themselves in New Jersey.

All he could do was think.

This couldn't be real. Even if the two of them truly were about to step into a police station in a state he had never been to for him to have his cheek swabbed and his DNA tested, there was no way that it could possibly come back as a match to some missing persons case that had gone cold decades ago. There was no act of the universe that would let Detective Strauss or some other office of the law walk into that room and tell him that his mother was not his mother and his whole life was a life.

At least, that was what he was trying to convince himself. 

It was the only thing he could do to keep himself sane, to keep his head on straight when all he wanted to do was simply disappear. 

With his prolonged silence throughout the entire drive, Gabi had not be willing to let him venture inside without saying her own peace, even if he was not ready to hear it, which he was not. In fact, all he wanted to do was cry and plead and beg that she just pull away and they never think about it so long as they continued to live.

"Baby," she voice soothingly, removing her hand from the steering wheel to reach for Nik's, squeezing it lightly in a silent beguiling for him to look at her. It took him several long moments, but he finally picked up his chin and turned his attention to her, though the expression that found him was woeful and forlorn. 

"I know this is... insane, and that you're probably thinking and feeling a lot, but we're going to take this one step at a time. We get out, we go in, we let them take their swab, we wait." Gabi shifted in her seat, able to turn more toward him with the way she folded her leg in front of her. The hand that wasn't clutching at his raised and cupped his cheek, her thumb brushing lovingly beneath his eye. "Whatever answer they bring back to us, we take it home with us and we play it by ear from there."

Nik could hear it, how sure she sounded. It was like Gabi knew that what she was saying was fact and really, at the root of it, it was. Nothing that she said said to him was wrong or even incorrect. All of those things would happen, yes, but he was not certain that he could guarantee how it was going to feel to work through the process.

"Gabi, I..." he attempted, but it fell flat as sand flooded his mouth, drying it out beyond the point of being able to articulate clearly. His lips pressed together and he fought to compose himself, to find the words he so desperately needed to say. "This is a television plot," he finally said. It wasn't a revelation of his feelings or a direct path forward in their conversation, but he was somehow hoping that it would attest to his disbelief.

"I know, it's hard to fathom. And for right now, we can stay suspended in the disbelief until we have concrete proof," she soothed, not having stopped the motions of caressing his cheek. "The only way we get that proof is to go inside and let them do what they need to."

He knew she was right. He knew that there was no way out of this; taking off and heading back home wasn't an option. Nik had to face this whether he wanted to or not, and he certainly did not want to.

He considered, only once on the drive, texting his mother. She was in the city, she would meet him and could explain, but he remembered the detective's request that he not alert her until they were absolutely certain of the circumstances. The man had stressed how important it was that she remain in the dark without solid proof that she was who they suspected her to be.

"I... I don't know..." he squeaked, his eyes darting over her face. "I don't know what I'll do if --"

"Shhh," she coaxed softly, her thumb dropping to press softly over his lips. "We don't know until we know. So... let's go know, yeah?"

As he gazed into those deep, dark eyes, something in Nik felt safe for a fleeting moment. In that car, all was right with the world. The very moment they stepped foot outside of it, everything changed.

They had done as she had said they would, following the map she had laid out almost to a T. That left them in that cold, empty room as Nik paced back and forth, his chest growing tighter and tighter by the minute. He understood it took time, that they had to go through certain processes and run the tests, but it was taking far too long for him to be comfortable with.

"You should sit, Nikolai, you're working yourself up," Gabi told him softly from her seat at the table. He knew she was trying to be helpful, that she was trying to keep him calm, but it was having the exact opposite effect, especially when she used his full name.

"I just don't understand what could be taking them so long. I get that they have to test it and everything, but we've been here for almost three hours," he shot back, though about midway, he realized that his tone had developed an unnecessary sharpness that she did not deserve. He took a breath and stilled his feet, allowing his eyes to slide shut for a moment as he attempted to center himself. Another breath slowed his heart just barely, granting him the clarity to finally sit down.

"I know," Gabi returned, her hand finding his back as she turned ninety degrees in her seat to face him. "And I know the longer it takes, the more anxious you get. At this point, nothing I say it going to change that and that's okay. But... You have to keep breathing and keep focusing on this, on me, on us. We're right here, together," she reminded him, her low voice still sweet in its delivery.

His dark hazel gaze lifted to her, his lips parking to speak. Before he could manage a sound, the door to the room they were waiting in opened and Detective Strauss strode in, though the expression on his face was unreadable. When the door clicked shut behind him, his gaze lifted to the couple and the sole offering he could provide was a tight smile. 

The legs of the chair scraping against the floor as he pulled it away from the table made something in Nik's stomach churn, heavy and violent. It was just a sound, an innocuous sound that should have had no context or connotation and yet, Nik felt as though he was going to vomit.

"Thank you for your patience," the detective began, placing his folder on the table. He wasn't looking at either of them as he opened it and turned it around so that they could clearly see the contents. He pointed to the graph on the top, his eyes finally lifting to Nikolai. "The top here is the sample that was coded and logged in 2000 from the kidnapping case. Below," he continued, his finger sliding down the page to indicate a second graph, one that looked identical to the first, "is the sample we collected from you when you arrived. They are..."

Detective Strauss hesitated just long enough that Nik felt everywhere in his body as every vital organ blipped out of existence and ceased to function. His heart wasn't beating. His lungs were not inflating or deflating. His stomach had morphed immediately into a black hole in deep space. His brain? Not a single neuron was firing, not a synapse to be filled. No spark of biological electricity could be found within him for at least thirty seconds.

The one thing that jump-started him back to life was the feeling of Gabi's hand grasping onto his like it was an absolutely lifeline. It wasn't one she needed, but she knew it was one he would need.

"Identical."

Nik blinked at the man, as if to clearly state that he could not believe it. That detective really thought he could just point to some images on a page and convince him without question that he was not Nikolai Malikov, son to Alisa Malikov? He really thought that Nik would be so stupid as to just take his word for it?

"That doesn't mean anything," Nik scoffed, his tone filled with anger, but Gabi squeezed his hand again. She knew he was in shock, she knew he was saying the first thing that was coming to mind, but he didn't need to square up with an officer of the law.

"It does, I'm afraid. And as hard as I know it is to hear, I have to officially inform you that according to an exact genetic match, you are in fact Nicholas Harkness-Vidal and you were taken from your home April 20th of 2000 by the nanny the Harkness-Vidals had hired, Wanda Maximoff." Nik could hear some of the words the man was saying, but only intermittent ones that somehow popped through the bubble of static that was nearly deafening in his ears.

"We believe that you may know her current location, and I..." The detective stopped and shifted in his chair, leaning back as a more empathetic look filled his features. "I know this is a lot. I know it's earth-shattering. But if you know where she is, we need to know."

The man wanted an answer, but nothing under the son was going to see to it that it came from Nik's lips. He was trying, he was doing what he could to speak or make some kind of noise that would indicate he did not know if he could help, but nothing hit the air. There was no squeak, no gasp, no choking breath that left him. 

So Gabi filled the silence instead.

Her grip on his right hand and arm were so tight they would surely leave bruises, but he didn't care. The pain was the only thing managing to keep him from passing out and while he would have appreciated the black-out period, it wouldn't have suited anyone. When she spoke, though, something in him plummeted to the far reaches of the earth's core, burning so hot he thought he might disintegrate.

"She came to visit this week. She's staying at the 1080 in Brooklyn. I don't know the room number."

No! No, Gabi! What the fuck?!

He wanted to shout, he wanted to spin on her and ask her what the hell she thought she was doing, but moving even a solitary muscle felt like an impossibility. How did he stop her when he couldn't even bring himself to speak? All he was doing was sitting at that table, feeling as she dug into his muscles in her own terror, and staring at that detective as if he might actually concede and admit that this was nothing more than a bad joke.

This wasn't a joke, and now, they were going to head into the city to arrest his mother.

His not-mother.

His nanny?

Wanda?

That was what he had said her name was, right? Wanda Maximoff?

No, her name was Alisa Malikov.

And she was his mother.

But she wasn't.

Detective Strauss was speaking again, surely informing them what this was all going to have to look like, but Nik couldn't hear him. All Nik could hear was thunder as it rolled and cracked in his head, drowning out every other sound. All Nik could feel was the tightening in his chest as it grew worse with each passing second. All Nik could taste was his own fear, his own sense of terror at knowing that he knew... absolutely nothing. And that was wreaking havoc on him from head to toe.

He began to tremble, his body rocking through it as his chest started to heave and his breathing became strangled and labored. His eyes were darting, though he felt like he could not see anything other than blackness with white spots of light, blinding as they came and went.

Nik was having a panic attack.

One of Gabi's hands released from his arm and moved to his back, smoothing up and down as she leaned in to be as close as she could, needing him to hear her.

"Baby, I need you to breathe," she whispered. Somehow, he heard it, but it sounded as if she were speaking to him underwater, muffled and warped. "If you breathe with me, I can take you home and we can deal with it there, in private, okay?" 

She sounded so calm despite the fact that she was on the verge of a nervous breakdown herself, but it was what Nik needed. He gave a weak nod, his attempt at letting her know he had heard her and he was going to try to listen. It wasn't the easiest task, but as she drew in a slow and even breath, he tried to match it. Tried was the operative word there.

It took several minutes for her to calm him enough that he didn't look like he was going to fall out of his chair and start convulsing, but he was still in pretty terrible shape.

"I need to take him home," Gabi voiced, forcing herself to look across the table at the detective, a pleading look in her eyes. "Do you think that we can have a day or two and we will get in touch?"

The man considered for a moment, his pitiful gaze falling to Nik.

"A day or two is fine. But... I'm afraid I need to inform the Harkness-Vidals as soon as possible. This is something they... They have been waiting twenty-five years for this day, and in good conscience, I cannot prolong it any further now that we know." The man's voice had tempered quite a bit and it was clear that the entire situation was not settling well with him. The fact that it was happening in his career at all was astounding, but he was seeing first-hand the heartbreaking implications of what one woman's selfish choice had done to several different lives.

"I -- I'm not.... I'm not ready," came Nik's panicked garbling, the fear in his eyes lighting them up for the first time since Detective Strauss had sat down across from them.

"I understand," the man returned calmly. "You're not under any obligation to meet with them immediately, but they deserve to know and as a respect to you, I wanted you to be made aware that I have to tell them."

A weak nod was all Nik could offer in response.

"The two of you should go home, be kind to yourselves and each other. This is a life-changing revelation and the gravity of it is enormous. Don't push yourselves to handle this all at once, just take it piece by piece. Get some rest and we will be in touch soon, alright?" the detective offered. It was obvious by the look on his fact that he got it, to the best of his abilities. He understood that this grown man was being told that everything he had ever known was nothing more than a lie, and that who he actually was was someone who never had the chance to be.

Gabi was the one who took up handling any conversation with the officer, thankfully leaving Nik with an ability to remain silent. It was good simply for the fact that speaking was not a cognitive function he felt himself capable of at that point.

In fact, even as they somehow migrated to the car, Nik was not entirely sure how they'd gotten there, just that they were suddenly moving and Gabi was murmuring to him over and over again that she loved him as she gripped his hand so tightly her knuckles turned white. 

Getting into the house was another feat entirely. In the forty minutes it had taken them to get home, Nik felt as though he had forgotten how to walk. It took every bit of effort Gabi had to support him enough to get him into the apartment and down the hall to their bedroom. The moment she had poured him into bed and crawled in behind him, she could not have known that he was only thinking about one thing, and it was what she had said to him the night of his birthday.

There will only ever be one Nikolai Malikov.

Nikolai Malikov was a figment of someone else's imagination.

So who the fuck was laying in that bed, dissolving to tears while a woman who did not know him held him?

Who the fuck was he?

 

Danica.

The air was already cool, but as the three Harkness-Vidal women stood in the middle of that parking lot, a mere twenty feet from their vehicle, it was as if the temperatures had plummeted to subzero. Every bit of moisture in the air was crystalized around them, rooting them to their spots, heels cemented to the blacktop below.

He'd said those words. That detective on the phone with her momma, he'd said something they had all three convinced themselves they would never hear in their lifetime. 

Nicholas was alive.

Nicky was out there somewhere, and now, the police knew where.

They were frozen, immobilized by a statement that had been deemed nothing more than a too-wild hope, a dream that could never be achieved. He had said those words and not a one of them knew how to react.

Agatha was still burning a hold in the phone in her hand, Rio was gripping Dani's forearm so tightly that Dani knew full well it would bruise, and Dani was simply stuck, stunned to stillness including bated breath that hardly stirred movement in her chest. Someone needed to say something, or do something, but it felt impossible. It felt like moving a mountain with one hand tied backside. 

What could possibly be done?

Dani made the initial sound, clearing her throat as she seemed to find her footing first. 

"Momma," she croaked at the exact same time the detective spoke on the other line.

"Dr. Harkness-Vidal?" he questioned, attempting to nudge her into a response.

"Y-You --" Agatha managed back, though it sounded as if there was a deathlike grip around her throat as the sound emerged. "Al-alive?"

Dani wanted to move. She wanted to pull her mom over, wrap her momma up and get them both to the car so that they could get to the precinct as quick as humanly possible. Dani knew that from where they were, she could have them there in ten minutes or less and with it being later at night, she was willing to hedge her bets on the latter. In those moments, she wasn't sure how to find the capabilities needed to execute such actions.

"Yes ma'am," the detective returned firmly. "I will be more than happy to provide all the details, but it would be best suited for an in-person conversation."

"O-Okay," Agatha forced out, nodding her head although he could not see her doing so. "Okay, Detective, we... We will be right over. Thank you."

She was stringing together words a little more coherently, but Dani could still see and hear that Agatha was verging on completely collapsing. She had to get both of them into the car, that was the first step in making progress toward getting the answers she knew both women were desperate to have now that they knew they were there for the taking.

"You and yours be safe, Dr. Harkness," he offered before the line clicked and such a life-changing phone call was over just like that.

The silence was thick as wool, chilled and weighted but still charged with the spark of possibility.

"We need to go."

Dani's voice was so soft, but there was an underlying urgency there that could not be missed. She let go of Rio's hand to press forward, wrapping an arm around Agatha's shoulders as she ushered her to the car, Rio right beside them. At Dani's behest, they both occupied the back so that they could indulge in the physical comfort they could provide to one another on the way to the police department. 

Truthfully, Dani knew she was the only one of sound enough mind to be behind the wheel of a car. Yes, this might have been a massive revelation, but she was technically an external party, someone who was looking in from the outside, even if the window was open enough that she could gauge the scent and the warmth of what was inside.

Dani had been on the other side of an anguish that she had not existed for and now, she could see as the door was slowly swinging open, offering her a chance to understand.

She ignored it, but a couple of minutes in, Dani swore she heard her parents crying in the back seat. She braved a quick glance in the mirror to see them folded into one another, clinging tight. Her heart squeezed at the sight, a pang of realization striking her in the chest.

They had spent twenty-five years not knowing. They could have guessed, and they had been told to give up hope more than once, but now they knew.

Now, everything they had believed for thousands of days on end had turned out to be true.

Their son was alive.

The silence carried with them as they made their way into the station, informed the clerk who they were there to see, and were escorted to a room in the back. They only had to wait a couple of minutes before the door pushed open and a haggard looking older man surged through, his tired eyes falling to her parents on her right. Agatha was next to her, holding her hand under the table, and Rio was on Agatha's other side, clutching that hand, too.

"Good evening, ladies. I am sorry for the late hour of the call, but as you know it was a necessity," he voiced as he took the seat across from them. In a move that was familiar to him that night but new to the three women, he laid out a folder on the steel table and opened it so that he could turn it around to show them.

"This is a DNA test. The top portion is the sample you provided us in 2000. The bottom is one that we collected this evening from a subject that had previously sent in a sample to an ancestry site. As you can see, they are an exact match."

Agatha's grip relinquished its hold on Dani's hand and flew up, covering her mouth as she processed the proof in front of them. On her other side, Rio let out a choked sob, cracking under the weight of what it was they were being shown.

"Fortunately for us, he lives in Brooklyn. We made the trip and convinced him to come in to provide the sample. After the results, he was understandably in shock and we released him to return home with his girlfriend." Three pairs of eyes snapped to him at this information. He had a partner, was living a normal life. Before anyone could raise any questions, the detective spoke again. 

"I understand that this is going to be difficult to work through and understand, but there are a lot of moving parts and pieces. There is no legal obligation that he has to contact you, and if any of you excessively try to reach out, he would still be able to file a no-contact order. It's... Obviously very fragile. I am not able to offer much, but I do want to impart the advice that... As cliche as it may sound, time will heal all wounds. How much of it remains to be seen, but rushing into this might only hurt all parties involved."

It was a lot of information, and Dani knew he was trying to be helpful, but if she could hear her parents' thoughts, she would have known that they only had a few select questions before they dared to bolt in a direction where this could have a happy ending.

"What... What is his name? What does he go by?" Agatha croaked out, lowering her hand from her mouth to land atop Dani's once more.

"The name he has known his entire life is Nikolai Malikov. Wanda moved him nineteen times before he turned eighteen. She --"

"Where the fuck is she?" Agatha cut in, her voice having grown in strength exponentially at the mere mention of Wanda's name. 

The detective paused, pulling back slightly at Agatha's sudden shift in demeanor. He had been building his response, but Rio was the one to speak up that time, her voice timid and quiet.

"Do you have her in custody?"

Detective Strauss gave a light nod. "A couple of my officers apprehended her in a hotel room in Brooklyn a little over an hour ago. She's being held and questioned while we decide how to formally charge her."

"I want to talk to her," Agatha announced, the rage beginning to leak into her tone. In turn, her cheeks began to flush and her grips tightened on the hands she was holding. "I deserve the chance to talk to her."

"You do," the man acknowledged, though his tone betrayed that what he was going to say next was not going to benefit anyone. "But that will have to wait until she's been booked and processed. I will be sure to get you the number to lock-up so that you may check visiting hours for tomorrow."

Dani was quiet as a mouse, just watching, just listening. She did not have the investment that her parents did, but she still comprehended the gravity of what was unfolding around them. She could feel Agatha's anger in her grip and she could hear Rio's in her soft sniffles as she tried to fortify her emotions while they were still in a public setting. And there Dani sat, having no idea what she could possibly try to do to make this better in any minute way.

"So she... She's just been running with him this entire time?" Rio asked, her voice a little harder and void of the sounds of her tears.

Detective Strauss gave a solemn nod. "She had documents forged for the both of them and rarely spent longer than a year in a given place. It appears as though she tried to keep it aligned with school years as to not relocate him mid-year. When he gradtuated high school, he moved to the city for college and has been there since."

At this, all three women blinked at him.

"You're saying..." Agatha started as she continued to assemble the full picture in her mind. "You're saying that he's been an hour away for... years?!" Her incredulity was thick, but it was also sharp. That realization was landing on them like a ten ton anvil that had been dropped from a cargo plane.

Detective Strauss' lips turned down at the corners in a deep frown as he nodded his answer. 

Dani felt sick. If she felt sick, she could not even begin to imagine how they were feeling as they sat there next to her, listening to information that they were almost certainly struggling to make sense of.

The moment Agatha suddenly got to her feet, yanking her hands free from the holds of her loved ones, Dani knew she could say for the first time in her entire life that she had no idea what her mother was about to do.

 

Agatha.

It was hot. It was swelterlingly hot and Agatha could feel acutely where every single drop of sweat had started to bead on her skin. 

Having this conversation was something she and Rio had been convinced they had wanted, no matter how long it took to have it. Experiencing it, and hearing these things that felt like knife after knife and dagger after dagger in her chest? Agatha wanted it to stop. She wanted to stop thinking about it, stop listening to this growing list of facts the detective was providing that were making it feel so much worse than it already had.

The numbness had come a couple of years after Dani had been born. It had been a despondency that had grown from lack of answers or leads. While Agatha hated copping to the idea that Dani had allowed them to 'forget' about Nicky in any way, she would admit that Dani had helped them process their grief. At the same time, she had made living with the uncertainty a little more bearable. 

There she stood, shaking from head to toe in the all-consuming rage that had swallowed her whole at the detective's latest revelation, feeling like she were miles from the woman she had grown to be after twenty years. Right then, all Agatha saw was red. All she felt was fury and pain and unimaginable heartache.

"What I'm gathering," Agatha tried, her palm sealing to her forehead in some silly attempt to quell her temper, "is that she ran him all over this fucking country to hide him from us and then... What? He became an adult and got to make his own fucking decisions?!" It was a miracle, really, that the glass window did not shatter with how shrill her voice became on those last two words.

"My love," Rio beseeched, giving the hip of Agatha's dress a light tug. Without words, Agatha knew what she wanted. Rio wanted her to sit down, to take a breath and to think this through as logically as they could manage given their heightened emotional states. Those wild blue eyes snapped down to her wife, lips pressed in a tight line. They had he loudest conversation without speaking, one where Rio reminded her they had to get through this -- the interaction with the detective -- to start getting through it as a whole.

Agatha released an unhappy sigh of resignation as she sat back down, her jaw clenching as she drew in a slow breath.

"Your emotions in this regard are all very valid, Dr. Harkness-Vidal. I understand the anger, the frustration. I know that you have your questions, and I promise you that we will get you those answers, but we need time." He was being kind, sweet even, but in her agitated state, it wasn't good enough.

"Yeah, that's all everyone fucking needs, isn't it? Everybody needs fucking time," she shot back, eyes dropping to the table as a scowl filled her face. 

"Dr. Harkness-Vidal, I do understand the frustration, truly I do. But I am going to be keeping the lines of communication as open as possible with you. What I know, you will know right after. And here's the number to county so you can call, as well," he reiterated, scribbling down a phone number on the back of his business card before he pushed it over to her.

Her eyes were fixed on him and she remained completely still, unmoving. For a moment, Agatha could have resembled a perched gargoyle waiting to strike. It was a rare moment where she had to be objective. This was not his fault. In fact, he was being exceedingly cordial in how he was handling it, and thus did not deserve her ire. Rio and Dani had done nothing wrong. Hell, even a son that was not ready to see her was not in the wrong.

The only person who had egregiously fucked up here was Wanda.

She had shattered the life of someone she had claimed to be her son. At the same time, she had shattered several others as well. Anyone who had ever gotten a chance to love Nicky -- even the idea of him, in Dani's case -- had suffered at her hand, and she needed to pay for that. 

Agatha would see to it.

"We should head home. We've got a lot to discuss," Rio voiced from her side, reaching over to give Agatha's knee a light squeeze.

Agatha knew she was right, but she wasn't done. She still had more questions, the important ones that they had initially been too stunned to ask.

"Wait," she offered, looking across the table to Strauss again. "You... You saw him? Spoke with him?" 

He nodded, but did not speak.

"Does he... Did he... I mean -- fuck." Agatha stopped herself, drawing in a steadying breath to try and clear some of the jumbled mess from her mind. "Is he healthy? Does he look... Does he look alright?"

This time, the man's face softened and he offered another nod. "He appears in good health, physically. The news is very hard on him, for obvious reasons. I cannot get into it much more than that, but... As shitty as it is, it truly is just going to need time and personal work. But... The young woman that brought him in seems to be a good support for him."

Agatha was listening, but she was also listening. There were the things that he was saying, but she was listening a little deeper. She was hearing the parts where her twenty-five year old son was a functioning member of society and he had someone in his life that cared deeply enough to support him through a very devastating new experience that no one could have ever envisioned. Agatha could hear that for every single night she had lost sleep hoping he was okay, he had been a hop, skip, and a jump away living a rather normal life.

She didn't know if she could find comfort in that or if it made her want to do a swan dive off of a dock into the endless abyss of ocean.

"There's hope here for you all, yet. It's a very complex situation, but I have full faith that there's a way forward where you reunite with your son again. It just might require excessive patience. And if it might make you feel better to hate me for saying it, by all means," he encouraged with a sad curl of his lips.

Agatha did appreciate the offer, even if she was mature enough to know that it wasn't his fault, even if she didn't want to hear it. 

The four of them rose simultaneously and Detective Strauss held his hand out over the table.

"I am aware that this is far from over, but I want to offer any emotion you might deem appropriate toward this scenario. As a parent, you have my support. As a detective, I will do everything in my power to deliver you the answers to every question you have ever had. You have my word." 

Agatha's jaw was tight as she shook his head, giving a curt nod of understanding. When he shifted to shake Rio's, she found words a little easier than Agatha.

"We appreciate what you have done for us, Greg. Truly. And yeah, it's not over, but... None of it's gone unnoticed thus far." Her words were rich and sincere, but Agatha could also hear Rio's pain, her sadness.

They had their answers, now, and yet, as they all shuffled in the front door of their dark house, it almost felt as though they had no answers at all.

"You're staying tonight, right?" Agatha asked Dani, sounding as exhausted as she felt.

"I'll do you one better," Dani answered, sliding up to Rio's side to fit under her arm, hugging herself to her mama. "I wanna sleep in bed with you guys tonight. I think we all need it."

Dani the intuitive.

Dani the intelligent.

Dani the wise.

Their Dani.

Agatha had always missed her son, but in her twenty-one years of existence, Dani had always provided answered to questions that Agatha had never known how to ask. 

It had been an easy agreement from both herself and Rio, the three of them dispersing to change out of their formal wear and into pajamas. Agatha had climbed into bed first as Rio finished washing her face. There needed to be conversations and yet, all Agatha wanted to do was curl up with her loves and simply sleep, perhaps finding herself in a dream world where Nicky wanted to run back to them with no reserves and their family was whole once more without a fight to get there.
