As Rio emerged from the ensuite, Dani came gliding in from the hall, so casually and playfully bumping right into her mom. Rio looked startled at first, but when she caught sight of the smile on their daugher's lips, her own lips sprouted one just the same.

"You're so mean to me," Rio pouted, placing a forceful peck to the back of Dani's head as she ventured to the other side of the bed to climb in. 

After only another moment, Dani had settled into Agatha's side and Rio had sealed her in between them by placing herself on Dani's other side, The moment everyone was comfortable, it was an instant tangle of embraces as their twenty-one year old daughter began to process of trying to hold them together.

There was no telling how long it might take, or how close to breaking they might come, but right then there was one thing that Agatha was absolutely certain of:

Whatever happened, they would take it on together.

Eventually, maybe 'together' would include Nicky, too.

 

Chapter 5: All the Songs That the Night Shouts

Rio.

What was a stronger word than empty?

What could possibly convey how it felt to know that after a quarter of her life spent wondering and hoping and praying to some deity Rio never believed in, their son was alive and less than a couple of hours away? 

There was not a linguistic syntax in any language that could compact that feeling and deliver it in all of its weight. There was not a single sensible way for that type of emotion to be expressed. Any choice she tried to make, it wouldn't have been accurate. It wouldn't have described the way their family had somehow floated back home like ghosts, silent and not disturbing anyone or anything on their way.

While trying to keep her finger on her own pulse, Rio was also trying to gauge the reactions of her loved ones, too. She was trying to figure out a way to soothe Agatha's seething rage, and trying to locate some course of action to make sure that Dani understood they loved her and anything she was feeling about all of this was more than valid, even if they didn't know how to field it until they could sort through the turmoil in their own heads.

This was a mess.

Rio was hardly sure what to feel herself; she was panicking without question, but there was this warped sense of relief that was fighting so desperately to take root in the very base of her brain. 

Nicky was alive.

Alive.

He had lived for twenty five years and now he was residing in a large city where he was just another face. 

Something struck Rio.

Dani lived in the city, too. Dani spent a lot of time in different parts of the city. She hung out with her friends, she went on dates. She ventured to new spots all of the time. Rio knew for a fact that she had spent plenty of time in Brooklyn. 

What if she had somehow occupied the same space as Nicky and had simply never known? 

She never could have. None of them could have. Hell, he could have been sitting next to the three of them when herself and Agatha would meet Dani for brunch somewhere and not a one of them would have had a single clue.

They knew Nicky as a baby and nothing more. Maybe they would have been able to see it. Maybe they would have seen him and been drawn to his striking and sharp features. Or maybe they would have seen it in the color of his eyes. Maybe they would have known if he just smiled at them.

There was no use wondering because even with the news that the search had drawn to a close, the battle was nowhere close to being over. They still did not even know what he looked like. At least, they hadn't when they walked out of the station that night.

In the early hours of the morning, the three of them were bunched up in the bed, all in sitting positions as Dani led the charge on scrolling through the various Google results and social medias that they could locate based on the name the detective had given them.

They had tried to rest, to sleep, but as Rio had curled into one side of Dani with Agatha on the other, their heads touching as they rested on their daughter's chest, she'd known it was never going to happen.

How could they sleep knowing what they knew?

How could they possibly find respite while thinking about what their son, Dani's brother, was doing in his home that they could drive to in less time than it took to watch some films? All they could do was lay and whisper and sniffle and shed tears that had surely soaked Dani's shirt. So, at 3:58, Dani had urged them to move and climbed out of bed to get her laptop. 

At 4:11, they found a page for a therapy clinic with his name, but no photo. He had a DPT and had been at that clinic for two years.

By 4:13, they had found a Google result for an Instagram that they were a little more confident about than the others. 

Dani clicked it.

Three things happened at one time.

A choked sob escaped Agatha.

Dani's hand flew to her mouth to suppress a gasp.

And Rio?

Rio just cried, the hot and emotionally torn tears ripping rivers down her cheeks.

They knew it was him. Just by looking at him, they could tell.

He did have impossibly pointed features, ones that were so very similar to Agatha's. His cheeks were high and sharp, his jaw angled. His nose was more in the vein of Rio's, but where she could really see herself in him was in his eyes. They were the most beautiful color, but also two colors at once. In some photos, they looked a very dark green and in others, they were a light brown. His smile belonged to neither of them, but both instead.

He was handsome. He looked healthy. In the photos with his girlfriend especially, he looked happy. 

Rio had noticed something: in the 45 minutes they spent scrolling through his Instagram, they had not found a single photo of Wanda, or even one of them together. They had only reached the tail end of 2023, but there was no trace of her, not even a mention of her in any caption or comment. 

Clearly she was close, too, and it was how the police had apprehended her, so why was she absent in his presentation of his life to the world? Why did he not want to share his relationship with her to his friends and people interested in who he was? Had she been bad to him? Was their relationship strained? Had she not loved him enough?

Rio could have chased her tail for hours, asking herself questions that she knew she might never have the answers to. 

That was the scariest part.

Even knowing the truth, he could still choose to keep away. He was a grown man who had spent a huge portion of his life buried beneath lies and misconceptions. Wanda had taken off with him and she had never stopped running, but she had still raised him. His entire life was something she had constructed, a world that she had created to deceive him and for what purpose, they still did not know.

Maybe Agatha might get more answers if she was granted permission to go to the jail where Wanda was being held and speak with her. After that long, there was little chance that Wanda would be too forthcoming. They could be hopeful, but Rio was not stupid. This had been calculated and Wanda had spent over two decades running with the ruse, spilling every bean was likely not going to be on her agenda.

The only thing she had done was hurt the man she had raised.

At least, that was what Rio assumed. Truthfully, they had no real way to even assume what it was he was feeling and they wouldn't until he made the decision to reach out. Knowing that they might have to go the rest of their lives without answers was a panic and a pain that Rio had only experienced one other time in her life in her life when he had gone missing so long ago. It was the same anxiety of knowing he was gone and the same pain of knowing they might never see him again.

But they were seeing him. He was right there, grinning and posing and kissing his girlfriend on Dani's laptop screen. Even so, they couldn't hear the laughter from him when his mouth was open and his head tipped back in his joy. They couldn't hear the conversation he was having as he was so focused that he looked just like Agatha. 

They had crumbs, only a couple of pieces to a massive puzzle. They needed more, needed to see more of the picture and that constant longing was going to rip Rio apart. She knew that she needed to find a distraction, but there they sat until almost eight in the morning, just looking through his Instagram, his Facebook, even his fucking LinkedIn.

From what they had found, Rio could see a good man. 

He had a career that was sensible and contributed to the betterment of others. He had a healthy and loving relationship with a woman that looked at him like he was the very reason the sun rose in the sky every day. He had friends, he went out and had fun. He enjoyed true crime documentaries -- per the several photos of title screens he had posted to his Instagram -- and the two of them spent a weekend a month volunteering at their local animal shelter. 

Perhaps it could have been considered stalking, but between the three of them, they had needed something.

Their chatter had been hushed and soft as they absorbed everything they were seeing and learning, and while Dani was clearly working to compartmentalize, Rio's hand had not loosened its grip on Agatha's where they had joined early on behind Dani's back. It was their way of speaking the things they couldn't say in front of their daughter. It was in those little hand squeezes when they saw a photo that had him looking the spitting image of the two of them. It could be found in the way thumbs would brush over knuckles in an attempt to soothe a wordless ache.

They had the ultimate answer now. Everything else was absolutely what they needed, but they knew that this was all entirely out of their hands. They couldn't message him; it would surely cause a uprising of unpleasant emotions. They couldn't track him down and try to force his hand. It wouldn't serve a one of them in any way and would probably crumble the already shattered pieces of the situation further.

By 8:30, Dani had climbed out of bed to shower, saying she needed it more to calm her nerves than anything else. 

The moment she disappeared and they heard the bathroom door shut down the hall, the space that had previously been filled by their little girl was instantly gone as they both scooted toward the other, meeting in the middle. They were a tangle of arms and legs, wrapping up so tightly that Rio was certain Agatha's hold on her could cut off circulation in some parts of her body. Then again, Agatha probably felt the same way about how Rio was locked around her, too.

Rio wasn't sure what struck her and pushed her to speak, but her voice didn't sound like her voice when the words tumbled out. It was a sentiment they had been sick of for twenty five years, but she knew nothing else to say.

"It's going to be okay."

It could have easily been deemed foolish. Anyone in the world could have called Rio an idiot and they would have been right, solely because that was what she had chosen to say, but she had to have the faith. She had to believe that in a month, or even a year, their son would understand that for his entire life, all they had ever truly wanted was the opportunity to love him and would find a way to reach out. 

She could be giving herself false hope, but it didn't feel like there was much else to hold onto. Rio needed something to keep her going when it felt like they'd been so fucking close to him only to have the reality snatch him away, instilling a painful distance between them, but this one was solely rooted in choice.

Even before Agatha drew in the breath she needed to speak, Rio had somehow known she was not going to like what Rio had said.

Agatha.

"Is it?" 

Agatha's clipped return was quiet, but it was sharp and filled with the anxiety and pain such a thought caused her. She knew that Rio was trying to be soothing, that she was trying to find a way to calm every wiry emotion that was straying over what was happening. There was just so much to pick apart and try to process that it felt too overwhelming.

"What has even changed other than just knowing he's alive and Wanda's in custody? He's still lost to us, Rio," Agatha tried to explain in a broken whisper, though she did not feel like she was doing a decent enough job of framing it in words. She sighed softly, burrowing her face into Rio's neck as she tried to search, tried to find the best way to phrase what she needed to say. It took her a couple of moments, but she finally got there. "He has to make the choice to be ours. Yes, we will always know he's ours, but when it comes to how we relate to him... We are strangers until he doesn't want us to be anymore. And that... That could very well never happen."

Agatha hated that she had to say it out loud. She knew they were both thinking it, and maybe even Dani too, but they needed to hear it. Even she needed to hear someone say it, even if it was coming from her own lips. It was the shitty, fucked up, awful truth and they needed to be real with themselves about it. 

The moment Rio began to tremble in Agatha's arms, she knew she'd said the wrong thing, even if it was the necessary thing. 

She got it; Rio was the softer of the two of them. She reverted to a problem-solving mode when any issues came up and now that there was nothing she could do to solve their biggest problem, she was beginning to flounder. She was beginning to lose sight of the blind hope they had been clinging to for so long because now, there was nothing they could do to hurry this along or make it any better.

"I'm sorry," Agatha whispered, squeezing her eyes shut as she pressed her face more firmly to Rio's neck.

Rio did not say it was okay, because it wasn't. All Rio did was cling tighter.

That vice grip they held one another in was enough of a comfort to allow them to doze, falling asleep tangled and safe, although the inner turmoil they were both experiencing was enough to completely sink them. 

They even slept through Dani coming in to check on them after her shower, covering them up with a sympathetic care that neither of them had known her quite so capable of. Dani was an understanding and kind person, but this was hitting her in a different way than it was the two of them and it might be some time before they could pull themselves out of the thick of it to understand that.

When Agatha had stirred several hours later, it was late afternoon and Rio was still sound asleep in her arms. When she gently untangled herself from their embrace, thankful Rio stayed dormant, Agatha's head turned to see a piece of paper laying on her nightstand, folded into a small tent so that it did not get missed. 

With a slowness instilled by grogginess, Agatha reached over and plucked it from its place, flipping it open to read what was scrawled inside in Danica's neat penmanship.

               I ran home to pack a few things. I've already emailed my professors and have asked to sit in on the online lessons instead of being in person due to a family emergency and they're okay with it. I'll film my sessions and practice will go on without me, so don't text me telling me to stay. I should be back by dinner time. I know none of us probably want to eat, but if you want me to bring anything, just let me know.

              I love you guys. See you in a bit.

Nothing Dani said in that note was indicative that she was struggling and yet, Agatha knew it anyway. She knew that Dani was having to sit sideline while Rio and Agatha attempted to wrestle the emotional havoc that was trying to completely shred them to pieces. Agatha was fully aware that there was no way they could mask it, not even to protect the one child they had gotten the chance to raise. 

That had to be remedied. Dani didn't deserve to feel their pain as well as her own.

But where in the fucking world were either of them going to be able to find that kind of perspective? All Agatha could feel right then, reading that note over a couple more times, was that she was letting down her daughter by diving straight into her own anger. If Agatha knew her wife at all, she knew Rio felt a similar way about her own anxiety, and they were less than 24 hours into this fresh version of their nightmare.

Picking up her phone, Agatha could see that it was almost 4pm and that they had accomplished nothing she had been hoping they might. She had wanted to be productive, to find some semblance of a solution. She had wanted to remind her wife and daughter that she loved them, even if she wasn't the best at showing it. She'd wanted to call that number to County and march in there and give Wanda fucking Maximoff a piece of her mind after twenty five years of sheer torture.

And still, it wasn't over.

No one knew when the end was going to come.

No one could look them in the eye and say "This is the day it will all be over."

Maybe it would never be over. That was something that they had to give a spot in the list of possible outcomes they could be facing. It was hard, but Agatha knew that it was realistic.

She was not sure how she would ever find the ability to be truly happy when she knew her son was alive, that he was out there, and wouldn't choose them. It was the most unsettling feeling to not have that answer, to not know anything about him that might help her build a theory. They had nothing to go on, not even a sliver, and as a result, it felt like staring a black hole down without even knowing what to look for.

Agatha's head lulled to the side, Rio's expression serene only due to the fact that she was unconscious and her face was half smashed into the pillow. She was resting, escaping from what a nightmare this had become in the matter of a phone call and an hour long visit to the police station. Their lives had found ways to settle over the years, but everything was upended and destroyed and in many ways, Agatha felt like she was 30 all over again, suffering from the same heartache she'd had then.

Watching her wife sleep, Agatha knew she could not lay in that bed another moment. She wasn't ready to face the outside world yet, but she needed to get up and move around, needed to make herself a cup of coffee or perhaps something a little stronger.

Despite the fact that her limbs felt as though they had ten ton anvils tied to them, she managed to push herself up and to place her feet on the carpet. It was the same carpet in the same house they'd been living in for almost thirty years and yet, it still felt different. In that moment, a new brand of panic swept through Agatha. 

Was everything in her world going to feel different now that they knew the truth? The walls looked the same, but the house had shifted. There was a room that held an office that should have been one their son could sleep in when he had a bad day at college or work. It should have been a place he could find refuge and yet, he had never even known it had once been his.

Agatha passed it when she dragged herself from their room, feet feeling heavy as they moved. She did not push the door open, did not look inside, but she still felt the weight of unexplored potential as it sat in that room. 

Somehow, she found herself in the kitchen, and while there was a pot of coffee brewing, Agatha had a sizeable handle of Evan Williams in front of her, calling to her. It wasn't even 5 yet and drinking alone was pathetic no matter the circumstances, but right then she needed to mute some of the raucous and invasive thoughts that were plaguing her.

She reached down and lifted the bottle, unscrewing the cap with an utter lack of finesse. Slapping it down on the counter, Agatha wrapped her thin fingers around the neck of the bottle and lifted, taking a long pull from it. Somewhere along the second swallow, the deadbolt to the front door jiggled and flipped, the door swinging open a second later as Dani walked through it.

Agatha severed her draw from the bottle, a couple of drops of the liquor rolling down her chin as a result of her startled adjustment.

"Take another one, fuck," Dani voiced when she came into the kitchen to see Agatha wiping at her chin. "Actually, don't," she amended, stepping forward to take the bottle from Agatha's grasp. She wasted no time at all as she brought it to her lips and tipped her head back, swallowing several gulps. The look on her face as she pulled the glass away was almost comical; it was enough to make Agatha breathe the softest chuckle.

"You're a heathen," Agatha voiced, but her volume was low and the edge she had been carrying around with her since they had walked into that police station seemed to have softened.

"We are collectively in Depression, USA, so I think one tug of three shots is more than reasonable," Dani returned, handing the bottle back over to her mother with a soft smile. "Is mom still sleeping?"

Agatha took the bottle and placed the cap back where it belonged, nodding her head gently. "I didn't want to wake her. She needs the rest while she can get it."

"For sure," came Dani's easy agreement as she paced to the refrigerator. She stood with the door open for a moment, face scrunching in her assessment of the contents. "When are you guys going to actually keep stuff to drink that isn't gross?" she asked, leaning enough that she could peer at Agatha around the corner of the door.

"Yes, Danica, you hate La Croix, I know," Agatha offered back, her voice intentionally condescending, though it wasn't pointed and instead came out in jest.

"Okay, but cranberry and grapefruit juice? Not even apple? Or grape? You haven't even hit sixty!"

Agatha laughed. It was an actual, real laugh that was genuine as it escaped her unexpectedly. The look that flashed across her face was brief, but it was shocked. It felt like a foreign act, like she was somehow betraying the main missive here, which was that they were realizing once more that they were helpless to put their worlds back on their axes. 

"Mom drank the last of the orange juice yesterday morning. And she buys the extra pulp anyway because she's a freak," Agatha voiced, though an affectionate smile had found her lips.

Dani bent at the waist, surveying deeper in on the lower shelves, a triumphant 'aha!' sounding as she reached inside, toward the back. A second later, she snapped up, clutching a can of cherry 7up and wearing a bright grin.

"Better than nothing!" she announced, cracking the can open. 

As Agatha surveyed her daughter, her beautiful little girl, a familiar warmth began to find her chest. It was in part due to the alcohol, but it was also the undeniable and endless love she felt for the brilliant and bright young woman in front of her. 

Maybe in her younger years they had been a little more on the neurotic side, but it had stemmed from a place of wanting to keep her safe. It had been hard when Dani started getting a little older simply because Agatha had worked so much that they hadn't gotten much time together. 

Rio had found a quick remedy to that. 

Every Saturday had been Dani and Agatha's day. They would sometimes go out to a film or go shopping. Other times, they would camp out in the living room and watch movies or play card games. All of that time was exclusively theirs; if they stayed in, Rio would busy herself with errands or tuck away in the bedroom. If they went out, Rio would grocery shop and tend to things around the house. The majority of the day was focused solely on Agatha and Dani spending quality time together. Sundays were family days, the days they all spent together, but Satudays had been a treasure until the time Dani had moved out.

That Saturday, the two of them standing in their kitchen, it was still a treasure. Not necessarily the day itself. No, that had never really been the treasure.

The important thing had become remembering what was, even in the face of more time and more uncertainty.

Dani was the true treasure. 

Dani had helped carry them through a life that might have otherwise been empty. She had given them that sense of responsibility back, had made sure that they knew they were destined to be parents. Dani had been the light in what had seemed like an endless dark and as such, Agatha knew that she would never to be able to tell Dani verbally just how much she truly was loved by the both of them.

Agatha's lips twisted for a moment as she considered a thought before she spoke. "Can I ask you something?" she posted gently as her eyes landed into ones that were nearly an identical reflection of her own.

Dani crossed over to where she was, leaning her hip against the counter as she looked at Agatha straight-on. "Ask away, momma."

A soft sigh passed through Agatha's nose, her gaze darting over Dani's features as she tried to establish some nerve. "Are you okay?" she questioned quietly, though she was quick to add on. "And don't lie to me. I know when you're lying. Just... Tell me the truth."

Dani's expression softened and that look in her eyes was gentle, vulnerable almost. She set her soda can on the counter and laid her hand overtop Agatha's, not breaking her focus on Agatha as she did so.

"Momma, listen," Dani voiced, giving her hand a light squeeze. "I want to tell you first and foremost that I am okay. So do not waste even a second of your time or an ounce of your energy on trying to cater to me and make me feel like I'm not being forgotten. I am a grown woman and I fully understand the gravity of what it happening, and what it means to both of you."

She paused, finally tearing her eyes away to glance down at their hands before she let go and stepped forward, wrapping her arms around Agatha's waist, hugging her tightly. There was zero hesitation from Agatha as she returned the hug, but Dani had not been done offering her unofficial therapy sesson.

"I can't promise that it's going to be okay. But... I can promise that we're going to get through it, whatever happens. Because that's what we do. We soldier forward and never stop. So, whatever you need... Just ask me. I'm here for a week at least. Finals are mid-May so, if needed I'm sure I can figure something out." She took a breath and Agatha could feel her hold constrict a little more. "I know this is hard. I know it hurts. But we have each other."

In that moment, her face buried in her daughter's hair, Agatha knew something for absolute certain:

There was nothing of greater value in all of existence than the love the three of them had for one another, and everything else be damned, it was going to carry them through.

 

Nikolai.

It had been three days.

Every single second of every minute that it had taken Nik and Gabi to leave the police station and get him home and in bed, they blurred together in a smattering of city lights and Gabi's soft voice as she surely tried to offer gentle affirmation and displays of her love, but he hadn't been listening. He could hear her, he simply hadn't been able to understand her. Maybe that was significant solely because he suddenly felt like she didn't understand him, at all.

The evidence for such a hypothesis lay in the fact that he did not know himself. If that fact held true, how could anyone else? He had been presenting this genuine image of who he thought he was. He had been a gentle boy, feeling estranged and isolated very frequently due to the way he was constantly moved around. He had been a dedicated and driven teenager, playing baseball and football on opposing seasons. He had been a smart student, a good friend when he could make them. 

Even as an adult, Nik had struggled, but he had still found his way. He had spent his senior year of high school and the beginning of his freshman year at NYU sleeping with anyone who would pay him attention. He would wake up tangled in some man he'd met after too much to drink, or a woman that had apparently come home with him after a night out. And then, he'd gotten closer to Gabi and everything changed.

He had told everyone that he was an only child with just his mother. He had spent so long dodging the 'other parent' questions because he had never had any answers to provide. His mother -- No, Wanda -- had deprived him of those answers. Now, he knew why.

In three days, he had consumed chicken broth and crackers two times and had otherwise asked to be left alone. A couple of sips of water occasionally passed through his lips when his mouth was unbearably dry, both otherwise he simply laid in bed oscillating between crying and trying to string together nonsensical pieces that would never fit together.

In any other circumstance, he would have been worried about Gabi's feelings before his own, but his entire world had been shattered and he cared for nothing other than trying to sleep as much as possible to prevent the tearing ache from sinking him to an unreachable depth. She would hold him, but he would not move. She would tell him she loved him, time and time again, but he never spoke.

Not until evening time on the third day. He had somehow dragged himself from the safety of their comforter and had showered, propping himself up in bed once he was done.

The shower had given him time to think.

Everything Alisa -- Wanda -- had done had been fake, a construction of what she wanted him to see. 

So what was it that she had been trying to keep him from?

Nik leaned over the edge of the bed and picked up his laptop, opening it as Gabi appeared in the doorway. His eyes flickered to her for just a moment and he could see that hope there in her soft smile, a small joy that he was at least moving around enough to have showered and be sitting up in bed.

"Can I make you some cheese toast?" she asked him from he place directly over the threshold. "You need to eat something with at least a little protein."

As he finished typing in his password, his head lifted and his gaze found her again.

Nik knew she was trying to help. He knew that she loved him and only wanted to make this easier and while he still did not feel as though he could stomach much, he gave a gentle nod. He didn't want it, but that wasn't the question she asked. She asked if she could. And yes, she could. He just couldn't guarantee that he would actually eat it.

"Thank you," she said softly. She started to depart, but she stopped and cast her gaze upon him again. "I love you, Nik."

A tight smile found him as a reaction, but he tempered it to be softer as he spoke. "I love you too, Gabi."

The moment she was gone, his focus was back on the laptop. He knew what he was looking for. He knew their names, knew where they lived. Without reserves, he began to type.

There were several old news articles, photos of them at press conferences and during interviews. There were also videos, but he could not even fathom the idea of  opening a single one. He wasn't ready to hear their voices, or see them in motion. In the text, he had found another name.

Danica Harkness-Vidal.

That was his next search inquiry. The results that appeared were varied, extending from accomlishments with orchestras or events were she had performed to her social media. He glanced through a couple of the articles, but they weren't inclusive of photos. What he had learned was that at twenty-one years old, she was already and accomplished musician and she had yet to even graduate Julliard. She played the violin and had traveled quite a bit to display her talent.

Without putting a face to the accomplishments, he doubled back and headed for the safest bet: Instagram.

Immediately, he felt like he had been struck by lightning. They didn't look identical, but he could instantly locate a few features in her that he could see so clearly when he looked at his own reflection. She had a bright smile, a sweet disposition, and the brightest blue eyes Nik was certain he had ever seen in his life.

So he scrolled. He saw photos of her at bars he had been to, walking through alleys he had passed too many times to count. He saw photos of her with her parents -- hers, not theirs -- and the light they held in their faces when they looked at her. They looked like a picture-perfect family, a complete family.

They looked like a family where he would never belong.

Despite the sudden overwhelming tidal wave of alienation that felt like it was going to drown him, somehow, Nikolai found the will to keep scrolling. Judging by other photos, he had reached winter of that year, earlier on. There were photos of snow, and of her ice skating. And then, there was a different kind of photo.

It was a photo of Danica with a cupcake. 

Nik wasn't sure what drove him to do it, but he clicked on the thumbnail and opened the photo. It was bigger now, her holding it in the palm of her head as she beheld it like it were special, like it was something more than just a celebration for her.

When he read the caption below it, he understood why. And, quite frankly, it made him want to puke.

             For the last 19 years, you've always gotten a cupcake. Even when I'm not at home, I still pick one up and video call the moms so we can wish you another good year. 

            Happy birthday, Nicky. May this new year bring you all you need.

He hadn't even finished reading it and his eyes had already started to fill with hot and emotionally distraught tears. They fell even harder when he realized she had posted nine other photos from the last nine years. He had tried to look, as if he felt he deserved to be punished, but the moment he came across the first one of the three of them together, something came over him that he did not know how to explain. 

Both hands launched for the top of the laptop screen, slamming it down in his panic. Without a thought, he lifted the laptop in one hand and with a fervored might, he flung it like a frisbee across the room. It hit the wall next to the door, leaving a massive dent in the drywall, before it hit the ground and broke into several pieces.

Even before he buried his face in his hands, Nik was nowhere near ready to have the conversation he knew Gabi was going to want to have at the sound of such a disturbance.

"Baby?" came her worried call as she surged into the room.

Nik was already in the process of rolling to his side and pulling the comforter up over his shoulders.

"I just want to go back to sleep."

She might have offered opposition, but as he was getting so good at doing, he tuned her out and closed his eyes, wanting nothing more than to forget what he had seen.

Trying to sleep while realizing that he had a little sister who had been celebrating his birthday for almost her entire life felt like it might actually prove to be pointless.

It took him little time to realize that he was right.

 

Chapter 6: You'll Find Half What You Deserve

Gabi Mendoza.

When Gabi had been a little girl, she'd had a fixation on princess movies and in them, there was the typical guard walls trope.  It wasn't until she had gotten older that she realized it was a metaphor, and how it could be applied to certain people.

Since they had started dating halfway through freshman year at NYU, Nikolai had made her feel like a princess. It had taken them some time to reach that point; by the time he had broken up with his boyfriend, she had still been in a relationship. When the woman moved across the country, it felt a little serendipitous in the sense that it felt like life had intentionally given them gentle nudges toward one another.

Embracing them had been the best thing she had ever done. She had fallen in love with him easily, if not a little recklessly, and they had fallen into an complex but meaningful love, something Gabi had never really had a chance to experience before. She had still been young, sure, but what Nik made her feel? She wasn't sure if another person was capable of such a feat, even all this time later.

Nik was special.

Right then, as she stood in the doorway and watched him curl into himself for what felt like the hundredth time in the last three days, Gabi had no idea how she could convince him of such a truth. He had extricated her, placing the princess on the outside of those guard walls. They were high and impenetrable, meant to shut himself inside.

She had no scope, here. Because of that, she was floundering in trying to figure out what it was she could do to help him. He was detaching, pulling away. He was retreating into himself because he had nowhere else to go. Every choice he had made had been unknowingly dictated by an incident that had occurred at the very beginning of his life. She knew that left him wondering who he could have been if it had never happened.

Would he have stayed in one place? Would he have actually had friends for longer than eight or nine months before he was leaving again? 

There was something else that Gabi was all too aware he had to be feeling. 

She had done her own research in the hours he slept and if he came to the realization that he had a little sister that was not too much younger than the two of them were, she knew it was going to crush him.

Nik had told her on more than one occasion that he had always wanted a sibling. He didn't care if it would have been a brother or a sister, but he had always just... wanted someone he didn't have to leave behind. Gabi understood it. He also was going to shatter the first time he saw what his sister looked like, judging by her own unhindered reaction when she had found the girl on Facebook.

What she did not realize was that the time had come and the evidence lie in the broken pieces of the laptop on the floor and the massive dent in the wall above it, but she had no context to be absolute certain of that. Whatever it had been, it was enough to pull him back under, leaving the plate of half-assembled cheese toast abandoned on the counter.

She wanted to crawl into bed with him, to get in behind him and just wrap him up in her arms and whisper to him that she loved him until she didn't have a voice left to do so. The first two times she had tried, he had almost been angry. It seemed like he didn't want her to touch him, did want to accept her comfort and it was difficult to not take it personally, even with everything going on.

This was an impossible situation; it felt like the options were limited and nothing she chose was ever going to be the right thing. The only thing she wanted in all of it was to love him through it. She could ease his strain if he would just choose to buckle a little and let her in. All he had to do was drop those walls long enough for her to step in and he could throw them right back up.

As much as she had wished it would happen, she had known it wouldn't.

The next eight days were nearly unbearable. Nik was emotional, aggravated. He seemed to find fault in everything she did, even when she was just trying to help him. He became snappier and a little more stern with his word choices. 

Gabi knew what he was doing.

He was trying to push her away. He was trying to provide her with a list of reasons why she needed to run for the hills and avoid the mess his life was becoming. 

She was not going to let that happen. She loved him too much for that and she was not going to give in to such behavior. It was warranted, to an extent, and she was going to continue to give him time, but she wouldn't have been able to say honestly that she hadn't started to hurt, too, and more than just it being on his behalf.

There was a sense of understanding, an intelligible comprehension that his world was almost completely collapsing around him. She wasn't, though. Gabi was fighting through this hellacious storm to stay steady and present for him, even if everything he was doing was telling her he didn't want it. 

Not even being able to touch him without upsetting him was crushing, a new kind of pain that Gabi had never experienced in the confines of their relationship. They had been together far too long and loved each other way too much to be reduced to this and it was killing her. 

Nevertheless, Gabi's persistence did not waver in the slightest, even if Nik's irritation didn't either. She had stopped trying to coax him into any kind of conversation and had instead opted to make him a bowl of soup or a grilled cheese sandwich that she would leave on his nightstand. When she would return a couple of hours later, there were at least a couple of bites missing. She'd refill his glass, replace it where it belonged and then spend about ten seconds fighting her urge to lean over and kiss his temple or cheek.

Nik had been explicit in his requests to be left alone and so, she had listened.

For an entire week after the laptop incident, she listened. 

It was the hardest feat to accomplish; she was living in that apartment like she was the only one there. She came and went as she needed for work and to do things like grocery shop. She declined texts asking her to come out, unable to explain the situation and not ready to leave him longer than she had to.

There had been only a couple of instances when Gabi had been almost concerned enough to make a phone call, to have him admitted into a hospital. She knew if she chose that route, he would likely never forgive her. Realistically, he needed the help, but she wondered if isolating him from herself would be the right move, even if he had done a pretty good job of doing it himself.

For a week, Gabi fell asleep on the couch with some Netflix show playing in the background. She would wake up in the middle of the night and not rest until she at least checked on him and made sure he was drinking some of the water that was being left.

On two of those seven nights, she did not accomplish such a mission. She would get up and hear the sounds of his sobs faintly as they carried down the hall and stop, silent. Gabi knew what he felt and what it was he had asked of her, but she knew on those nights that if she made it into the bedroom, it was going to be next to impossible for her to not crawl into bed with him and completely drown him in her embrace.

By the time they were tiptoeing closer to two weeks of his endless moping and isolation, Gabi was at her wits' end. She had to do something because so far, nothing else was working. As much as she wanted to claim that it had everything to do with his misery, it was more than that.

She felt absolutely fucking useless.

Gabi was his girlfriend, his partner in crime, his whole world for the last seven years. There was not a single thing in the world that she would not have done to make his life easier. She would have traveled to the farthest reaches of the planet if it meant finding a way to ease his broken heart. 

The fact that he was not letting her was driving her to the brink of madness. She loved him, more than she had ever known was humanly possible, and so... Gabi pulled out her tablet and began an avalanche of morally ambiguous decisions. 

First, she dug right back into the news articles and interviews that had been uploaded in terrible quality from when everything had first happened. The photos from the newspapers seemed a little clearer than the images on the videos, but she found exactly what she needed 20 minutes in.

One of the interviews she had watched had stated that the family lived in North Ironbound. In one of the paper scans, she could see the house number '8805' lined vertically down a front white post.

Next, she searched for houses in North Ironbound with such a house number. There were two.

Fuck.

Wait! Street view!

She tapped a couple more times, bringing up the view for the first one, her breath catching the moment it displayed across the screen. That was it. It was that one.

8805 Townstall Drive.

Something took over her; she tapped on the arrow that displayed the exact time and route that would take them directly to his parents. 

It was forty-five fucking minutes away. 

They were so fucking close.

The only reason Gabi realized she had started to cry was because it had suddenly become impossible to see her screen with the blurriness that came with the tears. He was so fucking close to a family that had likely been waiting his entire fucking life to know he was okay. 

And he wanted nothing to do with it.

All he wanted to do was lay in bed and avoid the world at large, her included. Some part of her understood that it wasn't personal and yet, it wounded her with vigor all the same.

Something had to change. There had to be some kind of give somewhere.

Gabi realized, after another forty minutes of watching the interviews again, that she herself was going to have to be the give.

After pulling down a notebook and grabbing a pen, she perched at the dining room table and stared down at the blank page. She knew that she could have been writing to both of them, but there had been something that pulled her attention more one way than the other.

Of his parents, Agatha had clearly been the one leading the charge. Every single time she was on camera, her shoulders were square and she held her chin high. She was defiant and demanding of his return, declaring that there would be rewards for those who helped and condemnation for the perpetrator. 

And then, there was Rio.

She looked just as determined and just as hopeful, but there was a softness to her that her wife did not care to utilize. Where Agatha used force, Rio used emotion. She would look out to whatever small crowd was before them, her eyes hollow as they searched for a familiar face, one she never found. She would glance at the camera and manage the tightest, most painful smile as if she needed the world to understand what it was she was feeling. She held silent conversations with everyone present as well as everyone that took the time to watch. Rio ached to have her son back, all those years ago, and something about that struck Gabi.

With a few more moments of contemplation, Gabi got to her feet and peered into the bedroom, not at all surprised to find Nik buried under the covers. She couldn't see if he was actually awake, but she supposed whether or not he was happened to be neither here nor there. He still didn't want to speak to her, or at all, and so Gabi made her way right back to the dining room table.

And then, she began to write.

            Dear Rio,

            I know that the last thing you're expecting on a random afternoon is to be opening an actual hand-written letter, but I was not certain what other avenue would be appropriate to reach out, given the circumstances. And... Who writes letters anymore anyway? Well, for the first time in years, I guess I do.

           I'm sorry. I have forgotten my manners. My name is Gabriela Mendoza. I have been dating Nikolai Malikov -- or, as we have recently found out, your son Nicholas -- for almost seven years. We met at NYU and have lived very full lives since then. 

         I am writing this letter to you knowing that I shouldn't. I know that if he were to finally get out of bed for the first time in nearly two weeks and see this, he might be very upset with me, but I am just so... lost, I guess is the right word. We have been through some trials throughout the duration of our relationship, things that don't need great detail, and yet I have never witnessed this side of him.

         In my deepest of dreams, he will simply wake up one morning and just know that he wants to change what he's been doing and find a way forward. In this world, in our reality, I do not even know that I can pinpoint when he will even shower next, let alone when he may brave to speak more than a handful of words.

        I understand he is suffering. I understand that his entire identity has been taken from him, but I also know that the further he slips from me, the more I worry he may never come back. And I also have thought a lot about that. And how it relates to you and your family. Your wife, your daughter. His mother, his sister. 

       I shouldn't be offering this because I have never kept secrets from him the entire time we have been together, but I'm going to leave my number below. If you think that you might be willing to meet up for coffee sometime, please shoot me a text message and we will figure something out. I know that he isn't ready to know you, but that should not prolong your ability to at least have some idea of the incredible man he is. 

      If you're comfortable, please do reach out and we can set something up. 

Sincerely,
Gabi Mendoza
973-899-1384

Gabi read over the letter, realizing that she should probably scrap it and start over, but it said exactly what she needed it to say, even if there was a little bit of rambling thrown in the mix. She was trying to convey just what it was that she was watching while not alarming the other woman if she could avoid it. 

It was likely as good as it was going to get and so, she folded it up, shoved it into an envelope and licked the seal, pressing it shut. Despite her still-shaking hand, she scrawled a neat 'Mrs. Rio Harkness-Vidal' and printed the address below it clearly. For a moment, her dark gaze flickered to the corner of the envelope and her lower lip tucked between her teeth, the enamel sinking roughly into the pad of flesh.

Ultimately, she decided that writing a return address was a terrible idea. In the event that he ended up pissed off at her for having reached out to people he was not ready to accept as part of him and his life, he would have been downright furious if she had so carelessly forked their address over to them without even speaking to him about it first.

After pressing on a stamp, Gabi had paced her way to their bedroom doorway, her voice soft as she called to him despite not knowing if he was even awake.

"I'm running to the bodega. I'll be back soon. I love you."

He didn't say it back. It made her hope beyond anything that it was because he was asleep.

To make her lie into a half-truth, Gabi had stopped at the bodega first and picked up a bag of chips and a pint of ice cream for herself and a bottle of Sprite for Nik. He might not touch it, but she figured it would be a nice change of pace from water. On second thought, she scooped up a packet of fruit snacks that tasted like Arizona beverages. Again, he might not touch them, but if he could put even a few on his stomach, he would be better off.

After the quick stop, she ventured to the post office and stood in front of the express mail receptacle, staring at it long and hard. Once she dropped the letter inside, that was it. There was no going back once she lifted the steel flap and let it fall amongst the other mail and postage.

Taking a deep breath, Gabi pulled down the handle and slid the envelope inside, shutting it with a loud SNAP of metal on metal.

With that, Gabi climbed back into her car and drove home to another night where she would fall asleep alone on her couch.

It would be another night that the man she loved lay still in his misery, unwilling to let her in.

Maybe the letter would work, maybe it wouldn't.

At least when she fell asleep that night, Gabi could lay claim to the fact that she had done something, at bare minimum.

 

Rio.

Although Agatha had made the decision to return to work, claiming that she needed to focus her attention elsewhere, Dani was still posted up in the office on the second story for several hours a day, tending to her lectures and prepping for her final exams. It had been two weeks to the day since they had found out about Nicky's very close yet very distant existence.

Rio knew the truth, though.

She knew it was killing Agatha to sit around the house and just hope that one of their phones would ring. Rio knew that when Agatha was home and unoccupied, her mind spun circles about the things they could not have, and it was tearing her apart.

Agatha had always found comfort in her career and if it could offer her some sort of solace in a time when they all felt as though they were talking on pins and needles, then Rio thought she should take it.

Rio also realized that Agatha's returning to work had been the likely catalyst for Dani's decision to stay longer. 

There were two people in the world that Rio knew like the back of her hand, and one of them was Dani. In turn, Dani knew her just as well. Rio never would have admitted it, but the thought of being alone when Agatha was at work and Dani had gone to finish out the year at school was damn near debilitating. 

Keeping busy had been easier when she had distractions in the form of her loved ones. Managing to find a place to put her mind that did not sink deeper and deeper into the pits of just wishing Nicky would call had been difficult, but when Dani wanted to play Wii Bowling, or when Agatha was spending money on things they didn't need, it happened with a little less resistance from her subconscious. 

It was nice sometimes just to hear Dani's voice down the hall when she was answering questions or asking them. It was nice when she would come downstairs for lunch and they would whip something up together and eat on the back patio to enjoy the weather. It was even nice when Dani would whip into the room, frantic about something in relation to school until they talked it out and Rio helped her form a plan.

Midday on a Friday, Rio found herself baking a batch of cookies to keep her mind centered on a task and not the length of time that had passed since their lives had irrevocably changed for the second time. When she heard the mail flap rattle and the soft woosh as a couple of envelopes dropped through and hit the ground.

It was not of utter importance; they were not expecting anything of significance and so, Rio kept her attention on the bowl of dough she was mixing. In fact, she had been in the middle of popping the sheet pan into the oven when Dani came down the stairs. Before she ventured toward the kitchen, she must have caught sight of the mail and went to collect it, flipping through it as she paced to meet Rio where she was closing the oven door.

"Bills, bills, bi -- Wait. What's this?" Dani questioned, picking up the envelope that had caught her attention. She stared at it for a moment before she flipped it around in her grasp, showing it to Rio.

In a very tidy script, it was her name, hand-written as 'Mrs. Rio Harkness-Vidal.'

Also obvious was the fact that there was no return address. 

Something dangerous in Rio's stomach began to twist and clench. It made no sense. She didn't know what that letter was and she didn't know who such handwriting belonged to, but something in her felt the dread regardless.

Her lips pressed as she gingerly plucked it from Dani's hold, bringing it closer for inspection. It didn't give her anything else, and she was sure she would find nothing until she opened it and revealed the contents.

"Mom?" Dani questioned softly.

At the sound of her voice, Rio realized she had been holding her breath for some reason she didn't understand. She exhaled and lifted her gaze to Dani first and then the timer on the oven; she had eleven minutes until the cookies would be done. 

Rio did not speak as she carried herself to the dining room table and sat, flipping the envelope over in her hands. With a steadying intake of a large breath, she ripped open the envelope and removed the piece of paper that had been cradled inside. 

When she unfolded it, Rio was not sure what she was expecting to find written on it. As she started to read, she was still confused throughout the first paragraph. And then came the second.

One of Rio's hands launched away from the paper, fingertips grazing the skin of her face as her hand raised to her mouth in nothing but pure shock.

"Mom? Mom, what is it?" Dani questioned, having taken the seat at the end of the table next to her. It kept her from being able to see what Rio was reading.

Rio did not answer. Instead, she kept reading. The tears had started and she was worried that at this rate, they were never going to stop. She kept trying to read, kept wiping them away so that could see clearer.

Dani, a foot away from her, was about to completely short-circuit. She was impossibly worried and concern had etched itself into every inch of her beautiful features. She wanted to keep pressing, clearly, but she had likely deduced that Rio was not going to immediately provide any kind of a response. She just kept reading.

As she got closer to the end, a choked and stifled sob escaped Rio, filtering out from between her fingers as her hand remained close to her mouth.

The secrecy landed somewhere uncomfortable in Rio's stomach, but there was something larger that was overshadowing it. What was bigger was the fact that this woman had been in a serious relationship with Nicky for seven long years and she had made it very clear that secrets were not a currency they chose to use. For her to be going behind his back to send that letter, it didn't show that she disrespect him and his wishes. It showed how much she loved him and how she wanted to find action in the throes of eviscerating inaction.

What Rio saw in that letter, and the two little spots at the bottom that had since dried, was a woman who was lost, who knew no answer to how to help the person she loved. What Rio saw in those words was a cry for help, and it hit her directly in the chest like a brass-knuckled punch, cracking ribs that poked and prodded her heart and lungs. 

When Dani spoke again, the only reason she garnered Rio's attention was because she touched her, fastening a palm over her arm. "Mom? Hey, look at me please?"

Rio's jaw swelled as it clenched and she raised her hand from her mouth to wipe at her soaked cheeks, covered in every bit of emotion that had spilled from her at the weight of what she was holding. After a moment of trying to collect herself, her eyes lifted and finally met Dani's, her lips twisting in her hurt and anguish.

"What is that?" her daughter asked calmly, her thumb brushing over Rio's arm in comfort.

"It's..." Rio attempted, but it could hardly be called a noise, let alone an entire word. She sniffled and drew in a full, long breath as she searched for any ability to be somewhat articulate in the face of such heavy and weighted emotions. "It's from... From Nicky -- Nikolai's girlfriend, the... The girl from the photos, I'm guessing..." she finally managed to stammer, her voice crackling and breaking despite her best efforts.

"Wait... She wrote you a letter? Not... Not him?" Dani asked back, her brow knitting as a sign of her confusion. Rio could hear that tiny little tremble in her words, the way she was as disbelieving as Rio had been when she understood what it was that she was reading.

"It sounds like..." Rio's gaze dropped to the letter and then lifted again, an uncertainty washing through those dark irises as she considered. "It doesn't sound like he's okay. He... Is struggling and she... She wants to meet with me..."

Rio had paused, but Dani chomped at the bit of silence she had been offered so that she could interject.

"Mom! She wants to meet you?!" 

The excitement in Dani's voice was almost soul shattering. She hadn't read the entire letter the way Rio had and she didn't know that this wasn't happy, it wasn't exciting. This seemed to be something that had been done out of necessity. Someone in his world recognized that while he was hurting, he was not the only one.

Rio realized that it didn't just apply to her, or just to Agatha and Dani. Clearly, Gabi was hurting, too. It was why she had made a very big and very brave decision to extend some kind of olive branch to a family who had spent so long knowing absolutely nothing. It was why she was willing to go behind her boyfriend's back because she was not certain that he would ever recover and if he didn't, the people missing him didn't deserve to be shut into the dark for the remainder of their lives.

For as much as Gabi saw their pain, Rio could see Gabi's, too.

Maybe she didn't have anyone she could talk to about the situation.  Maybe she was isolated in her knowledge and clearly, it didn't seem as though they had an open line of communication about his thoughts and feelings. Whatever it was she was feeling, it had pushed her to the point of reaching out. Maybe Rio should have been a bit more concerned over the fact that the woman had obtained her address, but with what had been poured onto that paper? She never could have been upset or even felt a drop of worry. The fact that she had sent a letter via snail mail was a very blatant display of that.

"I..." Once more, Rio's dark eyes fell to the paper that was now wrinkled from her grip on the left side. "I don't... Know what to do."

Dani could see it, the way Rio was beginning to panic. She could see every single thought, all one thousand and eight of them, as they whipped through her head and across her dark eyes.

"Mom, look at me," she commanded quietly, giving Rio's arm a firm squeeze. "It's okay. What we're going to do right now is we're going to fold it up and put it back in the envelopes. Then, when momma comes home, you're going to get it out and the two of you are going to talk about it." She sounded so fucking calm and Rio simply couldn't understand. Instead, she chose to pull from that serenity, trying to absorb as much of it as she could possibly manage. 

"But I --"

Another squeeze, another silent request for attention the moment Rio had started to lose her focus. Very carefully, Dani raised her other hand and pinched the paper between her fingers, lightly tugging it in an attempt to get Rio to release her hold.

"It's going to hurt you more than it's going to help you to read it over and over again until momma gets home. We need to put it away until there's an availability for both of you to handle it how you see fit."

Rio was over fifty years old and yet, right then, her barely alcohol-legal daughter was somehow stitching her together enough to keep her whole. She was supplying logic and pointing out the obvious things Rio could not see. Dani had a clearer perspective; her hopes were of course to meet her brother, but not having done so, she could be unequivocally objective.

Watching helplessly as Dani folded the paper back up without intruding on its contents by reading it, Rio felt a despair that almost seemed surreal. How could it hurt this bad to know that answers could be right there, but there were heavy considerations that needed to be taken? How could it be this fucking painful to know that if she said no, it was very possible they might not get them any other way?

Tucking it back into the envelope, Dani laid it down on the table and pushed it away from the both of them. She turned her attention back to Rio, picking up her hand to give it a tight squeeze of comfort.

"I have another class, but when I'm done, I'm going to run to the market and pick up some things to make enchiladas. Can I take the car so I don't have to pay for an Uber?" Dani was keeping her engaged intentionally, asking question that required Rio to think about anything other than that letter, currently burning a hold in their dining room table.

Rio tore her eyes away from it, landing into Dani's sweet blues. "Y-Yeah, of course. You know where the keys are. I think... It's probably best if I lay down for --"

Committed to the idea of trying to rest when she was absolutely buzzing, the way the timer rang shrill and loud to indicate that the cookies were finished sank a pit of disappointment to the bottom of her stomach. Before she could push to her feet to tend to the still screaming timer and the cookies in the oven, Dani stood and kissed the side of her head, departing to do it for her.

"Go lay down, mom," she offered from her place in front of the oven, turning her head over her shoulder a beat to ensure that Rio had heard her.

Rio did not nod, did not verbally agree, but she did stand and make her way toward her daughter. The moment the pan was out of Dani's hands and Rio was free to do so, she pulled her little girl into a strong hug, grappling her tightly with a forlorn sense of guilt that somehow, she was letting Dani down.

"Do you know that momma and I sometimes talk about how we do not know what on earth we did to deserve you?" Rio murmured at her, clinging a little tighter.

"I can tell you, if you'd like," Dani whispered back, her arms wrapping a little more around her mom. She did not give Rio the time to decline the offer before she started anyway. "You have always loved me, probably before I was even born. You have always taken care of me and have always given me what I have needed. You have always encouraged me to chase my passions and my talents. You have taught me countless lessons in what it means to be a good person and to make choices with the knowledge that sometimes I'm not always the only one effected."

Rio could feel that welling of emotion rise, threatening to spill the longer Dani went on, but Rio couldn't bring herself to cut her off.

"You have looked me in the eyes when I broke off an engagement that I had no business agreeing to in the first place and you told me it was okay, even when it didn't feel that way. You have always been there for me, both of you, and that's what you've done to deserve me. I am who I am because you and momma raised me and helped me to become this person. So..." Dani hesitated, her eyes flicking unwillingly to the dining room table before they landed back on Rio. "When you start feeling as though any of this is your fault, please remember that you've loved us both every day of our lives, and you have always done what you could to protect us. Both of us." 

She pulled away and Rio could feel the tears falling before Dani even reached up to cup her cheeks in both palms.

"This is a baby step. It's one you and momma get to decide how to take. But... We're not completely stalling anymore," Dani offered. Her thumbs were so gentle and tender as she brushed at Rio's cheeks lovingly.

"You're right," Rio agreed in a sniffle. She took an even and deep breath, letting it go just as slowly. "I'm going to go lay down. But wake me up when you come home from the store please?"

"How about I wake you when dinner's done? Or momma might get to it first depending on when she gets home," Dani bartered. It was her underhanded way of urging Rio to take a little more time for herself, even if she wouldn't state it outright.

Rio found herself lost in those eyes, so moved by just how solid Dani was being in the face of nothing but pure chaos. As Dani let her go, Rio took her own turn to cup Dani's cheek in her palm, tilting her head a little in her reverence.

"I love you, Boog. Me and momma both."

Dani knew it, but seeing the look on her face at hearing Rio reiterate it finally stoked the smallest flame in Rio's chest.

"I love you too, now get some rest."

"Aye aye, Doctor Dani."

Dani didn't speak again, but the way she rolled her eyes and gave Rio a light push seemed to say enough, and Rio disappeared up the stairs to try and find some stillness in sleep.

 

Agatha.

As Agatha walked through the front door to their home, she should have been drained. She should have been upset that she was almost a half an hour late because her last surgery had run over due to unexpected complications. She should have been frazzled, but the only thing she could find purchase in was the anxiety that had overwhelmed her at the text she'd gotten from Dani when she'd finally been able to check her phone.

Boog: I'm at the store. Is there
anything you need me to pick
up? Mom's sleeping, but make
sure you wait for me to come
home before you wake her up.
There's something I need to
tell you.

Agatha's lips had twisted and pressed, so firm and tight that she was almost chewing on the insides of them. Sitting in her car after such a shift had given her only a moment of respite before she was winding her way home, able to feel every single pulse point in her body as they pounded with her anxiety and cluelessness.

Me: I'm heading home now. My
last surgery ran over. Are you 
home now?

Boog: Yeah. Starting dinner.
See you when you get here. I
love you, momma.

Me: I love you too, boog. See 
you soon.

Agatha slipped her phone into its holder and headed home, walking in that door a short while later to a plethora of delicious smells as they filled the house.

After shedding anything she did not need -- including her scrub top that left her in a tight white tank top -- Agatha made her way into the kitchen. The first thing she saw was Dani hard at work at the stove, though it looked like she had just gotten into the thick of it.

"Hi my little chef," Agatha crooned, stepping up behind Dani to place a hand on her back and a kiss to the side of her head.

"Hi, momma," she greeted, turning to toss a light smile Agatha's way.

"Is mom okay?" Agatha questioned softly, her palm rubbing mindlessly at Dani's back.

"She will be. But..." Dani set down the tongs that she had been using to tend to the chicken before she looked up at Agatha, her gaze vulnerable. "She received a letter today. A letter from... From Nicky's -- Nikolai's -- Whatever we're calling him until we know for sure, but it was from his girlfriend..."

Agatha felt like someone had launched a spear of ice directly through her chest.

Rio had gotten a letter? A hand-written letter? From their son's girlfriend? She was trying to answer those questions with the information she had just been provided, but it didn't seem like it could be a possibility in any reality.

"You... What did it say?" Agatha stumbled, her eyes wide as she stared her daughter down, assuming she had all of the answers.

"I don't know, I didn't read it," Dani admitted. 

Something about the admission caused Agatha's brows to pinch above the bridge of her nose. She could have. Dani could have read it if she had wanted to, but she still had made the decision not to. Agatha didn't need to know why, but she couldn't stop herself from asking.

"Why not?" 

"Because, momma, I saw what it did to mom and I realized that it's something you both should see and discuss first. If you want to show it to me after that discussion is over, I'm okay with that. But... You guys need to talk about it first." Her voice was so steady, even as she turned back to the task of tending to dinner.

"You're an insane kid, you know that right?" Agatha asked her, leaning in to place another loving kiss to the side of Dani's head.

"Yeah, I get it pretty honestly," she shot back, managing a smile that touched her eyes as she glanced to her mother. "But she's been sleeping a while. If you go now, dinner will be ready when you're finished."

Agatha knew she was right, and she had every intention of listening, but there was something she had to say first.

"There's not a day that goes by where momma and I don't realize how lucky we are to have you. I hope you know that." 

In a reaction that surprised Agatha, Dani laughed. Agatha's eyebrows shot up, stunned by the sound and her eyes were curious, wondering. She didn't have to wonder too long; Dani answered with a grin.

"Mom and I had a very similar conversation before she went to rest. So... It's just funny how you two have a hive mind after all this time." Dani had diverted her attention back to the skillet in front of her, but the only thing she was missing was the utter adoration and affection that was broadcasting from Agatha's expression.

Agatha stepped away and pulled a bottle of water from the refrigerator before glancing back at Dani, softening at the sight of her cooking away in front of the stove.

"I love you, booger butt," Agatha called, heading upstairs to wake her slumbering wife.

The first thing that Agatha noticed when she entered their bedroom was that Rio had turned on the fan, and that it was all the way up. It wasn't pointed at her, but Agatha quickly realized it had been to help her sleep. Dani's voice had likely been keeping her away and so, she'd tried to make it a little less prominent. 

Casting her eyes toward the bed, she was genuinely surprised to see Rio fully on the wrong side -- Agatha's side -- of the bed, the comforter shoved back and the sheets twisted around her torso, legs fully exposed. 

It wasn't necessarily an indication that anything was wrong, per say, but Agatha could see with an internal illumination that Rio had missed her while she was gone. They had been married a very long time and while they weren't exactly clingy, there were some days when the forced absence of responsibility was a little harder to shoulder. Going back to work had been for the betterment of Agatha's mental well-being, but with recent events, she admittedly had been a bit selfish in that she hadn't really stopped to consider how Rio was feeling about it, too.

Instead, Agatha had focused on her own feelings, on the anger she tried not to stew in at being told time and time again to call back to the county jail and they might have an available time where she could go and speak with Wanda. 'Speak' was probably an impossibly loose term there, but Agatha deserved face time with the woman who had ruined so many lives and she was not going to rest until someone granted it to her.

Until then, work had been enough to keep her distracted.

At least, it had been. Now, Agatha had the corner of that envelope pinched tight in her grasp as she moved silently about the room, wanting to allow Rio just a few more minutes. Moreover, she wanted to give herself some time to discover what had been sent to her wife and why it had her daughter being vaguely supportive in the best way. 

The bottle of water landed on the night stand and she let the envelope fall to the bed so that she could shed her scrub pants and climb onto the bed, covering her legs with a small portion of the comforter her wife had discarded. In her settling, she glanced to her left, watching her sleeping wife with her face buried in Agatha's pillow, searching for comfort even in her slumber.

Finally, Agatha grabbed the envelope off of the bed and did not waste a single second before she was removing the letter, discarding the vessel that had been holding it, and unfolding it before her so that she could reveal what it was that had everyone she loved out of sorts.

Agatha had been lacking that anticipatory anxiety despite seeing the impact it had delivered, but the moment she began to read enough that she understood, something in her swelled and pressed on every single nerve she had.

Someone that knew their son -- very, very well as it seemed -- was reaching out. Someone that loved him and cared about him was too scared of what could happen if he did not find some form of recover and so, she was trying to offer what remedy she could as a concerned third party.

The other woman's guilt was clear in her words, an overt display that it was not her goal to betray her boyfriend, but to try to bridge a gap that he was not willing to acknowledge.

Agatha read it three more times and was in the middle of a fourth one when she jumped at the feeling of Rio's hand landing lightly against her hip. She sucked in a sharp breath and dropped her gaze to the woman next to her, the exhaustion still visible on her face, esepcially with how her eyes were still closed. 

"Hi, my love," Agatha cooed at her, lifting her right hand to brush her knuckle along Rio's cheek. "I think you got a little turned around. You ended up on the wrong side of the bed." The joke fell flat, but it was only due to the fact that Agatha's voice was shaking too badly to make her sound confident in the delivery.

"I didn't. You couldn't hug me, but I could still lose myself in you when you weren't here," Rio muttered, causing Agatha's already crumbling heart to crack further. She had rushed so quickly to try and find a sense of normal and it was clearly impacting the woman she loved, maybe even more than she was seeing in those moments.

Agatha reached down for Rio's hand, lifting it so that she could press her lips to her wife's knuckles. When she lowered it, she did not let go and instead formed a tight grip over Rio's fingers.

"I know. But... Dani left me the source of your discord and I have read it... A few times..." Agatha looked back toward the paper for just a moment before looking down at Rio again. This time, she had opened her eyes. Agatha's lips worried together for a moment as she tried to map out how this conversation might play out best. She had options but something in her felt as though she needed to charge forward, taking to it head-on.

"What are you thinking? Do you... Do you want to message her?" Agatha questioned softly, her thumb brushing automatically over Rio's fingers.

Rio was quiet, taking the time she needed to find the right answer to that question. Before she dispelled it and broke through any selfless facade she had been trying to maintain, she sat up and pushed the covers aside so that she could move to sit perpendicular to Agatha, Rio's knees bumping Agatha's hip and she side of her leg. Rio picked up her hand again.

"I do. And I've thought a lot about it. It... It unsettled me, the secrecy, but... Then I saw the desperation and the love. I saw that she is out of options and so, she wanted to help somehow, even if she cannot help him right now." Rio was so fucking earnest in her delivery, so hopeful that they had been offered some sort of life vest when it felt like they'd started to drown all over again.

Rio drew in a shallow breath before she continued.

"I want to because selfishly, I feel like we deserve it. I feel like having some answers is... It's better than not having any at all." There was a beat of silence as Rio stared straight into Agatha's eyes, not blinking, not wavering. Agatha felt her grip tighten as she started to speak again, posing her question in something barely louder than a whisper. "What do you think I should do?"

The question was so small, so scared, as if Rio actually thought Agatha might tell her it was a bad idea. Truthfully, Agatha wasn't certain whether or not it was good or bad, but she didn't care. They had been starved of their son's presence for two and a half decades. Turning down even the smallest crumb of who he had become simply was not an available option.

"I think you should text her. And I think maybe you should offer Sunday at the cafe near the edge of town. Just the two of you. As much as I want to go... She wrote to you for a reason and I won't tread on that." Agatha's honesty was there, but it was clear that her reasoning was something she clearly held conviction in. Yes, she wanted to be there, but something in her gut told her that Rio might be able to get a bit more in return than she herself could.

Agatha could be... A little much, especially in high tension situations. The likelihood that she could grow frantic that they weren't getting enough, even though it was more than they had, it was high and she was firm in her belief that neither of them wanted to spook this poor woman.

"You're sure?" Rio asked quietly, playing with Agatha's fingers absentmindedly in her lap. 

"I am. Why don't you go ahead and do it now, that way we can go eat the enchiladas our daughter is making us for supper and watch a movie with her?" Agatha knew she didn't need to be convincing, but she wanted to offer a short list of distractions that might make the night ahead of them a little easier to get through as they tried not to focus on waiting for a text back.

 

Rio.

Languidly, Rio leaned back and stretched out to grab her phone off of Agatha's nightstand as she pulled it toward her and sat back up.

Agatha read the number off to her as she typed it into her phone and saved it under 'Gabi' and proceeded to pull up a message window. Before she even started to type, Agatha's hand landed on her knee and gave a gentle squeeze, as if to say 'You can do this.'

A deep breath helped to calm her as she typed out the message.

Me: Hi, Gabi. This is Rio. I got
