your letter and... I was wondering
if you might be able to meet me
at the Blueprint Cafe on Sunday 
morning. Whatever time would
work best for you. Please let me
know. Thank you.

And then, she pressed send.

 

Chapter 7: Please Keep Me in Frame

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Gabi.

When a soft ping sounded from Gabi's lap as she lounged on their couch with the television muted in the background, the sight of an unsaved number caused her stomach to leap into her throat. She couldn't see what it said right away, but something in her knew.

She knew it wasn't just a random number.

She was right.

862-978-0499: Hi, Gabi. This is Rio. I got
your letter and... I was wondering
if you might be able to meet me
at the Blueprint Cafe on Sunday
morning. Whatever time would
work best for you. Please let me
know. Thank you.

Holy fucking shit. 

When she penned the letter, Gabi wasn't entirely sure what it was she was hoping for. She wanted to say that she hoped Rio would engage and reach out -- like she was obviously doing -- but some part of her also hoped she would ignore it. It was the part of her that felt like she was betraying the man she loved in this roundabout way. 

He was clearly of no mind to be able to entertain the idea of conversing with his biological family, but Gabi had a unique perspective.

The more she watched Nik struggle and suffer, the more she found herself slipping into the shoes of what must have been an opposing party. She did her research, learned what she needed to know, and it tasked her with the comprehension they were probably suffering, too.

Maybe what she was doing would be considered a betrayal to him, but at this point... She didn't really have a whole lot of him left to hold onto.

He was slipping further and further away with every hour that passed and was clearly never going to be the one to reach out without extensive therapy and a deconstruction of his entire life. Understandably, it was going to take him a while to get there. That face alone, however, did not mean that the parents who had already been missing him for twenty-five years deserved to stay in the dark.

They should get to know who he was, even if they couldn't meet him.

Her head lifted, dark locks falling out of her face as she glanced toward their bedroom, not a sound coming from it. Nik was probably sleeping, and if not, he was wallowing in his misery and unwilling to let her help him. Stormy eyes stayed locked on the doorway for a moment longer before they dropped again to the phone in her lap, reading the message for a fifth time.

She shouldn't.

Gabi knew she she shouldn't.

But she wanted to, almost felt like she needed to.

So, she typed her response.

Me: I can do Sunday morning. Is
9:30 okay? I should be able to 
make it over there by then,
if it's alright with you. I just
need to figure out the best 
way to do it.

When she sent the message, Gabi also did something beyond her own comprehension: 

She held her breath.

She only realized she was doing so about twenty seven seconds later when her phone pinged again and she released it in a massive exhale, the tension in her body unlocking instantaneously.

862-978-0499: That would be perfect.
I will see you then. And I will be coming
alone. 

862-978-0499: Also... Thank you. For 
reaching out. You... There's hope now.
Thank you.

The moment the second text came through, Gabi's eyes filled and overflowed with silent tears. She wanted to sob, to cry, to completely throw herself to the ground in a tantrum of feeling utterly overwhelmed, but she didn't. All she did was sniffle softly, wiping at her cheeks with the back of her sweatshirt sleeve. 

If Nik heard her, she would have to explain.

She wasn't ready to do as much quite yet.

Me: No problem. Happy I could
help.

It was nonchalant but entirely feigned. Gabi could have spilled her guts then and there in a text message, but it wasn't the right way to go about it. She needed to physically see with her own eyes the kind of effect the entire ordeal was having on other people, the people who never stopped loving him, looking for him. She needed to meet these women he seemed to be so afraid of. Hell, she still hadn't been able to pry out of him why he'd smashed his laptop and that said something. It said he'd done his own research and did not like what he found.

Gabi told Rio in her letter that she and Nik didn't keep secrets. She meant it, but it was beginning to feel like the tides of change were coming in. Now, he was hiding his emotions and his thoughts from her. He was cocooning inside himself and shutting her out entirely and she could no longer take it. If she had to find his roots before he was able, she could no longer sit on her hands and do nothing. 

Gabi loved Nikolai and she meant what she'd said to him the night she placed that stupid fucking DNA test in his hands.

No matter who he was or where he came from, she was still going to love him. And she did. She loved him so much that she could feel herself aching with him, hurting with him, losing themselves to the darkness. She could feel his pain and she fucking hated it. Maybe it wasn't going to change after her coffee with Rio, but at least she would find some peace in knowing she made a slight difference, even if not for him. The misery was simply too much for everyone involved. Finding a way to taper it felt necessary, so she would do what she had to.

Gabi stowed her phone and made them both soup and grilled cheese for dinner. When she returned an hour later for his plate, he was wrapped back up in the comforter and did not move a muscle upon her entry. 

Despite the lack of... well, everything, Gabi was at least thankful that one side of the grilled cheese had maybe four bites taken out of it.

At least he was trying to eat.

"I love you," she voiced softly before slipping out of the room to clean up and try to sleep.

Saturday was more of the same dull ache and silence, but Gabi found herself hinging her hope on her meeting the next morning. When it finally came around, she hardly knew how to handle herself.

She woke at 6:13, which wasn't entirely unusual for her but still felt different due to the way her skin was buzzing with an emotion she knew not how to identify. She took a shower, pulled on a camisole, a cardigan, and a pair of dark wash jeans and dusted her face with a light layer of make-up, just enough to hide the bags beneath her eyes and the constant rosiness of her cheeks.

The last thing she needed was to show up looking like she'd been crying for weeks. That most certainly would not make the best first impression.

After leaving Nik with a soft kiss to his still cheek, a quick train ride, and an even quicker cab ride, Gabi found herself wrapped tightly in her cardigan, arms fastened over her middle as though she were trying to protect herself from a non-existent chill in the air.

She was really trying to ward off the immersive waves of guilt that crashed into her with every step she took toward the cafe. 

The moment she started to pass the windows, her eyes fell to look through them, scanning the inside of the business. Illogically, they landed on the near corner and landed on the sight of a lone woman, hair dark and chin tucked as she looked at whatever was on her phone. Gabi couldn't see the whole of her face, but she saw enough to match the nose and profile to one of the women she'd found in her research.

It was Rio.

She really had shown up. 

Gabi wasn't exactly surprised, but something in her churned and twisted, making her feel sick.

No.

She had to do this.

She had to walk into that cafe, question the woman gently to know for certain it was who she was there to meet, and sit down across from her to try and hold some form of conversation about the man she loved and the crisis he was in.

With the deepest breath she found herself capable of, Gabi pressed onward and entered the cafe.

The older woman's head did not lift and the bell above the door didn't seem to pull at her attention. She was fixated on her phone, leaving Gabi to do most of the work. That was fine, if not a little unnerving.

Slowly, she shuffled to the table, careful to keep her distance in case she'd approached the wrong person.

"Mrs. Harkness-Vidal?" she managed. She tried to make it sound strong, but instead she just sounded like a church mouse, barely a squeak to be heard.

Immediately, the woman's head snapped up and a kind smile warmed her face.

"You must be Gabi."

 

Rio.

The moment her dark eyes landed on the woman near the corner of the table, Rio wanted to melt. She'd been convincing herself it was all a fluke, that the woman who wrote her that letter would feel too guilty to actually show up. It was poured into every word she wrote; Rio could see just how much she loved their son and how badly it was hurting her to go behind his back. 

Yet somehow, Rio understood it without ever having to experience it. She understood that this young woman had loved their son for years and was now watching as a life-shattering revelation was completely tearing him apart. She understood how Gabi felt like this was the only thing she could do to try and find peace in the chaos. Maybe it would prove to be foolish, but admittedly, Rio just wanted to hear someone tell her their little boy was okay, no matter how big he'd grown.

"I am," the young woman replied as she tucked her hair behind her ear. The same hand jutted out, as if to offer a handshake uncertainly. Rio glanced at it for a moment and looked back up to the woman before her. 

"May I hug you instead?" she asked softly. When Gabi nodded, Rio pushed up from her chair and wrapped her in a firm embrace, holding her tightly. It made no sense to hug this complete stranger, but Rio was already so thankful for her that she didn't know what to do with herself. She was offering them the smallest glimpse of what they'd been missing for twenty-five years and as a result, it was simply... a lot. She felt the need to at least try to convey just what it meant to her.

Neither of them cried, thank God, but when Rio pulled away, she could see the faint shimmer of tears sitting on the younger woman's lids.

"Thank you, Gabi," Rio voiced softly, giving her shoulders a light squeeze before placing herself at the table and indicating for her to do the same. Once, seated, Rio couldn't help but to take a second and just... study.

She knew what Gabi looked like before she reached out because of the night her, Agatha, and Dani stayed up scouring the corners of the internet for any search of Nicky, but seeing her in person was far different.

She looked tired. She looked like beneath her thin layer of make-up, she'd done quite a bit of crying. She looked confused and worried, like she felt what she was doing by sitting there was somehow wrong. The way her hands shook on the table top made Rio ache; all she wanted was to reach out and place her own over them to try and calm her, but the hug had been enough as it was. 

The fact of the matter was that Rio did not know this woman. She knew only what she saw online, and what she had derived from the letter. She and Agatha spoke about it frequently and after Dani read it, she offered in her own perspective.

Clearly this woman loved their son. She loved him before all of this for seven long years. Who his parents were or what he was going through would never change that.

It was why they were there, wasn't it?

She wanted to see what he was not allowing himself to have for herself. to see what he could truly obtain if he would get out of his own way. The likelihood that she would disclose their meeting together was slim, but at least it might help her find some peace when he could not.

"It's... Really nice to meet you," Rio ventured softly, her soft honey gaze carefully tracing the features before her. "I know it isn't the ideal circumstances... And I can tell you half want to bolt out of here, but... It would me a lot to me -- all of us, our family -- if you would stay. Even if it's only a few minutes."

Under her studious watch, Gabi seemed to melt the tiniest bit. Her eyes glassed over again, but she did not cry; still, the mere sight made Rio's own prick with the threat of tears.

"I'm staying," the young woman returned. She was clearly trying to sound certain, but her voice cracked and her lip quivered just barely. 

"Okay," Rio soothed. "I didn't know what to order you, obviously. So... Maybe some tea first and we can talk once you've had a moment?" When Gabi gave a solemn nod, Rio raised a hand to flag the attention of the waitress, calling her over to collect Gabi's order. Once she disappeared, it seemed as though the other woman didn't so much care about having the tea first.

"I... I just want to say that I realize the conflict of morality here, but I feel..." She paused, her lips rubbing together as she fought back tears.

God, seeing her so emotional was not helping Rio keep her own composure in the least.

"I feel like there's not really an end in sight with him. This is... the worst I've ever seen him. He's supposed to go back to work at the beginning of the month, but I don't know how. He doesn't leave bed, rarely eats and rarely showers. His whole life... It's a lie to him and I think he just..." Gabi's voice trembled again and Rio made a choice. Maybe it was the wrong choice, but she made it all the same.

Gently, she reached across the small table between them and set both of her hands atop Gabi's, giving them a small squeeze. 

"I just think he doesn't know who he is. And it's killing him. If I thought I could get him out of bed, I'd help him get into therapy, or get back into running. But... He wants nothing to do with me."

Gabi's head dropped and she closed her eyes, leaving Rio pained to watch the fat tears as they rolled down her cheeks. 

This was fucking awful.

Sure, the three of them had been aching at the idea that their son might not want to know them, but Rio never stopped to think about what it was he had to be experiencing. Sure, it was easy to think about being told nothing you knew was actually right and how to handle it, but the harsh reality was that there was no knowing what it actually felt like without being having to go through it firsthand.

Nicholas was suffering and Gabi was doing what she possibly could to somehow make it better. Maybe it would only end up making it worse when she inevitably told him the truth, but for now, this was her way of doing something as opposed to doing nothing. 

"I don't think that's true," Rio tried to offer. Sure, she didn't know the first thing about them as individuals but the duration of their relationship spoke for itself. They'd been together since college. That was loud, that was important. "This is... For us, it's a potential happy ending. For him... I imagine it's like having every mirror smashed into pieces to a point where he doesn't know who is supposed to be looking back at him."

Rio paused, gingerly brushing her thumbs over the backs of Gabi's hands.

"The only person that can be the mirror of his true self, that can show him who is really is, is you. And you coming here to talk with me is a step in the right direction. I know you came here with the intention of telling me who he is, but even if you don't, I still think this is... It's a good start. It's good to just... see how you care about him. It tells me he has someone in his corner that won't tap out." Rio's tone was measured and soft, cognizant of how fragile the situation before he was, and the woman herself.

"I love him," Gabi admitted, her lip jutting out as she tried to stifle another sob. She pulled her hands from beneath Rio's wiping furiously at her face; it clearly wasn't the touch but rather the embarrassment of nearly sobbing in the middle of a cafe at 10 in the morning. "And I have zero clue how to help him."

"I know. And I'm afraid I don't have much advice in that regard because I... I don't actually know him. But it's so very apparent how much you love him, and that you would do anything to help him. So... Just know how much I, my wife, and our daughter appreciate you agreeing to this, let alone being the one to suggest it."

Rio's words were sincere but they were so impossibly heavy, something they were both aware of.

"I... I did my research, obviously," Gabi offered, wiping at her face once more in an attempt to dry it. "And from what I could see... You three just look like the family he deserved, the one that deserved him."

Something in Gabi's tone shot a chill right up Rio's spine. She wasn't being spiteful or mean about Wanda, but it made Rio think that maybe Nicky's life had not been as perfect as they were hoping it was.

"Was she... Was Wanda good to him?" Rio managed, licking her suddenly dry lips out of nervousness. 

Gabi just blinked at her, almost as if she'd forgotten who Wanda even was. It settled a moment later, action slipping back into her form.

"Alisa was... She wasn't bad to him."

Okay, Rio thought, but that's not implying she was good to him, either.

"But when she moved them around so much... It was really hard on him. He never got to have real friends or build long term relationships until college. She hovers always... Even right before all of this happened. It was for his birthday, but she picked a place to live close enough that she could have a good idea of what was going on with him."

Oh. So she was out of her mind and controlling? Good to know. Heartbreaking, and causing an ulcer in the pits of Rio's stomach, but still good to know.

"She was worried," Rio theorized aloud, not actually meaning to speak. 

"I think he sees that now. She... Never wanted him to be found."

The words smacked into Rio individually, one after another in the center of her chest. They hurt more and more with each impact, leaving her feeling as if she were choking on nothing. It had been Wanda's intent to hide him for the rest of their lives, to keep it all a secret from him. He was hers and she hadn't wanted to let him go.

Now, he was free.

And he was drowning without much to keep him afloat.

When the waitress arrived with Gabi's tea, both women thanked her softly before turning their attention upon one another once more.

"Okay, so," Gabi voiced after a slow sip of the hot liquid. In an instant, the warmth both filled and relaxed her, allowing to slump in her chair the slightest bit. "We did not come here for a tear fest, I am sure."

Oh. Rio liked her already.

"Better we got it out of the way first then, hm?" Rio offered as she lifted her mug of coffee for a drink of her own.

Gabi's expression was soft, her eyes tender as she became the one to truly look at Rio. What she said next almost shattered Rio to millions of very, very tiny pieces.

"He has your eyes. And your smile."

That hurt. It was meant to help, Rio knew, but it fucking hurt.

This woman who had looked at her son for the better part of a decade was telling her he looked like her. Surely, he looked like Agatha, too, as they knew, but hearing her voice such a thought out loud was almost enough to sink Rio herself.

Nicky was free.

Yet everyone seemed to be drowning.

"Admittedly, we did our own research. And... I'm of the opinion that he looks a lot like Agatha, but she said the same things you just did. So I can't really argue with you both."

The joint but soft laughter provided an air of warmth around the two of them, if only for a moment before they were staring back at one another.

Alright. It was time to put up or shut up. Gabi hadn't up and scrambled out, and the way she was talking insinuated she wanted to stay, so Rio slowly and cautiously trudged forward, offering the softest question.

"What does he like for breakfast?"

It could have seemed weird that of all the things in the world she could have asked, but the flash of tenderness in Gabi's eyes attested to her understanding. Rio wanted to take baby steps. She could ask things like his favorite breakfast or wha kind of music he listened to. She didn't want to push, didn't want to make Gabi feel as though she was violating his trust.

She just wanted to know who, after twenty-five years, her son had grown into.

"On the weekends, he likes when I make papas con chorizo y huevo. It's --"

Rio was grinning before she spoke. "I know what it is. It's one of my favorites. Agatha burned out on it ten years ago."

For a moment, there was quiet. The dull chatter of other occupants and the distant clinging of dishes could be heard, but the two women just watched one another, trying to figure out who was going to be brave enough to say something else.

Gabi beat Rio to the punch.

"You both... You really love each other, don't you?" she questioned gently, arm resting on the table as she fiddled with the handle of her mug. "I mean... You stayed together, he has a sister... You... You really held out hope this whole time?"

The question itself was loaded; there had been many nights when Agatha had shouted at her because she was so improbably angry and there had been just as many where Rio fell asleep on the floor because she was mad at Agatha but not enough to want to sleep in another room. They faced many, many struggles over the years but never once had Rio ever considered leaving. 

For every minute of raised blood pressure and every second of spit-fire anger, Rio still loved Agatha and always would.

So yes, Gabi was right.

"We do, and we have. I think..." Rio paused, her eyes finally tearing away from the young woman before her to stare into her coffee, the color of burnt caramel. "I think we've always known he was somewhere. We didn't know where, and we didn't know if we would ever know. But... You've been so close this whole time; Dani lives twenty minutes away on foot. And we never  would have known if it hadn't been for the DNA test."

There was the smallest ripple in Gabi's expression; guilt. The detective had loosely detailed how they obtained the sample, but as Rio looked into Gabi's eyes again, she saw nothing but self flagellation. She wasn't speaking, but her eyes had welled up and started to dart over Rio's face. 

"Hey, it's okay," she tried to soothe, though she knew better than to reach out again. "I take it you got it for him." It was a reasonable deduction, but the way Gabi's face folded even more while still not shedding another tear tore at something inside her.

"He just wanted to know about his second parent. She would never tell him. I..." Gabi drew in a slow breath through her nose, clearly trying to keep herself calm. "I thought he had a right to those answers. I just had no clue those answers would be... this. And... I'm still caught up on how I feel about it."

Rio knew she needed to be sensitive, to be gentle, and so she tried.

"Sometimes the answers we get are the ones we need, even if they aren't the ones we like. I just hate that it has to feel this way."

 

Agatha.

Kissing her wife and watching her slip out the front door, Agatha knew she needed to busy herself. She needed to find something to do to occupy her mind, mostly because the only thoughts that seemed to be in abundance were the ones demanding answers.

By ten-thirty that morning, she managed to clean both the living room and kitchen before making a mess of it again with far too many pancakes to count. When Dani turned up shortly before eleven looking like she hadn't slept a wink, she was more than happy to put a small dent in Agatha's hard work.

When she started deep cleaning ten minutes later by pulling out the stove, Dani called her out.

"What's wrong?" she asked flatly from her spot at the counter before shoving a bite of pancake in her mouth.

"Nothing," Agatha dismissed, waving her off.

"You're lying. You only deep clean when you're angry."

Sometimes, Agatha really hated how one of the traits Dani seemed to inherit from her was her perception level.

"I'm not angry," Agatha informed her though she did not bother lifting her head to look at her daughter.

"You're stewing, then," Dani corrected smugly.

"You're being annoying, Danica," Agatha clipped in warning.

With a soft huff from the counter, Dani finished the last bit of her breakfast and slid off the stool to rinse her plate off in the sink. Before she departed, she sidled up to her mother and placed a kiss to her cheek.

"It's going to be okay."

Dani sounded so fucking sure, but how? How could she be sure when Rio was at a cafe a half an hour away meeting with the only link in the world they had to their son? There were so many things she needed to know, so many questions that demanded answers. 

So how could Dani say it would be okay?

Weeks had passed and their son wasn't ready to enter their orbit. Maybe he never would be. Maybe he was his own man, with his own life, and would never want to know the love they still harbored for him.

Her Nicky.

Her sweet boy.

He was Nik.

And she didn't know the first thing about him.

But she still loved him, and so did Rio. Dani, for that matter.

"Say it enough times and I might start to believe you," Agatha murmured back, leaning into Dani's shoulders. In a flash, she felt her daughter's arm hook around her shoulders, pulling her closer. 

"It's going to be okay. I love you." She stole another rough peck to the side of Agatha's head and released, making her way to the stairs. "I'm gonna shower. We should go to the park later!"

Agatha didn't even want to dignify that with an answer so she offered a light laugh instead. 

Her mind was somewhere else entirely; she started thinking about questions and answers. Rio was surely going to get some, to gain some knowledge about their boy, but she wasn't going to get the right answers, not the ones to the tough questions.

No, there was only one way to get those.

Quickly and quietly, Agatha climbed the stairs to their bedroom and changed into daywear; a black blouse rolled at the sleeves and black trousers clung to her form, leaving her a shadow meant to darken any space she occupied, or at least the one she had in mind. After shaking her hair out and giving herself a look-over in the mirror, she collected her keys and phone and made her exit, climbing into her car a moment later.

She pulled up the GPS and typed in her destination with precision.

ESSEX COUNTY CORRECTIONAL FACILITY.

She would get her fucking answers one way or another.

 

Chapter End Notes

hi! welcome back.!
hope it was worth the wait.

Chapter 8: Weight in the Words Exchanged

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio.

Only twenty minutes passed and somehow, Rio felt as though she'd known Gabi for years. The way they conversed was easy, natural, and took little will to make it happen. It was soft-spoken and easy, a gentle balm to an intense situation.

Rio learned quite a few things over the course of those twenty minutes.

     1) Nicky's favorite color was hunter green. No other shade of green. Just that one.
     2) Nicky, like Agatha, had a terrible habit of picking at his fingernails.
     3) His favorite kind of music was pop-punk, but they loved going to raves together.
     4) Whenever it stormed, he sat in their picture window and watched it roll through (something Dani had done since she was little).
     5) His comfort food was noodles with butter and garlic.

The most painful one, though, was one Rio never anticipated.

     6) He had told Gabi many times throughout their time together that more than anything as a kid, he wanted to be a big brother.

He was a big brother. He had a beautiful little sister that thought of him all the time, that wished him a happy birthday and a good new year every single January 1st of every single year since she'd been old enough to understand the importance of the day.

"She thinks about him all of the time, even before this," Rio disclosed softly. "Sometimes, she'll see a silly t-shirt or hat and ask me if I think he'd wear something like that."

Before Rio could continue, Gabi cut her off with a soft laugh.

"Not out in public, but he has a mini-collection of terrible t-shirts. He has one he thinks is hilarious. It's got a cup of noodles on it and says 'Send Noods.' I'm still waiting for the teenage humor to wear off a little more." Gabi's voice was so soft, so tender as she disclosed Nicky's penchant for bad humor. Rio didn't say anything aloud, but she felt a kinship to the ability to laugh at the sillier things. 

Rio's humor was something she clung to for over twenty long years, something she used to protect herself when the world was so impossibly cruel. It was how she laughed off the bad nights, the long ones, and the ones where she wondered what life even actually meant anymore.

"He sounds like the type that reminds the world it's a better place when you can laugh."

Gabi's shoulders fell slightly and that gentle look returned to her eyes.

"You sound just like him, actually."

Rio marched into that cafe earlier that morning as a woman on a mission. As she sat before Gabi in those moments, she was simply a mother longing to know the amazing man she was being told about. Maybe he didn't know who he was right then, but the one person who did was trying to make his life easier, better, in any way she could. 

It was so painfully clear that Gabi loved him. Maybe they weren't married, maybe he had no plans of proposing, but that didn't seem to matter to the woman sitting at that table, battling her nerves and her morality for the sake of trying to soothe what and who was capable of being soothed. If it wasn't him, it could be Rio instead.

Her plan in writing that letter, it was working.

It wasn't as good as what it could be to have him be the one to pen her and show up, but it was the next best thing. Maybe, Rio thought, it was even better because she was not getting his own -- possibly misguided -- view of himself. She was getting the view of him from the person who saw him day in and day out, who had fallen head over heels in love with him. Sure, maybe Gabi wasn't telling her pivotal things, but Rio didn't expect her to. They'd just met and while she was being entirely forthcoming, Gabi was still treating it cautiously, gauging where to steer the conversation.

Gabi was young, yes, but the handle she seemed to have on life and on the rather jarring situation they all found themselves in impressed Rio beyond measure. Sure, she shed her tears, but they were both guilty of that. Overall, it was simply good to see how supportive she was of Nicky -- Nik as she called him -- and comforting in its own right.

That time, the tears welled in Rio's eyes at the comparison, but she was quick to blink them back.

"I..." Gabi began, clearly catching the blunder. "I can stop doing that. Comparing him to you, I mean... If it upsets you."

God, Rio thought, this woman is too fucking sweet for her own good.

She shook her head in a gentle dismissal, a sad smile tugging on her lips.

"No, no. Please don't actually. It's just... Really strange to hear that we can be similar when we... We've never really known each other." It was her truth, something she had come to realize in their time at that table, but that was changing. Maybe she didn't know him, exactly, but she knew what the person who knew him best thought of him.

Still, there were more questions to be asked.

"If you're sure," Gabi offered softly to which Rio only nodded. 

She liked hearing it, even if it hurt.

"Can I ask you more things about him? Am I keeping you from anything?" 

In the same way the young woman before her was showing endless compassion, Rio was just the same. She was infinitely thankful that Gabi was willing to give her so much, but she also did not want to cause any strain on her life otherwise.

"No, not keeping me. I plan to grab groceries on the way home, but I..." She faltered for just a moment, very obviously stopping herself from saying something that might have come across as a little cold. She cleared her throat and rephrased before she finally voiced it aloud. "I don't think he will be out of bed enough to tell how long I've been gone."

It was a sad reality, but one Rio hoped they could change soon. Somehow, someway, it needed to change.

"What was he like in college?"

Gabi considered for a moment, an affectionate gleam flashing across dark eyes. The smallest smile curled her lips before she answered.

"Silly. Charming. We... We tried to be friends first, just because we had a lot on our plates with our course loads. But he... He would show up when I was awake at midnight studying with my favorite take out to help me power through. He'd stay on the phone with me when he couldn't be there in person. Even the first time he kissed me, we were just supposed to be enjoying a friendly walk but he couldn't keep it in. He offered me the chance to forget it and apologized profusely. The only way I could get him to stop was to kiss him again."

Her eyes sparkled and the smile on her face grew at recalling the memory, almost as if she was reliving it all over again.

The two of them had been young, still in their first year of college, and it was clear even back then, Nicky had a soft heart. He was chivalrous and caring, kind but also smart enough to go after the things he wanted in life.

"You said it about Agatha and I, but... I'd like to return the favor. I can tell that you really love him just by the way you speak about him. And... I can tell he loves you, too, even if he's not great at showing it with everything going on."

"I do know that," Gabi conceded, tipping her head to look into her tea. "And that's why I won't leave. It's why I won't give up on him. Because yes, a lot of his world has been turned upside-down and he doesn't know what's real and what's not. But I am. And I don't want him to lose the one thing he can be certain of."

Rio gave a nod of understanding, thin fingers pressing into the ceramic of her coffee cup. For a moment, her lips twisted slightly and she braved another question.

"Does his work make him happy?"

The way Gabi softened each time Rio asked a genuine question that was not a baseline of 'how-to-get-to-know-someone-101,' it struck something within her. Maybe Gabi had built expectations of this meeting in her head prior to showing up, but it appeared as though Rio was countering every possible scenario she'd cooked up with finesse and ease.

"It does. Which... I'm hoping we can get him to the point where he's ready to go back. I think it will be good for him. He's... A social butterfly. He feeds off of learning and growing, and he says the best way to do that is to listen to what other people have to say."

The more Gabi disclosed, the more Rio could feel her heart squeezing in her chest. Her boy, her sweet boy who chose the path of a healer and loved speaking with others. Her kind young man who gave a shit about the world and how it operated and only wanted to fill it with compassion and laughter.

Maybe she and Agatha had not been given the privilege of raising him, but it still seemed as though he'd found his way anyway.

"Can I ask something... A little more loaded?" Rio questioned, her gaze dropping to the table. She knew she shouldn't press any harder, but there was something she needed to know.

Gabi studied her long and hard, trying to gauge whether or not it was going to be a question she was capable of answering. After what felt like an eternity, she nodded her head.

"Did he... Did he love her? As his mom, did he love Wanda?"

It was irrational and Rio knew better, but she couldn't stop herself. There had been countless days where they had loved him without him ever knowing who they were. Something in Rio simply needed to know whether or not Wanda had been good enough to him to earn that type of emotion.

Gabi shifted slightly in her seat, leaning forward with her elbows on the table as a call for Rio's attention. When their gazes locked, she offered a kind smile, one that soothed Rio far more than it should have.

"I think he felt obligated to love her. But she... She made his life very hard. And... He resented her for it, even if he continued to entertain her after he moved away. All Nik ever needed was... support. Companionship. And she ensured he never got it until he was an adult."

Even though it shouldn't have, it felt like a small victory. She took a steadying breath, doing what she could to not let it show on her face. Wanda took him, deprived him of having the love Agatha and Rio both wanted to pour into him and instead of being some super-parent or someone who gave 'their' child everything they needed, Wanda had failed him.

It felt wrong to be happy about that, especially given what Nicky was currently going through, but Rio couldn't help it.

They would have been better for him. There was no questioning it.

There was also no changing it.

"Can I ask you one last thing?" Rio beguiled quietly, nibbling on the inside of her lower lip immediately.

Gabi again nodded, clearly willing to answer anything at that point.

"Do you think there's hope for us?"

For a split second, Gabi froze in place. Her chest stopped moving, her eyes locked onto Rio and not even a strand of hair was rustled by the vent over her head. She thought it over, clearly gave it consideration and after a breath, relaxed and offered her answer.

"I do," she returned in earnest. "But I can't promise a day. I can't say 'Oh, on this Tuesday in June, he's suddenly going to be okay enough to meet." While it was blunt, Rio understood it. There was no timeline on the grief and devastation he had to be feeling and putting him on one was absolutely unfair. Still, hearing there was some hope as opposed to none, that meant something. "But I think... I think once the pain starts to fade, he will find enough objectivity to understand what he's missing out on."

Rio's lips parted to speak, but Gabi wasn't finished.

"Because from what I can tell... He is missing out. You haven't talked so much about yourself or Agatha, but... I see that look in your eyes every time you learn something new about him. You love him. Never stopped since he was a baby, even if you don't know who he is now." That time, Gabi was the one to reach across the table, covering Rio's hands with her own. 

"He is a good man. And once he can work through some of this trauma, I know he will prove that to you."

She was being so sincere that it almost hurt Rio to hear the blind hope in her voice. She told Rio it was there, but she seemed to convinced. 

Softly, Rio's thumbs rubbed at the backs of her hands.

"He already has."

 

Agatha.

Breathe, idiot.

Breathing was important, yes, and it would likely help temper the crimson blush that formed on Agatha's cheeks in the twenty minutes it took her to reach the county jail. The truth was, the closer she got, the more angry she became. Maybe she had been stewing before, but the longer she was alone with her thoughts and the idea of being mere feet from the woman who had robbed them of a lifetime with their son, the more enraged she became.

She could ask herself all the questions she wanted -- who did Wanda think she was? What the fuck was wrong with her? How could she do this to them when they had only shown her kindness -- but it didn't matter. 

Agatha would never have those answers until she could ask Wanda herself.

As she was pulling into a spot in the visitor's lot, her phone dinged from its holder on the dashboard.

Incoming Message From: Boog.

Alright, perhaps she should have left some kind of note. That became more apparent when she opened the message itself.

Boog: Momma? Where did you go? Are
you okay? What happened? Is mom
okay?

Shit.

Agatha had been too caught up in her own thoughts to think clearly in the moment; she snuck out to avoid Dani's interrogation, but she forgot to shoot a text to let her know nothing was on fire.

Me: Everything is fine, Danica. I just
ran an errand. Mom is still having 
coffee with Gabi as far as I know. I
will be back ASAP. Promise. I love 
you.

Was it a shit move to lie to your kid when such heavy things were going on? Probably, but Agatha didn't have the time to sit in that parking lot and argue with her daughter about the questionable decisions she was choosing to make.

In her defense, she'd done nothing but wait. It had been a topic of conversation between herself and Rio and they agreed she deserved to go and say what she had to say, but they hadn't settled on a right time. 

Agatha was tired of waiting to settle.

She wanted action.

As she climbed out of the car, her phone dinged in her hand again and she glanced down to read Dani's response.

Boog: Okay. I love you too.

Agatha knew she was upset; Dani didn't like being left in the dark and she was smart enough to recognize when it was happening. She had long since picked up on the tells her mothers had, the things that gave them away, and she knew if Agatha had slipped out without a word, it was for a reason.

But this was something Agatha needed to do and she did not need anyone, her daughter included, trying to stop her.

Once inside, she went through the process of checking in, declaring who she was there to see, and being told where to sit as she waited. As she crossed her legs at the knee to bide her time, she began to subconsciously pick at her cuticles, not even noticing when the one on her ring finger pinched and stung, a thin line of blood cracking through pale skin.

When she glanced down a moment later, the blood had seeped into her nailbed. 

Ah, who cared. She didn't feel it anyway.

Checking her phone one last time, Agatha's head whipped up as she was called.

"Harkness-Vidal for Maximoff," the security officer voiced, his bright green eyes scanning the room. His hair was dark, jaw chiseled and strong. In a way, he almost looked like Nicky, but Agatha knew that was her anxiety-ridden mind looking for traces of her son anywhere she could find them.

She gave a nod and pushed to her feet, quiet and boiling as she followed along behind him, her eyes scanning over her surroundings and the cubicles they passed by until he indicated the one she would be occupying. When she took her seat upon the cold metal chair, there was about three solid inches of plexiglass before her and a phone wired into the wall on her right.

Agatha hadn't ever been in a prison, not to visit or for any other reason, but it didn't feel like a prison for her right then.

It felt like a fighting cage.

Maybe she wasn't going to physically be able to get her hands on Wanda, but she was almost certain she had enough to say that would make her feel even worse. Agatha's tongue was sharp, and her mind was vast and filled with too many pointed thoughts to not use them as weapons against the woman who ruined her life and the lives of her family.

Everyone under their roof had mostly kept their cool. Rio cried sometimes and Dani asked to be left alone, but over all, they came together to push forward. Agatha, most of all, wore a placid exterior around her loved ones, but she never stopped thinking.

She always thought of what Wanda could have been doing for two and a half decades with their son. She thought about him, his relationship, how he had someone who loved him enough to reach out to a family he was probably terrified of. She thought about Wanda's motives, her reasoning. She thought about how unfair it was how it all played out.

Wanda could have talked to them, could have asked for help. Sure, she had still been new to their world, but they would have still tried to help improve her life in any way they could. They trusted her enough to leave her alone with their son.

And she hadn't just broken that trust, she'd used every shard to stab them for twenty-five excruciating years.

Agatha merely heard a door on the other side of the room click open and in she shuffled, guided by a security guard a good foot taller than she was.

Wanda Fucking Maximoff.

He placed her carefully in the seat and leaned over her, clicking her cuffs into place on a metal loop in front of her. Once secure, he unlocked the one on her left side so she would have access to the phone. The only thing was, when he walked away, she didn't reach for it.

No, those piercing green eyes just stared right back at Agatha.

Wanda looked defiant, like she did not want to be sitting there, even entertaining the idea of picking up that phone to let Agatha say her peace.

But that was her right.

Wanda seemed to know it as Agatha stared right back at her, teeth grinding as she clenched her jaw. 

Slowly, Wanda raised a thin and bony hand, plucking the phone from its cradle on the wall. Following suit, Agatha did the same, though she used a little more force. Once both phones were pressed to an ear, the staring match resumed.

Agatha had given this moment a lot of thought. She thought about screaming, about yelling, about telling Wanda to fuck all the way off the face of the planet. Every single thought possible about that moment had crossed her mind and yet, she did none of those things. Instead, she calmly pressed her lips together, never once diverting her blue gaze as it burned hot with her ire.

"Why?"

It was the only word that left her lips, but it barely phased the woman on the other side of the glass. Wanda merely blinked at her, almost as if she did not understand the question. She wasn't under sedation, didn't have to be dulled by drugs and yet, she looked completely dumbstruck at such a question.

The longer the silence wore on over the line, the more Agatha's blood started to boil.

She was there!

She was right fucking there!

And somehow, she still couldn't get the answers she ached for.

"Tell me, Wanda. Tell me why you fucking did it." It was gruff and low, a snarl in the shape of a demand.

Again, silence.

Again, Agatha's blood was boiling so hot it showed in the flush of every visible inch of skin.

"Fucking tell me!" she roared, leaning forward so quickly she almost slammed her face against the glass but stopped an inch short. She was tired of the bullshit, tired of the hiding and silence and not knowing.

"What do you want to hear, Agatha?" Wanda asked coldly, her Slavic accent a little heavier than Agatha remembered from all those years ago. It was probably something she used for cover that she was not immediately able to slip out of. 

"The fucking truth, you bitch," Agatha clipped back in a growl. "I want to hear why you ruined our fucking lives, the life of our son for twenty-five fucking years."

At such a statement, Wanda actually looked offended.

What fucking right did she have to be OFFENDED?

Agatha was ready to launch the phone in her hand right through the plexiglass in front of her.

"I did not ruin his life," Wanda countered sharply, her brow knitting tightly. "I gave him the best life I c--"

"You did! You ruined any fucking chance he had at knowing the two people who loved him more than you ever could! You deprived him of any chance he had to know us, to know his sister. We are his parents, no matter how long you hid him from us!" The side of the room around her had grown quiet, the other occupants all stilling enough to let the conversation she was having with Wanda have the air it needed to breathe.

Agatha should have been embarrassed.

She was too fucking pissed off for that.

"Just fucking give me an answer, Wanda!"

The primary emotion Agatha was aiming for was rage, but the way her voice cracked betrayed her as desperate for the reality and not what she could concoct in her own head.

As she watched, steeled and seething, Wanda leaned back as much as she was able with one wrist cuffed to the table and considered her reply. When they had first interviewed her, she never once came across as cold or calculating, but what she'd done could have been considered little else.

All Agatha wanted to know was why.

"Two months before you hired me," Wanda voiced through the phone, her chilling demeanor never fading, "I found out I could not have children. I thought it would be enough to be around them, to help me get over it. But... Nicky... He deserved better than two mothers who left their son at home with a stranger and worked countless hours. He deserved... He deserved attention and love and --"

"Fuck you," Agatha hissed into the mouthpiece, though it was a threat. "Fuck you, Wanda. We hired you because we thought you wanted to help us, not steal our fucking baby."

Agatha wanted to put her fucking chair through the glass and vault over that counter so damn bad it physically hurt. She wanted to punch Wanda, to choke her within and inch of her life and force her to make it right.

But it wouldn't have accomplished anything.

"He's a good b--"

"I don't care! I don't give a shit what you think about my son, Wanda. Because whoever he became, I highly doubt it was because of anything good you did for him. And now --"

"Aga --"

"No! You listen!" Agatha nearly shouter over her. "And now, he's suffering. He has to be. He won't speak to us, which is fine. But did you ever, for one fucking second think about what this would do to him once he found out the truth!? No! Because you're selfish! You don't actually give a single fuck about him, or you would have told him long before now and let the choice be his."

Agatha drew in a sharp breath, her anger inducing a mild light-headedness that she fought to push away. She had to remain upright; she wasn't done giving Wanda hell just yet.

"You know what? It's clear you're not going to be forthcoming or explain what the fuck's been going through that empty head of yours for a quarter of a lifetime, so you will hear me."

For just a moment, Agatha thought Wanda was going to hang up the phone. It was the tiniest twitch in her arm that was about to ignite Agatha's last fuse, but she did not follow through and instead held it in place.

"I cannot stop him from ever coming here to see you because I am a stranger to him. But so help me god, if he turns up here and you aren't fucking honest with him and you don't tell him that we have missed him every fucking day since he's been gone, I will do absolutely anything and everything in my power to see that your existence is every bit as miserable as you've made ours for far too fucking long. That is not threat. That's a goddamn guarantee."

Agatha was not screaming, she was not spitting the words into the phone. No, her voice was measured and cold, like a blade. She was offering a warning, one that Wanda would be wise to heed.

"You have caused him enough pain. You need to let him go."

Wanda did not speak, did not offer any kind of return. For the longest time, the two of them simply stared one another down, lips twitching on both sides of the glass in a fight to say something but neither woman found their words.

Instead, Wanda simply gave a nod and hung up the phone, leaning back to snag the attention of the security guard.

"No! I'm not finished!" Agatha shouted, but no one on the other side of the glass was listening. "Wanda! Wanda, no! Pick up the fucking phone! NO!" To punctuate her last word, a heavy hand smack loudly and cleanly to the glass, trying to bring her back but it was of no use. The security guard unlocked her cuffs from the table and lifted her to her feet, walking her away without another word spoken.

"FUCK!"

It was the loudest she'd said the word within the walls of the jail, but it wasn't the last time she said it that day.

 

Nikolai.

In all honesty, Nik had lost track of the days. He knew it was the weekend, given Gabi hadn't gone to work two days in a row, but he had no clue just how many had passed since his world had been turned on its head.

What he did know was that he was getting nowhere by just lying in bed.

It felt good, felt like the right thing to do, mostly because he could not think of how to function otherwise, but he knew that somehow, he had to move on.

How could he when he didn't know who he actually was?

Everything Alisa instilled in him, everything she'd taught him over the years was a projection of her fear and uncertainty. She'd driven home a strong sense of paranoia for much of his childhood, and finally understanding why felt like an absolute gut-punch. She'd only ever been looking out for herself; that much had become painfully clear.

So where did it leave him?

Right then, it left him wrapped up in blankets in a bed his long term girlfriend had not slept in in weeks because he couldn't bear the thought of being close to her.

He'd barely eaten and the last time he showered was probably the week before.

It would be so fucking easy to do more of the same, more of just laying around and ruminating on his own misery, but nothing worthwhile was ever fucking easy, was it?

By 11am when Gabi was still out and about, Nik had come to a conclusion.

His life was never going to be the same. That was a fact. But, if he could maybe understand why, it might help him rebuild with what he had left. It wasn't a promise he could make to himself, but he knew where he had to start, even if the thought made him want to vomit.

He had to talk to Wanda.

So, by 12:30 with Gabi still absent, Nik had managed to dress himself -- terribly in joggers and a too-large sweatshirt -- and shove down a few crackers in an attempt to settle his stomach. Feeling a small pool of resolve beginning to well within him, he caught the first train to Newark and drowned most of the trip out with heavy metal in his headphones as he travelled.

Climbing out of the Uber that rolled to a stop in front of the Essex County Jail, he had no idea what awaited him within those walls, but he was tired of waiting to find out.

He climbed the stairs and passed through the front doors, knowing he needed to check in first. As he headed through the lobby, his eyes lifted to take in the sight of a woman storming out from the back, her cheeks pure scarlet and her outfit black from head to toe. Her wild sandy brown hair with grey roots blew haphazardly behind her and she was clearly angry with whatever had just transpired.

And then Nik saw her eyes.

They connected with his as the woman went to blow by him and something in him knew who she was. He'd seen her photos on google, had read up on her prestigious career in neuroscience. 

He was staring into the eyes of Agatha Harkness-Vidal, his mother.

And he chose not to say a word.

If she recognized him, she did too.

As she exited the lobby and made her way outside, Nik was almost too fucking thankful for it.

Before she made it, he heard the soft "Fuck" as it fell from her lips.

 

Chapter End Notes

Hi so please don't think I'm back in my prime but. This story has been chattering in the noggin and is wanting me to tell it again. I can't promise updates regularly, but I will be getting to this when the brain allows. Thank you so much for all the positive words on the last chapter, it means so so so much to me even if I don't always know what to say. Thank you again!

Chapter 9: All I See Scares Me

Chapter Notes

me yesterday: I'm not back on my bullshit just yet guys
me today: *tyler the creator that was a fucking lie gif*

Agatha.

Fuck. Fuck. FUCK. FUCK!

The moment Agatha pushed her way through the glass front doors of the jail, something in her completely snapped. There was not a singular thought racing through her brain outside of her need to get to her car.

In a dead sprint, she tore across the lot and spotted her destination, but as she reached it, she bypassed the car completely to throw up just on the other side of the trunk, vomit splattering haphazardly on the pavement at her feet.

No. No no no no no. No fucking way.

When Agatha first arrived, she'd sworn to herself that she was just looking for Nicky in other people. When she was leaving, she hadn't been looking, but she spotted him anyway. It wasn't just picking out some of his features on the young man that looked like he hadn't slept in days, it was him.

Agatha spent hours pouring over those online photos, even though she knew she shouldn't. Fixating would never solve their problems, but just seeing his face on a screen was enough to offer her some modicum of hope to hold onto. It was something that tethered her to the reality where he was still alive, even if she might never get to know him. Him being alive, even after all that time, was the most important thing.

Seeing him in the flesh hit her in every way imaginable, pain ripping throughout every inch of her being. It was an ache, a pull, and absolute burning need to simply reach out to him and wrap him in her arms.

But they were strangers.

He didn't know her.

And she didn't know him.

Breaching his sense of safety in those moments was simply not an option.

For as selfish as Agatha wanted to be in those fleeting seconds, she couldn't do it. She couldn't put her own needs above her son's no matter how severe the pain was upon seeing him. She wanted him in her life.

The way to get him there was not to assert herself into his.

By the time her retching stopped, Agatha knew she needed to get home. She had zero fucking clue how she was going to manage as much with her hands shaking so violently, but she needed to. She needed to get in the car, drink some of the water in the cupholder, drive herself to the house, paint on the best damn facade she could manage to stave off any unwanted inquiries from Dani, and collapse into her big bed until her wife inevitably came home.

She needed to do all of things, and she did start the process, but as she recapped the water bottle, Agatha could do none of them as her eyes began to fill and overflow with tears. They were hot and fast as they poured down her cheeks and both hands raised to slam against the steering wheel.

How had this happened?

How had her life gotten this far away from her?

The answer, in her mind, was simple, really.

She'd been stupid enough to trust someone.

Not leaving Dani alone throughout her child only asserted such a fact to her, a proof that they and they alone were the only people who could protect their child. Being stupid enough to think anyone in the world had good intentions burned them once; neither herself nor Rio would ever let it happen again. Sure, Dani was grown now and the rules were different, but the mission remained the same.

Protect at all costs.

But with Nicky right fucking there Agatha could not protect him in the least. She could not save him, could not take away his pain, could not tell him everything would be okay.

It wasn't her place.

But, with him walking in to most likely see Wanda, Agatha realized that he actually had no one in that place in his life.

The only person that might have been able to do those things was currently sitting with Agatha's wife in a cafe a good twenty minutes away. Considering, it seemed as though she reached out because he was not allowing even that.

It was fucked, to put it plainly.

Every single bit of what had happened to them was t-totally fucked and there was never going to be any repairing it without extensive amounts of time. But Agatha didn't want time. She wanted her son. 

She wanted to march back into that jail, hand over a business card, and march right back out.

But she couldn't.

No matter how deeply she yearned for it to be her reality, her muscles knew better. She was immobile, stuck in her car in the parking lot while sad sobs squeaked out of her and tears streamed helplessly down her cheeks. She knew, in those long and excruciating moments, that she loved her son more than could ever possibly make sense. Because of that, she was not going to make his life any harder.

With several steadying breaths, Agatha pressed the button on the dash and started the car, taking her time in making it back to the house by slinking around backroads until she found herself ready enough to face the scrutiny of her daughter. 

As predicted, Dani was seated in the lounger in the front room, head head snapping to attention as Agatha breezed through the door and closed it behind her. Before she even finished slipping her shoes off, her daughter was on the offensive, leaping to her feet and meeting her where she stood.

"Is everything okay?" It was the same thing she asked in the text, and it was the second time Agatha was going to have to lie to her.

She wanted to scream it, to sob it: I saw your brother!

What good would it have done? What would it have accomplished?

"Everything's fine. Just had to run to the hospital to sign something I forgot about."

God.

Even as it left her lips, Agatha fucking hated lying to Dani. It was necessary, she told herself, simply because things were so fragile. It hurt her to experience it; she couldn't fathom the idea of telling her daughter and watching whatever emotions wrote themselves on her face as she imagined what it must have felt like. Things were a fucking struggle as it was; adding more onto Dani's plate when she seemed to be the only one truly holding it together just felt cruel.

"Momma," Dani deadpanned, staring down at Agatha with a blank expression on her face.

Fuck if Agatha didn't want to crack.

She couldn't. She just couldn't. Not until Rio came home with hopefully better news than what she had dragged in with her.

"Danica, baby," Agatha soothed, reaching up to cup one of Dani's cheeks in her palm. "I'm okay. I promise. But I'm pretty tired, so I think I'm going to lay down for a bit. Tell mom it's okay to wake me up when she gets back. I want to hear all about it."

The look in Dani's eyes all but shouted her doubt. She knew, looking right into Agatha, she was being lied to. She knew Agatha was hiding something from her and for the briefest moment, Agatha was almost convinced she would keep fighting her on it.

Thankfully, she did not.

Instead, she slipped out of the light hold and stepped forward, wrapping her arms tightly around Agatha's neck. For the tenth time that day, Agatha almost shattered. 

Her little spat with Wanda hadn't gone anywhere, really, other than a promise that she was thankful she'd made, even retroactively. With her saying as much and Nicky walking in right as she was walking out? Hopefully, the sound of her hard and cutting voice was still fresh in Wanda's mind enough to make her heed the warning.

But Agatha wouldn't know. She might never know. 

All she knew was Nicky had walked in there to sit across from Wanda and that conversation was something she would never be privy to. And somehow, uselessly, she stood in the foyer of her own home wrapped in the arms of her beautiful and emotionally intelligent twenty-one year old who kept promising everything was going to be alright. 

Agatha wanted to believe her.

But wanting something and being able to do it were two completely different things.

"I love you, kiddo," Agatha murmured softly, nuzzling a little into the side of Dani's head as she clung a little tighter than she meant to.

"I know," Dani managed in a croak. "But if you squeeze me any harder, you're gonna break a rib."

With a soft chuckle, Agatha's hold loosened and she took a step back, holding her daughter at arm's length to get a good look at her.

Dani was... She was the best of them.

She was the resolute one, the one who seemed to be soldiering on and shouldering the weight of everyone else's grief. It wasn't a fair position for her to be in by any means, but Agatha was trying to find recovery enough to lift some of her burden. She was being so strong, being so steadfast, and she was the youngest of the three of them.

Agatha understood it, in some ways; for Dani, she'd never had the chance to meet her brother. She hadn't touched him or held him or heard his soft giggle, not the way Agatha and Rio once did. She knew who he was, knew what he symbolized, and knew that what happened to him had ripped holes in her parents, ones likely to never heal.

Then, the hope peeked over the horizon. 

He wasn't just some story to Dani, not anymore. He was a real, grown man who had been living scarily close to her own apartment in the city, a mere cab ride away. He was someone that looked like her, someone she had always tried to picture but always fell short.

It might have seemed so easy for her to take it all as it came, but Agatha knew the truth about her daughter and how she worked. Dani would take it all on and do so out of the pureness of her own heart for as long as she could.

When she inevitably returned home, that was when she would fall apart.

Agatha hated Dani's way of dealing with things, mostly because she knew she actively hid her anguish sometimes, but she also respected it. She had to, didn't she?

It was exactly what she was doing right then.

"You are my sunshine," Agatha told her.

In response, a warm and genuine smile filled Dani's face, even if it did not quite touch her eyes.

"My only sunshine, momma. Go, take your nap. I'll be in the basement."

It was a concession, but Agatha read it for what it was. As much as she needed the time to process her time out of the house, Dani needed her alone time, too. It was clear she knew there was more going on than Agatha dared to tell her, but -- much like Agatha had with Nicky -- seemed to understand the time for pushing on those sore spots hadn't quite arrived.

"Will do. Wake me up if you need anything. I love you." She placed a kiss to Dani's cheek and gave her arm a soft squeeze before heading up the stairs and down the hall to the bedroom. Once inside, she closed the door most of the way and stripped out of her blouse and jeans, trading them in for a pair of boxer shorts and a loose t-shirt, though she paid no mind to what shirt it actually was.

Although she was aware it would likely not be much longer, Agatha had really been hoping for the sight of her wife when she walked in the door. She could have texted Rio to see where she was, but the thought completely slipped her mind upon seeing their boy. It was something she likely would have done, had that not happened.

So instead of bothering her while presumably still out with Gabi, Agatha crawled into bed and grabbed for one of Rio's pillows, hugging it tightly to her chest as she buried her face into it.

And then, she let herself really cry.

 

Rio.

When Rio illuminated her phone to check the time and for any messages she might have missed in her attention to all Gabi had to tell her, the last thing she expected was for it to be almost one in the afternoon.

They'd been posted at that cafe for almost three and a half hours, just... talking.

Although she received far more than she could have ever hoped for about Nicky, realizing their meeting needed to come to an end hit Rio like a stack of bricks being swung around in a pillowcase, right in the stomach.

"I didn't realize how late it was," she voiced, lifting her head to take a look at the woman across from her, checking her phone as well. 

"Oh shit. I really should go --"

"No, no. I know. it's okay. I guess we just... Lost track of time." It was an honest sentiment, but Rio bit back the part where she wanted to ask for more of it. She wanted to ask if they could meet again, if they could talk more but she realized what she had in her hands now, it was still a gift. It was way more than she had when she walked through those doors and posted herself at that little corner both.

"I..." Gabi started, her eyes dropping into her empty mug. "I can't promise that I can do this again. And I can't say that I think keeping in active contact would be the best idea, but..."

Rio knew she was right, even if she hated it.

However, there was a very obvious 'but' tacked onto the end of her words.

"But?" she parroted quietly, hopeful.

"But if anything changes, or things get worse... I promise I will let you know. I..." Gabi stopped, her lips worrying against one another for a moment in thought. "It's not my goal to betray him, and I don't ever want him to get that idea. I just... You clearly love him. You deserved to have something of him to hold onto, even if it's just my perception of the amazing man he is."

Of course Rio wished it could be more, but Gabi had given her a gift. Hell, she'd given all three of them a gift. They could theorize and hypothesize all day long about what his life was like, who he had become in the years of his absence, but nothing they could have concocted would have been anywhere close to the truth.

The truth was, he was a gentle soul. He chatted up strangers for fun because he liked it when they smiled. He donated hundreds of dollars worth of toys at Christmastime. He volunteered twice a month at the local shelter serving meals. He loved his girlfriend when his life wasn't falling apart. He had a good life, was a good person.

Now, he was just hurting.

"I can't tell you what it means to all three of us, truly," Rio offered as she pushed off the table and onto her feet. "If it's okay, I'd like to hug you again before we leave."

The look on Gabi's face went from resolved to broken in the blink of an eye.

It was clear she hadn't been entirely sure of what their meeting would bring, but she was now staring at the reality of what it did for Rio. It did give her hope. It did make her feel like there could come a day when their son decided he wanted them to be a part of his life. There was no definitive date, no way of actually knowing, but the possibility still dangled in front of her like a victory just out of reach.

Without a word, the younger woman stepped forward and wrapped Rio in her arms, hugging her tightly. In some ways, it almost felt like the kind of strong and warming hug Dani would give, but in others, Rio could feel as Gabi clung to her for those last few seconds just how desperate for a resolution she truly was.

They all wanted a happy ending, an ending where Nicholas -- Nikolai, whatever name he chose -- was able to accept his past and embrace what future they could give him.

Nicky had four women who loved him impossibly so, even if he'd never met three of them. The one he knew, she was doing everything she could to facilitate something better, something more than what they were all currently stuck with solely because she loved him and could see what he would not allow himself to have with an objective perspective.

As Rio pulled back, she pulled her bag over her shoulder and turned to the woman before her, offering the kindest smile she could muster.

"Thank you, Gabi. Seriously. What you did... It took guts. But... You've offered me so, so much of him. And I..." Her lip quivered and her eyes stung with tears she did not cry and instead wiped off her lids with a quick thumb. "Anything you need, please do reach out. We are always here for you, whatever you need."

Maybe it was stupid; Rio knew she shouldn't make such promises, but how could she not? How could she not at least try to give something back to someone who had given her so much?

"Thank you, too. I... I think I needed this to remind myself that everything's going to be alright, some day."

The way she said those last two words, Rio felt them very acutely in her chest. It was sharp and it stung, but she knew Gabi was right.

All their lives were, at that point, was one giant waiting game.

Every single one of them had no choice but to play it.

"Some day," she echoed sadly, though the ghost of a smile played at her lips. "Until that day, you have my number. Have a good rest of your day, sweetheart." Rio gave her one last soft pat to the shoulder before Gabi offered a nod and made her exit. For the longest moment, Rio simply stood in place with one hand clutching at the strap of her bag as she watched her disappear into the throngs of foot traffic on the busy city sidewalk.

After a beat too long, she finally remembered where she was and where she had to go; home. She needed to see Agatha, to hold her as she relayed every bit of information Gabi had bestowed upon her.

It was a blessing, one she couldn't wait to share.

When she arrived home, then, to the sound of violin coming from the basement and neither her wife nor daughter present, something didn't feel right.

It wasn't so much that Rio cared whether or not anyone was there to welcome her home, but to know Dani was diving into music and Agatha was like hiding in their bedroom, that felt...

Ominous.

Shedding her shoes before taking the stairs slowly two at a time, Rio was a little uneasy as she nudged the bedroom door open to find Agatha lying on the bed, her back to the door, and a pillow clutched to her chest.

And she was shaking.

Fuck.

What could have happened in four hours to leave Agatha Harkness-Vidal -- of all people -- in a crying heap in the middle of the day?

Without a word, Rio shed her shirt and jeans, climbing easily beneath the comforter atop the bed to slide in behind her wife, a strong arm hooking around her from behind in a tight embrace.

"My love," Rio breathed softly in alarm, her forehead creased with her worry. "What's going on?"

When Agatha did nothing but start to cry harder, what was concern slowly began to twist into panic.

What the fuck had done this to her?

With a careful hand, Rio reached up to move some of Agatha's hair away from her face, leaning over her to kiss at wet cheeks. This had happened very seldom throughout the course of their relationship and as such, Rio knew something had happened, something severe that pushed her to this point.

"Breathe, baby," Rio requested, kissing more of the wet skin on Agatha's face. "I need you to breathe and tell me what's gotten you so upset." She knew with the state Agatha was in, it was a big ask, but she couldn't help if she had no clue where to begin.

God damnit. Everyone was falling apart left and right.

How were any of them going to stay afloat at this rate?

It took a few additional minutes of coaxing and another good twenty light kisses, but eventually Agatha's breathing slowed and her sniffling decreased as a partial sense of calm settled into her. Rio never let go, never stopped showering her in gentle and quiet love to help her get to the other side of her struggle.

"Can you tell me what happened, Agatha?" Rio requested in a whisper into the back of Agatha's neck as she settled on the pillow beneath her.

"Rio, I..." she began, but her voice broke and shattered, leaving her sniffling again.

"You can tell me, Agatha. It's okay. I love you."

Rio meant it, but Agatha seemed to disintegrate again, crumbling in her hold.

"I saw him!" she cried, shoving her face into the pillow below them, her sobs buried in Egyptian cotton and down feathers.

She saw him?

She saw who?

Rio's lips parted and just as she started to ask, she realized exactly who Agatha was referring to.

"You saw Nicky?" 

Her head whipped off the pillow and she pushed herself up, looking over Agatha's shoulder despite the way Agatha was still hiding her face. When she continued to sob but nodded her head, Rio felt as though a hot coal had been dropped down her throat.

"Agatha, what do you mean? Where did you see him?!"

Getting immediate answers was unlikely, especially given the way Agatha's body continued to rack with her stifled crying. When she settled a few moments later and finally rolled to her back to look her wife in the eyes, Rio understood why.

"At the jail. When I went to see Wanda."

WHEN SHE WENT TO DO WHAT?

Rio loved her wife. More than anything in the entire fucking world, Rio loved her wife.

That, however, did not mean that her wife was not capable of making poorly-thought-out choices, as she had seemingly committed to that morning. Rio wanted to be angry, wanted to ask what the fuck she was thinking but...

She already knew the truth.

That truth coupled with the painstaking look on Agatha's face told her she couldn't.

Although she was certain her cheeks had surely flushed with emotion, Rio took in a slow breath as she tried to calm herself and lower her blood pressure. 

"And why, my love, did you do that without talking to me first?" It wasn't harsh or demanding; it was merely a request for knowledge, for understanding. Rio just wanted to understand what on earth could possibly compel her wife to make such a reckless choice. Clearly, there had been more than one repercussion that reared its head already.

Agatha's silence spoke for her.

She didn't actually know, and Rio understood that much. They were all floundering, doing what they could to grasp onto anything that would keep their heads above water, but seeing Wanda alone was a choice they both knew would only hurt her.

"I was ti-tired of waiting," Agatha finally returned, her voice laced with shame.

That, Rio could understand, maybe even more after her morning spent with Gabi. Rio was out and about getting some form of answers while Agatha had been left at home to sit on her hands and wait to hear from her. Somewhere deep down, Rio had been banking on Dani's presence keeping her distracted, but it seemed as though it hadn't worked as she hoped it might.

"I know, baby," Rio breathed at her, leaning in to place the softest kiss to her cheek. A hand raised, her thumb brushing at Agatha's cheek tenderly as she considered her next question carefully. "Do you... Do you want to tell me about it first? And then we can save the good parts for after?"

With watery eyes and a strong down-turn of her lips, Agatha gave the most pathetic nod Rio was sure she'd ever witnessed from her.

Before Rio moved to position herself curled against Agatha's side, the hand brushing her cheek moved to cup it lovingly as she placed a soft kiss to her lips. Once settled with her head on Agatha's chest, Rio picked up her hand and threaded their fingers together.

"Tell me, my love."

 

Dani.

If there was one thing Danica Harkness-Vidal had learned how to do early on in her life, it was listen for the front door, no matter where she was. Even over the sound of her un-amped violin, she knew what it sounded like.

When she heard it click overhead no more than half an hour after Agatha came home, she knew Rio was home too.

Hoping to catch her before she headed up the stairs, Dani stowed her violin and climbed the stairs from the basement, hopeful she could get at least a nibble or two out of her mom about how her morning went. 

When she reached the ground floor and there was no Rio to be found, something in Dani's middle sank. It wasn't illogical for her mom to have gone upstairs, especially with no one else out in the open up on her arrival, but something about it gnawed at the deepest parts of her. It was this dull burn, an ache that ate away more and more of her stability and mental fortitude.

Realistically, Dani knew they were living a nightmare. 

They were living a reality where consequences of actions long since past finally surfaced. 

That was where the true struggle was, Dani believed.

This woman had committed an atrocity against her mothers, had wounded them irreparably for life, and with her behind bars the theory was that everything should just be... good again.

But that was a fairy tale. It was a myth where no party was phased and everyone lived happily ever after. In real life, that was never how things would work out, and it was especially true for everyone involved in the mess they found themselves in. That woman's actions didn't have consequences that effected only her. The consequences of the choice she'd made to kidnap Nicky were hitting them all at full force. 

They hit her moms because they were now aware their son was within driving distance and yet, they still could not go to him.

They were hitting Gabi, clearly, who apparently felt so desolate and hopeless that she chose to go against Nicky's wishes and contact his real parents.
