They were hitting him -- probably the most -- to a point where he was isolating those that loved him, let alone people he didn't know that loved him as well. While not in his shoes, Dani had always grown up in the shadow of what he could have been. 

Maybe, she wondered, there had even been a time or two she'd walked in it while living in the city and had no idea.

Lastly, while the wouldn't admit it for the world, those consequences were impacting her, too.

Dani was always the dependable soldier, the steadfast pillar everyone could always lean against. In some aspects, she knew feeling such a way in regards to her parents was not the healthiest, but she also understood what they'd gone through before she was even born, and what they were going through now. If she could be the one to hold them together and tell them it was going to all be okay while they were staring down the face of adversity, then it was what she needed to do.

Quietly, Dani climbed the stairs and turned down the hall, her frown deepening at the sight of the shut door that led to her parents' room.

Shit.

That couldn't be good.

For a moment, she hesitated in her indecision.

She should go back downstairs, pick up her violin again and just play.

Or...

She could resort to immature and childish behavior because she was so tired of showing up to be shut out. She knew it was what her moms thought was the right thing to do, but she was tired of it. Wherever Agatha had gone earlier in the day, it wasn't to sign some stupid papers at the hospital. Dani was more convinced of that right then than ever.

So if her only way to get answers was to listen through the door?

Fuck it.

And so for the first ten minutes, she stood with her ear pressed to the corner where the door met the frame, straining as Agatha recounted the truth; it was every -- slightly muffled but -- unpleasant detail about her encounter with Wanda.

That hurt Dani's feelings, but she stayed planted to the floor. After an additional five minutes, she sat down.

Eavesdropping was bad. Sure, whatever.

But hearing Rio talk ten minutes later about the things she learned about Nicky?

That was fucking worth it.

That conversation wore on a little longer and Dani was certain there were parts of it she missed, but by the time she was no longer able to hear the voices inside the bedroom, she lifted herself to her feet and pulled out her phone.

Dani was the rock, always tried to be. But what happened when she was the one who needed a shore to crash upon?

She pulled up her contacts and scrolled down halfway, stopping on the name she was looking for.

Curious George.

Or, Georgina Diavallo; Dani's best friend, her next-door neighbor, and her ex-fiancée.

Although she stared at the text box for a beat too long, Dani finally managed to type out a message. 

Me: Hey George. Any chance you
would want to come to Newark
for dinner? I could really use a friend.

By the time Dani reached her room, her phone dinged softly in her hand.

Curious George: Anything for you,
Dan the Man. Should I bring anything?

Dani chuckled softly, punching in her reply.

Me: As much weed as you can get
your hands on, please and thanks.

Curious George: You got it, dude. See
you in a few hours. I'll text when I'm
close.

Dani smiled softly to herself, not hesitating to type her response.

Me: Thank you, ily.

Curious George: Ilyt, Dan. Be there ASAP.

Flopping onto her bed, Dani stared at the ceiling overhead as she tried to find some way to take an emotional inventory before George showed up and she completely lost her shit. No one needed that to happen.

Yet, all Dani could really think about was the fact that her brother was, again, twenty minutes away. Only this time, he was taking on the woman who had ruined his life and the lives of many others.

And for some insane reason, the only thing she truly wanted in that moment was to be sitting next to him as he did so.

 

Chapter 10: Only Light Can Take Our Bones

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Nikolai.

Not ten seconds after setting foot into the county jail, Nik knew he'd made a mistake. Seeing Agatha -- seeing one of his birth mothers -- felt like a haymaker straight to the chest. It was breathtaking in the worst, most excruciating ways, and while part of him knew he should have run right back out and tucked himself away in the dark reprieve of his bedroom, the other part knew he'd come too far.

When he was told he would have to wait an hour before Wanda was able to have another visitor, it would have been all too easy to just pack it up and go home.

But he couldn't.

For the first time in weeks, he was half-clean and out of bed. Even more, he was out of his apartment. Sure, he probably should have texted Gabi and let her know where he was but the idea she was out enjoying a brunch with friends or shopping with her step-sister stopped him from doing so.

She deserved to keep living, even when his world came to a screeching halt.

As much as Nik loved her, they were still two separate entities. And... Truth be told, Gabi deserved more than he was able to give her. If she could get that through spending time with the people who loved her, the thought eased some of his woes. 

In some ways, in the easiest ones he could find for himself, Nik felt as though he was tied to a dock post by his wrist as an angry, fierce tide tried to pull him out to sea. The post itself was the life up to the point of no return. The sea was no return. It was uncertain and churning, chaotic and lawless. He had no map to follow, no stars to guide him through it. In his fear of being lost in the endless, he needed the tether to what he once had to hold fast.

How could it when he wasn't sure what of it was real?

In the lobby of that jail, he tried to remember what in his life was.

Gabi was real. She was the realest thing he had and he knew he needed to start showing her as much. Pushing her away, refusing to speak, it was going to pile up into every reason she could leave. Maybe, at one point in his despair, he wanted her to, but that time had long since passed. Gabi was the only thing keeping his head above water. She was real.

His job was real. The job that was impossibly understanding in regards to his circumstances. It wasn't as though this happened on the regular; his employer understood it as a major life change and told him to take what time he needed. Without it, he felt a little aimless, but again it was something he'd done by his own choice.

His home was real. It had been his cocoon while his life fell to shambles around him and offered him somewhere to find respite. It was something he and Gabi owned together, something they'd done as a couple because it was what they wanted for their futures. It wasn't something his mother had gifted him or bestowed upon him.

His integrity was real. Nick was a good man, if not a little more in tune with his emotions than most. It was what allowed him to be the man he was, the man who cared for others and always tried to do what was right in any given situation. He had a good heart and a good head on his shoulders. That was his doing, not his -- not Wanda's.

His degree, his accomplishments, they were all his, even if the initial impact of reality left him feeling as though they were all due to her.

The life she'd given him had let him down those paths, but ultimately, Nik was the one who made the choices. 

"Malikov for Maximoff?" 

A quick hand swept up and plucked the pair of headphones off his head as he met the gaze of the security guard from across the room, giving a not of confirmation. He stuffed them into his hoodie pocket as he got to his feet and followed along being the guard throughout the facility.

By the time he found himself seated in a cold steel chair facing a thick wall of glass, the sense finally smacked right into him.

What the fuck am I doing here?

It seemed like a good idea to come for answers in the throes of his depression, but with all that had crossed his mind in the past hour, he suddenly realized he didn't know exactly what he wanted to say.

He'd just have to wing it.

When the door on the other side of the room clicked open and Wanda shuffled into view, something in his squeezed most painfully. It was a constraint around his heart; this woman he'd called 'mother' for so long, who he'd loved unconditionally due to that title, she was not a mother at all. She was just a woman who made a terrible choice, one that caused him to question who he even was in the world. Maybe to her, it was what it was. To him, it was every fucking waking moment.

He watched, completely stilled and slouched in his chair, as she was fastened to the table and allowed the use of one hand. The moment the security guard walked away, she used it to swipe up the phone with an undeniably bright look in her green eyes, even if it didn't touch the rest of her face.

Nik was not exactly apathetic, but her eagness caused his stomach to turn. He did not doubt that if his phone had been on, she would have been trying to call, but seeing it written on her face made him feel sick.

Didn't she understand what she'd done? Didn't she see, just by looking at him, what the choices she'd made had turned him into? He was but a shell of the man he was mere weeks ago, caught between wanting to cling to what he knew and wanting to get lost in the sea of everything he'd been deprived of his entire life.

He not only had a mother, but he had two. Even more, he had a sister. He was a big brother.

She took that from him.

Because she took him.

He stared at her, critical and silent as her eyes flickered toward the phone, encouraging him to pick it up. He wanted to, knew he needed to, but action did not immediately find him. He was trying to fortify, trying to prepare himself for anything and everything she might have to say when he knew it would likely hurt. When she glanced at it again, he finally caved and picked it up, placing it to his ear.

He knew he should have taken more time, especially since he could have predicted exactly what she would open with.

"Hi, my b--"

"Absolutely not," he barked gruffly into the phone. "That illusion is shattered. I have never been your boy. And you don't get to call me as much, especially now." His words were a low rattle through the phone, but they hit Wanda with precision.

Her back stiffened and her posture straightened a bit, wide eyes simply blinking at him.

In all of their years shared, Nik had never dared to speak to her with such malice laced in his tone. He had never dared to defy her, to challenge her, to truly stand up to her. Now, he had the right. Now, she'd given him a reason.

"I'm sorry, Nikolai, I --"

"No!" 

That one was a little louder, a little more forceful. He did not follow it up, but he also did not break eye-contact with her as he stared at her through the glass.

"Then what am I to call you?" she asked lowly, though he could still hear the panic in her voice no matter how hard she tried to hide it. "The name they chose for you?"

He knew she was genuinely looking for an answer, but hearing it asked aloud felt like a battering ram against his ribcage, knocking every bit of wind right out of him. 

That wasn't what he wanted. The problem was... He didn't know what he wanted.

Nikolai wasn't his name but... Neither was Nicky.

So who was he?

"You call me Nick. It doesn't matter how it's spelled. It's... That's what you can call me."

Part of him wanted to elaborate primarily for himself, to talk out why that felt like the best fit for the time being, but doing so would have allowed her to be privy to his thought process and that was something he wasn't ready for. In fact, he wasn't sure he ever would be again. Wanda had taken so much from him; he did not owe her anything more.

"Okay," she agreed quietly, scooting forward in her seat the most minute amount. There was a heavy pause between them, thick and wrought with tension, but she was brave enough to try and be the first one to speak. "How have you been?"

Her shallow question earned her a dry snip of a laugh, thin lips pulling back to show bared and sharp teeth. Was she serious? She wasn't looking at him enough to glean an answer to that question? He knew he looked like shit. Sure, his hair was clean and he had fresh clothes on, but the deep wells beneath his eyes and the gaunt arches of his cheeks spoke well enough as to how he was feeling.

"What do you think, Wanda?" he clipped, not missing the way she winced at the use of her real name. "I've barely gotten out of bed. My girlfriend probably thinks I hate her and she should leave me. I suddenly have three people who want to meet me and I know nothing about them. I --" Nick's jaw clamped shut and he sat back in her chair, eyeing her with contempt. No. She didn't get to know what he knew. She didn't get to know that he was well aware she'd spoken with his mother earlier in the day. 

He wanted to see if she would tell him herself.

He knew she wouldn't.

"I'm miserable," he told her, using it more as an insult than something that would cause her to show him pity. "And it's because of you. Because of what you did."

The more he went on, the more Wanda seemed to tense. It was clear that she'd asserted herself into a delusion where she could talk him down, but it was not the reality of the situation. The reality was there was no talking him down; she ruined his life by being selfish twenty-five years prior. There was no way around it.

He let another silence befall them, hoping for at least an apology, but she offered not a word. Instead, he took up the mantle of driving the conversation forward, driven on by his need to know the truth.

"Can I ask you something?" He didn't actually wait for her to agree before he continued. "Why didn't you tell me when I was an adult? I mean..." He took a breath, his jaw tightening as the words seemed to ball up and catch in his throat. He was angry, irate, even, but he knew her. He knew how to handle her. If he started screaming and demanding she give him what he was asking for, it would get him nowhere. He had to be reserved, had to play his hand right.

"I get why you kept it from me as a kid. But when I moved to New York, when I became an adult... Why didn't you tell me?" 

His demand was not harsh; it was a plea.

Wanda simply blinked at him, as if she hadn't understood the question.

But she did.

He knew she did.

"Seven fucking years. For seven years, you took my choice away. You took away my right to be the one to make the decision. I had a right to know, Wanda! I had a right to make the choice myself, whether or not I reached out. I... I would have. But now... Now it's like..." Oh God. Oh no. The longer he tried to talk, the more his voice started to break. He was reaching panic, he knew, but he needed to reign it in.

"Now, there are expectations of me. Expectations that I don't know how to meet because I can barely even figure out what my own fucking name is. And that's what you did to me. You took me from them, you changed my name, and you gave me the life you thought I should have, not the one I would have if you'd never been in the picture. God, I wish you'd never been in the picture."

It was harsh, but the way he was trying to ramble his way through an explanation was far from. The words themselves were not intended as weapons, even if they were anyway as they struck the woman across from him, piercing right into her.

"You don't mean that --"

"I do!" he cut in, not allowing her to speak. This was his time. "I don't know who I'd be if they'd been the ones to raise me, and that's the fucking problem, isn't it? I don't know what school I would have gone to, or how many friends I would have had. I don't know what teachers I would have liked, or how excited my little sister would have been at each of my graduations. I don't know any of it because you never let it happen. And why?! For what?! What do you have to show for it, right now, in this moment?!"

His intent was loud, but his voice had grown louder. 

"Can't you just tell me?! Can't you just tell me, of all fucking people?!"

His cry was pained and broken, his eyes filling with confused and angry tears. He doubted she would tell him the truth, but of everyone involved, didn't he deserve it the most?

"P-please. Just... just tell me why."

The display before her was raw and emotional, obvious in the way Wanda slinked into her chair as she tried to shrink herself down, to try and shirk off the weight of what Nick was thrusting upon her.

She was silent but he could not understand why. Was she cooking up another lie? Was she going to say she had to leave? Was she going to run away like the coward he was realizing she was?

Whatever it was she was trying to do, he'd had enough. If she wasn't going to give him the answers he was seeking, there was no point in staying. He sat up, glancing toward the cradle on the wall as he started to lower the phone. Somehow, he knew it was exactly what might get her to speak, if she was ever going to.

"I didn't want to be alone."

It was so small, probably the smallest Nick ever heard her be.

"And so I took you to make sure I wouldn't be."

Somehow, he wasn't sure if it was better than not knowing the truth at all.

She was a selfish creature. She was someone who had committed an atrocity to serve herself, everyone else be completely damned. They were all paying for it now, in their own ways, and Nick wasn't entirely sure what to do with that. It was a known fact; he'd been aware the entire time that he was not the only one hurting throughout it all, even if his pain felt the most obvious to him.

"And how's that working out for you now?" he asked back, his voice tired and ragged. "Thanks for at least telling me the truth."

With that, he plucked the phone away from his ear and started to set it down, but the way Wanda jerked to attention caused him to hesitate. A hand flew up, a lone finger raised as if to ask him for just one more moment of his time. He shouldn't oblige her, but something in him willed it to happen anyway as he lifted the phone back to his ear.

"What?"

"I..." she started, clearly fumbling for the right way to say what was on her mind. "Agatha... She was here earlier."

Holy shit, he thought, she's actually being fucking honest.

"And?"

"And she..." Wanda sighed, seeming to stare her own resignation in the face of the man she'd stolen away all those years ago. "They never stopped looking for you. And... And I don't think they ever stopped missing you."

The sting behind his eyes was immediate and overwhelming but Nick did not let himself cry. Not again, not in front of her. It still hurt, in some bittersweet way, that the people who lost him so long ago never gave up hope that they would find him. They never stopped wishing for him.

They never stopped celebrating him every year on January 1st, his real birthday.

Somehow, even though he learned as much from stalking his sister on social media, hearing Wanda admit it hurt ten times more, only this time he did not have a laptop to fling across the room or a bed to burrow into. All he could do in those moments was blink at the lie of a mother before him as two hefty tears streaked down his cheeks and he hung up the phone.

She didn't get a single goodbye, not even a wave, as he rose to his feet and made his exit to call a ride and go home to his girlfriend.

Dani.

Curious George: I'm outside.

When Dani poked her head out into the hallway, the door to her parents' room was still shut and as she approached it, the interior still carried heavy silence. The likely scenario was as such: After the emotionally guelling and taxing conversation her moms shared it, they probably both fell asleep.

Honestly, that was fine with her.

She needed space of her own and while she loved them impossibly, she wasn't sure she could answer a 'where are you going?' without having a breakdown of her own.

Dani knew she shouldn't have sat outside their door, shouldn't have eavesdropped on their private conversation, but she needed to know. She needed to be in the loop just as much as everyone else and she was still fighting with her indignancy over the fact that Agatha had chosen to run off to the jail without her. It wasn't so much that her momma had gone alone, but rather that she lied several times throughout the process.

On the other hand, hearing her mom recount all of the incredible things she'd learned about Nicky at coffee that morning wounded her in a different way. From what she could make out, he was a smart guy, had a good job, and his girlfriend thought the world of him.  He liked music and went to raves -- God, what were the chances they'd been to some of the same ones? -- and liked going for runs when he needed to clear his head (which honestly left him sounding a lot like mom).

All of that information and Dani wasn't supposed to know any of it. Because they hadn't decided to tell her. 

She'd been stubborn and invasive and while she wanted to feel bad, she couldn't.

So, she grabbed her phone and threw on a coat, quietly making her way out of the house and to the awaiting Honda Accord in front of the family home. When she climbed inside, tired blue eyes fell onto the other occupant; Dani's light, her savior, her safe place.

George was... Well, to the naked eye, she was beautiful, that much was painfully obvious. Her features were chiseled and pointed, high cheekbones and a slim nose, but there was a softness always found in her dark grey eyes that sometimes looked blue and sometimes looked green. Her lips were thick and full and often times, Dani still woke up from dreams where she got to kiss them.

The only reason she did not, in reality, was by her own choice.

Dani and George -- who majored in Music Theology -- met sophomore year and became fast friends. They quickly found a lot of common ground, shared in music taste and film taste and often went on day-long shopping trips because they could. It had been Dani's first year of real freedom even if it was her second year in college and she could not have had a better partner in crime to do it with.

By the end of sophomore year, any and all charades where they were trying to maintain neutrality were tossed to the wind and the two of them began dating.

A year later, as Junior year drew to a close, George proposed. 

Surprisingly, Dani had known it was coming. Even more surprisingly, she agreed with ease. It seemed like the right thing to do at the time, the right path for her life to take but as school work and personal responsibilities came into the picture, they both knew they'd made a mistake.

It had been a hard conversation for Dani to broach, but when she discovered they both equally felt as though they'd jumped the gun?

Well, it made her believe even more that George was the woman she was meant to spend the rest of her life with. At the same time, she needed to establish priorities, which left them where they were:

Not dating, but best friends who were still in love, just smart enough to wait for graduation before venturing on a life where they were meant to be together. It also was rather convenient that they shared an apartment wall and had constant access to one another most of the time. 

Well, at least until... all of this shit started.

They'd been in contact, of course, but George understood Dani's need to time and space to try and process everything that was so rapidly changing in her life. Now, Dani needed someone to talk to, someone who could listen and understand that while this was all about the discovery of a missing piece of their family, she was beginning to lose herself.

She was accepting her parents' lies with an indifferent smile on her face and sneaking around to get the actual truth.

That wasn't her. It wasn't who they were as a family. And yet, it was where they'd come to exist.

There, in the dim light of the setting sun, that blonde hair and those grey eyes felt like salvation.

With a quick hug over the center console, Dani pulled back to behold her best friend for the longest moment, a twinkle of appreciation flickering in her eyes.

"Thank you," she voiced softly, leaning in to place a light kiss to the other woman's cheek. "I know I haven't been party central lately, but... I really appreciate you dropping everything to be here for me. I... Well, you know."

George's smile was instant, but it did not touch her eyes.

"I do. And you know I'll do it again and again. Let's get something to eat."

So, she drove them into town and they did just that, grabbing a couple of burgers and fries before George took them toward greener pastures and a spot they'd spent too many nights at to count.

It was an overlook on the outside of the city, a place to behold the speckles of light both below and above when the sun disappeared and the night sky was left in its wake. They spent too many summer hours there, both romantic and not, and it was somewhere Dani often found peace.  

As they ate with only the dull sound of the radio humming on in the background, she could actually feel it find her again.

As if it were a normal Sunday night, she and George were sitting at a favorite summertime spot -- albeit in the spring -- eating their cheeseburgers and taking time to just exist together. There was no expectation, no demand. Dani asked her to be a friend and it was exactly what she chose to do. Maybe it was hard, sometimes, to act like those things didn't make her fall even harder for the woman behind the steering wheel, but Dani knew they were closing in on the finish line. In weeks, they would graduate and then, they could figure life out from there.

Until then, they could just share space while Dani built her courage to leap and George was waiting to catch her.

As they finished, the air in the car shifted and George turned in her seat. The look on her face was gentle in the light of the moon, but it tugged on Dani's heartstrings.

"You know I'm not one to ask questions when it comes to you," George started, reaching up to tuck a strand of hair behind her own ear, "but are you okay?"

That was a loaded question. An incredibly loaded question.

Physically, Dani was fine. None of this had actually harmed her and yet, inside that little racetrack of a mind she possessed?

She was a storm, a whipping and whirling hurricane that never seemed to lose speed. There were so many thoughts, so many feelings, so many things she simply did not know how to say out loud. If she never found a way to, though, it was going to tear her apart.

"I want to be," she answered quietly, looking out the windshield to the night sky above. "But... How do you even know what okay is when the cautionary tale you always heard as a kid actually has a face? And a fucking apartment four blocks away from ours?" Her voice wavered and broke the tiniest bit toward the end, causing George to reach for her hand.

"Babes, it sounds to me like you've been holding a lot of this in."

Ha. What a fucking understatement.

Against her wishes, Dani could feel her tears as they gathered atop her lower lids, fighting to fall.

George loved her, Dani knew that much. It was why she'd abandoned her plans to be there for Dani, why she bought dinner and drove them to a place of comfort. Because of that love, Dani knew she was in the one and only spot she could truly be honest, the one place she could find salvation from the chaos inside her head.

"I... I felt like a kid again today, sitting at my parents' bedroom door, listening to their conversation. They... Mom went to meet Nicky's girlfriend and... I thought maybe momma and I would watch a movie or find something to do, but she... She took off and went to visit the woman who took him. And I..." Dani's lip quivered as she lifted her head to look toward her best friend, the tears adding a pathetic shine to her eyes. "She saw him. She didn't speak to him, but she saw him. And I... I asked her what happened. She lied to me. She told me nothing was going on, fed me some bullshit about going into work. I -- Augh!" 

Both of her hands flew up, cradling the entirety of her face as she exhaled a low and long groan, trying to sort through her feelings and finding herself unable.

"I get it, I do," she managed as she pulled them down and looked to George again. "They want to protect me. They always have. But I'm grown now. I'm graduating college in three weeks. I... I don't need them to fucking baby me about this. They've spent my whole life talking about him, wondering what he's up to or how he's doing. They've always talked about him like he was still alive and now that he is... They don't seem to want to talk about him at all."

She paused, tucking her lower lip between her teeth. It was unnerving, really, to say it all aloud, but she knew it was much needed. More than that, she knew it was safe with George.

"It feels... Unfair. I've been hoping for this moment just as much as they have and it feels like... I don't know. They're shutting me out? Or infantilizing me? And I just... I want to know, too. He's my brother too. And maybe it makes me sound like a spoiled brat but... I deserve to be in the loop. I've spent my whole life being the vessel for their unresolved trauma and paranoia and it's... It's fucked that they won't give me this part of it!"

Somewhere in the middle of that last little tirade and completely unaware of the heat on her cheeks or the tightness of her throat, Dani started to cry. 

Dani didn't cry. It wasn't something she did. Sure, it happened a time here or there, but it was often something she actively fought.

In those moments, she hadn't even realized she was doing it. 

As if it were nothing more than automatic reflex, George pushed up the center console and gave Dani's hip a nudge before climbing into the seat with her and pulling her into her arms.

Although her mothers had hugged her countless times since the start of the storm, there was something about the way it felt to be wrapped in George's embrace that quieted the thunder in her head. It hadn't stopped for days, driving her out of her mind, but being in her best friend's arms somehow muffled the severity.

There, being held by someone who would always love her, Dani found peace.

They stayed like that for a short while with Dani a teary mess as she cried into George's shirt until she fell asleep. Only a few minutes later, her phone dinged from its place in the door handle. Carefully, George made a play for it, already having a sense of who it was. When she saw 'Momma' above the '1 New Message' bubble, she knew a response was required.

Instead of waking the woman in her arms, George -- having known her passcode for the last two years -- unlocked her phone to see the message from Agatha.

Momma Bear: Are you here? Did you go 
somewhere?

Even in those seven words, George could already feel Agatha's anxiety seeping through the screen.

Me: Hey momma, this is G. I grabbed
Dani for dinner and we came to
do some stargazing but she fell 
asleep. I'll bring her home soon.

Almost immediately, the animated bubble at the bottom of the screen as Agatha typed her response.

Momma Bear: You're a good egg,
Georgie. Thank you for taking care
of her.

With a soft sigh, George locked the phone and squeezed Dani a little closer to her chest. 

 

Agatha.

After their rather emotional exchange, both Agatha and Rio had fallen asleep tangled in one another with quiet tears soaking the pillows beneath their faces. When they awoke a little after eight, it was to a completely silent house.

Rio scoured every room to no avail, returning a few moments later to announce that she was unable to find Dani.

While Agatha's initial reaction was the panic, she was very quick to remember that she had a phone and was perfectly capable of responding like any rational adult by shooting her daughter a text before she called in a search party. So, she did just that.

Me: Are you here? Did you go
somewhere?

She took a breath and sent the message, though in the time it took for a response, she'd already started going over through the endless scenarios where she might never see her daughter again.

"My love," Rio soothed, sliding into bed to sit next to her as she handed over a bottle of water. "I'm sure she just went out for some air. Give her some time, I'm sure she'll text back."

Rio was right; she was always right, but Agatha still hated any moment in the here and now where she did not have full awareness of what was going on in her life and the lives of those she loved. Dani was a grown woman, yes, but she was still their little girl and if something ever happened to her?

Agatha feared she might not survive it.

Her phone vibrated in her hand, pulling at her attention.

Boog: Hey momma, this is G. I grabbed
Dani for dinner and we came to
do some stargazing but she fell
asleep. I'll bring her home soon.

"Oh," she breathed in relief, her shoulders slouching slightly.

"Oh?" came the soft question beside her.

"I didn't know George was in town. Did you?" It was a stupid thing to ask, but it tumbled out before Agatha could stop it.

"No, but it's not surprising they're together. Is Dani okay?"

Rio had a fair point; those two were usually attached at the hip, but with everything going on, Dani had obviously been trying to figure things out on her own. Apparently, her stubborn tenacity could only get her so far.

"She's fine. She fell asleep. George said she'll bring her home soon."

Quickly, she typed her response.

Me: You're a good egg, Georgie.
Thank you for taking care
of her.

The moment she locked the screen, a set of nimble fingers reached out and plucked the phone from her fingers before Rio leaned across her to set it on the nightstand.

"What are you doing?" Agatha questioned softly, catching Rio's gaze as she settled back into her spot.

"Well," Rio began quietly, her hand raising to cradle Agatha's jaw. "It's been a very long time since I looked my wife in the eyes and told her I loved her, so..." She paused, their gazes locking as she took the lightest of kisses. "I love you. And while I admittedly don't feel up to sex... I would really like it if you would let me kiss you for a little while."

For just a moment, Agatha thought she was going to cry for the third time that day.

The lot of them, they'd been through hell. It was hard, dealing with what they were and still trying to live a normal life. It was even harder to act like it wasn't eating them up and trying to spit them back out. They were all wringer-thin to a point where Agatha had not even stopped to consider just how much strain the situation was putting on every facet of her life.

But Rio noticed.

She always noticed.

"That's funny," Agatha whispered, taking a light kiss of her own. "I would really like it if you would kiss me for a little while."

The most tender smile curled Rio's lips, one that caused Agatha's heart to skip a beat or two in her chest.

"I'd love nothing more. Well, other than you, of course."

Chapter 11: A Welcome So Changed

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Gabi. 

After departing the cafe and managing to keep her trip to the market short, Gabi made her way home and was not at all surprised to find the house quiet. If anything, she would have surprised it it wasn't quiet.

She took her time stowing the items she'd brought home with her and put a kettle on for tea. If she could be convincing enough, she might be able to get Nik to have a cup. 

That was wishful thinking and she knew it. 

Nothing she chose to do was going to get him out of bed.

Well, she was half right on that.

Gabi headed for their bedroom with every intent of changing her clothes and curling up on the couch, but she was struck the moment she walked through the doorway and her eyes fell on their bed.

Their empty bed.

Their empty bed where her boyfriend was not wrapped tightly in their comforter and his own misery.

Immediately, panic filled every inch of her being as she began to scour their home in search of him. He obviously was not in the front room, not in the bedroom, and he was not in their bathroom. She even checked the office; empty. However, something about the bathroom caught her attention.

The boxers and t-shirt he'd been wearing for three days were in a pile on the ground.

Curiously, she made her way to the closet and was genuinely surprised to smell the faint leftover traces of his cologne.

He was out of the house.

That was good.

That was amazing, actually.

What was not so amazing was knowing he was out of the house and having absolutely no clue where he had gone.

If she had to guess, though, she probably could.

In the same way she was trying to make things better in some way by going to the cafe to meet Rio, she was realizing very quickly that he was reaching the same conclusions on the opposite end of the spectrum. He spent his days laying in bed, mourning a life that felt like an illusion, and it didn't accomplish anything. He wasn't healing, wasn't taking steps toward figuring out what his new life was going to look like. He was punishing everyone else in his life because he was too lost in himself to know which end was up.

Gabi would never fault him for that.

Everything he knew, everything, was a lie. That was a trauma she knew could not be funneled into words, something Nik might never be able to articulate. It was pain and grief and confusion all wrapped up into one chaotic package that seemed to have blown up right in his hands.

So, if he felt the need to pull himself out of bed to look into the eyes of the person that spent a quarter of his life lying to him, who was she to be upset?

Nik needed closure. More than that, he needed the ability to let go of what happened to him so he could focus on a way to move forward. Gabi knew -- even more after her morning spent with Rio -- that every single person missing him would have done any damn thing in their power to take his pain away. He had two mothers who relentlessly loved any and every version of him. He had a little sister who missed him without ever meeting him.

He had an entire life waiting for him, one he just needed to decide he wanted bad enough.

That was going to be a decision that could only be made by Nik. Whatever he chose, she would support him, but if they went the rest of their lives and he chose not to embrace what he was missing, it would surely kill her.

Rio was so incredibly kind in the face of so much devastation. Gabi knew she'd fucked up a couple of times in comparing them, but for as much as it seemed to hurt the other woman, she liked it, too. She explained as much, but some part of Gabi couldn't help but feel guilty. She was giving a mother glimpses of a son she didn't know by being told she just had to look in a mirror. It was a heavy sentiment, but it clearly meant a lot to her.

With hopes that Nik would find his way home without her added pressure, she undressed and showered, pulling on one of his hoodies and a pair of leggings once out. She fixed herself a cup of the chicken chili she'd made a couple days before and ate at the table in silence, fighting her urge to text her boyfriend by telling herself everything would be fine.

After her meal, Gabi made her way to the couch and flipped the television on to continue waiting.

She didn't have to wait long.

Her phone sounded quietly in her lap and her focus snapped to it, the incoming message popping up on the screen.

From: Nik

Her heart stuttered her in chest and she rushed to open it, thankful to see what was inside.

Nik: I'm on my way home. I 
stopped at Mario's and got a
piece of their tiramisu.

Gabi paused in her reading to take a moment of reverence.

He had been miserable for weeks and on the one occasion he braved to leave the house, he was coming back with a gift. It was something he knew she loved, something he knew would say 'I'm Sorry' better than he could for the time being.

Nik: I went to see Wanda. It...
We'll talk about it when I get
home. I love you, Gabriela.

By the time she finished reading, the tears were begging to overflow. 

She let them. 

She blinked them out, letting them roll cleanly and heavily down her cheeks. All of this was no, there was no questioning as much. However, learning to deal with it all? it was a different process for every single person effected, something Gabi came to realize sitting across the table from his mother, one of his real mothers.

Although she was nervous before about his absence, something about the wait for him to return was made more intense by the knowledge of where he'd been.

He went to see Wanda. Not Alisa. Not 'Mom.' 

He went to see Wanda.

Someone who ruined his entire life.

There was something to be said, however, about the fact that he stopped for dessert. However bad it had gone, he still cared enough to offer a wordless apology of something Gabi liked.

It was only another ten minutes or so until the front door swung open and he shuffled through it, clutching the small brown sack in his hands. His head -- covered by his hood -- lifted and those beautiful hazel eyes found her across the space between them.

"Hi, mi amor."

Gabi almost melted. His voice was so soft, but she could hear how genuine it was. Even more than that, it had been weeks since he used the chosen pet name for her, knowing how much she loved it.

"Hi, handsome," she offered, pushing herself to sit up a little against the arm rest of the couch. He slipped his shoes off and made his way to her as he set the bag on the coffee table, but before she could adjust more, he simply laid atop her, his torso between her legs as his head landed on her sternum.

For a moment, Gabi just felt his weight. For the first time in weeks, she felt what it was like to have him against her, to have his arms around her as they wedged between her and the cushions. It was the most indescribable thing; she'd spent too many hours wishing for it and to finally have it was pushing her closer to her breaking point.

Gabi tried to be strong for everyone involved, but she forgot what it meant to be strong for herself.

That was out the window as the silence fell over him and Nik simply laid against her chest.

She let the night turn around them for a little while longer before she felt compelled to say something, something she wanted to make sure he knew.

"I love you," she murmured softly, reaching up a hand to lightly run it over his hair in the most soothing manner she could muster.

He didn't say anything but he did tighten his hold on her at the exact same time he gave a soft sniffle.

She heard it without a word spoken.

I love you too. I do.

"We don't have to talk about it tonight," she whispered to him, lightly pinching and rubbing a few strands of his hair between her fingers. "I'm just happy to have you so close."

He sniffled again, but he also snuggled in a little tighter. She knew the flurry of thoughts inside his head was immense and it was fighting to keep him below the surface, but he was fighting so impossibly hard to keep it at bay. If he needed to cling to her like some kind of life raft, she would more than happily be that for him.

Gabi would have been anything he needed whenever he needed it. She just hoped he realized as much.

Although she picked up the remote and turned on one of his favorite movies -- The Voices -- he stayed quiet throughout the duration of the film. That, Gabi realized, was because he had pretty quickly fallen asleep. When she woke him up a few hours later, she was careful with him as she coaxed him up and back to bed, hesitating by his side after pulling the covers up his torso.

Should she ask?

Should she just... get into a bed that was half hers despite sleeping on the couch for weeks?

Thankfully, she didn't need to dwell on it much longer because Nik spoke.

"Will you sleep in here tonight?" His tone was laden with exhaustion and his hand slowly raised to wrap around hers, dark eyes sweeping up to her in the dim light from the hallway.

How could she not? It was all she'd wanted for weeks and now that he was offering it, she knew she would be a fool to turn it down.

"Of course, baby," she murmured as she leaned down to kiss his forehead. After shutting off the lights and shedding her sweatshirt for a tank top, she climbed in beside him. Per their normal routine, she would have folded into him and drifted right off to sleep.

But nothing was normal anymore.

Instead, Nik was quick to roll to his side as he placed his head on her chest and fit himself to every curve of her body.

One more time, her heart shattered for him. 

She couldn't remember the last time he'd been so desperate for physical affection, to know he had her right there in front of him. He wasn't a distant boyfriend by any means, but it was rare for him to show any overt need for closeness. What she was seeing right then was a man clinging to the only thing he knew was safe.

Because Gabi would always be that for him; a safe place to come back to every single time.

After about twenty minutes, she considered he'd fallen asleep again, but he spoke.

It startled her, but not as much as what he had to say.

"I saw Agatha at the jail," he disclosed in a whisper, sniffling softly again.

Holy shit.

Before she could say anything, he continued.

"I didn't talk to her, but we made eye contact as she was leaving. I had to wait a while because she was obviously there to see her, too. And... I don't think it went well."

Gabi was so close to silent she was nearly holding her breath. It was the longest string of words he'd spoken in some time and the weight of the ones he was choosing was immense. It was one thing to get out of bed and try to speak with someone he was owed answers from. It was something else to run into a birth mother longing to see him and not speak to her.

As much as she hated, Gabi understood it.

He simply wasn't ready.

He was coming to understand, however, that while his world stood still and he fell to pieces, everyone else's kept going. Agatha and Rio were still out there, missing him, and they wanted and needed answers just as much as he did.

"And did yours?" she finally asked in a hushed murmur. "Go well, I mean?"

Nik's arm tightened around her middle and her eyes squeezed shut. She knew what it meant before he was able to speak.

"I think it went better," he offered, trying to snuggle in a little closer. "I... She didn't say much, and what she did say didn't help me as much as what I had to say myself... Things out loud that I didn't want to inwardly acknowledge. I... Asked her why she never told me, even when I was an adult. I told her it was my right to make the choice. She didn't answer, but..."

When he stopped speaking, Gabi could feel as his arm constricted around her and pulled her tightly to him.

"She did tell me the truth about one thing."

Her hand lifted to gently brush over his hair again, something she knew often soothed him. It was clear he wasn't angry, but he was still upset.

"And what was that, baby?"

"She told me Agatha was there. And that... They never stopped looking for me. And they never stopped missing me."

Gabi's heart squeezed in her chest; it was a lesson she'd learned earlier that day, too, something Rio had made abundantly clear. She couldn't tell him that, though, not right then. He said it best; it was his choice. Telling him right then she'd gone over his head to offer comfort to a struggling family wasn't going to help either of them, but it did make her realize that she couldn't keep it from him forever.

Gabi loved Nik and lying to him was not something she ever chose to do.

Hiding the truth right then was what was best for both of them.

"And how does that make you feel?"

Her voice was calm and devoid of any nerves, but she could still tell it was a hard-hitting question. He was quiet for a long few minutes, almost long enough to convince her he truly was asleep, but he surprised her again by whispering softly into the night.

"Confused. Because... I know I should go to them, I should try to meet them, but..." He sniffled again but this time, he lifted his head to look at her in the dark. "This isn't the me I want to show them. And it's not the me I want you to see. I just... need a little more time."

Gabi's hand dropped to cradle his jaw and she lifted her head, pressing her lips softly to his in a loving kiss.

"It's okay to get yourself where you need to be. I'm sure they'll understand."

She said it like it was a hopeful misnomer, but the truth was she already knew they did. She knew they would wait for days, weeks, or months for him. It was just that no one wanted it to turn into years.

That could not happen.

Nik yawned and laid his head back on his chest, one last sad admission passing through his lips quietly.

"I think they love me more than Wanda ever did."

Oh, he was right about that.

 

Dani.

When Dani awoke in George's arms, it was almost eleven at night. She was a little disgruntled with herself for falling asleep when she was meant to be spending time with someone she cared about, but George had been quick to assure her she needed the sleep.

"When you take on the weight of everyone else's pain, it's going to burn through muscles that were under prepared."

It was so profound as it left George's mouth and landed uncomfortably in Dani's ears as George pressed a kiss to the side of her head and climbed into the driver's seat again.

Dani knew she was right.

She was trying so hard to keep everyone else afloat when she hadn't been ready. It wasn't like she woke up the morning of the gala and thought 'We're finally going to know if my brother is alive today.' It wasn't even like she ever thought the day would come for them. It had been her entire lifetime of her mothers missing a son Dani never got to meet, an entire twenty-one years of her parents hovering over her to make sure they did not lose her like they lost Nicky.

He was the warning, the reasoning, the rationale as to why her entire childhood had been locked up and secured in every way imaginable. He was the reason she couldn't go to slumber parties, the reason she couldn't go to an amusement park without one of her parents present. Hell, he was even the reason she lived so close while not being in the exact same city. Sure, she would have gone to Julliard no matter where it was located in the country, but it helped to know it was close enough that her parents wouldn't obsessively fret over her once she was out from under their care.

Even then, her entire freshman year was spent under their roof until she turned eighteen. It was understandable and she couldn't exactly live on campus as a minor, but the moment she found an apartment a half an hour away, she jumped on it.

As much as Dani loved the idea of Nicky, it was also safe to say she blamed him (unfairly) for what she'd had to face. Older now, she was able to see it from all angles, but at the time had been frustrated by the circumstances. She had never done anything to warrant the way they helicoptered the living fuck out of her, but because he disappeared before he could walk and talk, she faced the consequences.

The older she got, the more she realized how childish that was.

Nicky could help what happened to him as an infant no more than Dani could control her parents' response to their loss.

Nicky was still her Imaginary Nicky. For as confused as it made her growing up, he was still the brother she wished she had. He was still the brother she wished she could have played baseball with, or learned to rollerblade with. He was still the brother she wished would have been there for her through high school and college.

Here he was, making his appearance just as she was going to graduate.

Stupidly, she wished he would be there.

She knew better than that. He clearly wasn't even ready to make contact with them, let alone show up at her graduation from one of the most prestigious music schools in the country.

He wasn't ready for family.

She couldn't place blame on him for that of all things.

The drive back to the house was quiet, though George did reach over the center console to hold Dani's hand on her thigh. When she pulled up in front of the Harkness-Vidal home, she turned to face her best friend with a kind smile on her lips.

"Give yourself a break," she coaxed softly, her thumb brushing over the back of Dani's hand. "And give the moms one, too. It's hard on all of you and I think... I think I have come to know them well enough to know they'll come to you... Just when they're ready. They need time, too."

Damn George and her sage wisdom.

Dani knew she was right even if she hated to admit it. Through George's perspective, Dani could see just how hard all three of them were trying. It was reasonable for her to be frustrated, but anger was unneeded. Agatha and Rio still loved her with everything they were, they just needed to figure out how to balance that with the grief and heartache of knowing their son was alive and wanted nothing to do with them.

"I don't know what I would do without you, Georgie," Dani murmured, leaning over the console to wrap her arms around her best friend.

"Go undeniably insane and spiral until you crash out and try to drink an entire bottle of SoCo again?"

They both laughed as Dani pulled away, shaking her head.

"Learned my lesson last time. Only top shelf shit from now on, and I pace myself. Because binge drinking is unbecoming of anyone."

She unbuckled her seatbelt, jumping slightly as she felt a light gracing beneath her chin just before George took hold of it and turned her head to look her straight in the eyes.

"Be gentle with yourself, Dan. And give the moms a little more wiggle room. It's going to work out. It's just taking its sweet time."

George's beautiful eyes sparkled in the light of the moon and it melted something in Dani's middle.

She loved Georgina with all of her heart and more often than not, she wanted to say fuck school and reestablish their relationship, but that was a conversation for another time.

"I love you, George," Dani told her reaching up for her hand to give it a light squeeze.

"I know you do, Dan. And I love you too. Now, go inside and get some sleep. Tell the moms you love them, even if they're asleep. Text me tomorrow, okay?" Her voice was velvet smooth and there was nothing but kindness woven into every inch of her expression.

Danica Harkness-Vidal did not deserve Georgina Divallo.

But she was really fucking glad she had her.

"Goodnight. I'll text you tomorrow." Against her better judgement, Dani leaned over and placed a soft kiss to George's cheek. "Get home safe."

With a light wave as Dani shut the door, George rolled away from the curb and began her journey back to the apartment. With a soft sigh, she turned to face her parents' home in the dark and climbed the stairs to let herself inside. She went through her usual routine of washing her face and changing into pajamas, but before she climbed into bed, she had a promise to uphold.

She was quiet as a mouse as she shuffled down the hallway and poked her head through the cracked door. Both of her parents were in bed, but the lights were on and they were both sitting up.

"Hey," she called softly, pulling at their attention. "I'm home, but I think I'm going to go to bed. I'm really tired."

Agatha's lips lifted minutely in a ghost of a smile as Rio lightly patted the bed; it was a request for a hug.

With a light nod, Dani pushed open the door and crawled onto the space between them. Unsurprisingly, they both caved in on her, hugging her tightly between them.

"We love you, Dani Banani," Rio teased softly, kissing the top of her head.

"We do," Agatha agreed, giving her daughter a tight squeeze.

She wanted to be mad. She wanted to be petulant and defiant and demand answers, but she was simply too tired.

"I love you too," she murmured softly, lifting her head to glance from one mom to the other. "But I'm exhausted. I'll see you in the morning, hm?"

Agatha nodded first and Rio placed another kiss, this one to her forehead, before she leaned back so their offer their final goodnights. 

When Dani ventured down the hallway and climbed into her bed a moment later, she let herself cry again. She cried over her confusion. She cried over the way it felt like she was being left out of important conversations. She cried that her momma didn't feel as though she could be honest. She cried for every day that passed where Nicky couldn't find his way to them. She cried because she could.

She also cried until she fell asleep.

The next morning, Dani awoke to a sweet smell in the air and a soft tapping on her door.

"Yeah?" she grumbled, reaching up to wipe at her face as her brain realigned with reality.

"It's me," Agatha called before she opened the door. "Came to tell you mom made waffles. And I went and grabbed your favorite jam from the farmer's market this morning."

Damn.

They read her like a fucking book the night before.

"And why did you do that?" Dani asked sleepily as she pushed herself into a sitting position.

Agatha's lips turned down at the corners and she glanced toward the bed as if to silently ask to sit there. Just as silently, Dani nodded her head. When Agatha placed herself in front of her, she didn't waste a moment picking up her hands.

"Because I lied to you yesterday."

It was impressive, really. Dani convinced herself they didn't feel the need to be honest with her, but that wasn't it at all.

Like Nicky, they just hadn't been ready.

Thankfully, they came around first.

"About?" Dani asked as if she did not already know.

"I didn't go to the hospital. I went to the jail. To talk to the woman who took your brother."

Both pairs of blue eyes honed in on one another, locking in the space between them. Dani remained rather placid in her reaction, not letting the betrayal she'd felt the day before touch her expression. Her lips twisted slightly as she searched for what to say.

"And... How did that go?" Again, it was pointless to ask, but she didn't exactly want to admit to eavesdropping, no matter how forthcoming her momma was being.

"As well as expected. I left angry and..." Agatha paused and Dani knew why. 

It was the hardest part to say out loud.

"I saw your brother. He was coming into the jail as I was leaving. It... I didn't speak to him, just let him be." Agatha's voice shook as she spoke in a way that caused Dani to grip at her hands. "I wanted to. But I knew I couldn't. He... He has to come to us."

Dani knew she was right, but it was killing her to see how much it was hurting her momma to say it out loud.

"I know. And you know. And mom knows. But... Was there at least something good about yesterday that came from her coffee with Gabi?" There she was again, Steadfast Dani always trying to find ways to soften the blows.

"Yes," Agatha answered, reaching up to wipe at the corner of an eye. "But I'll let mom tell you about it over waffles."

Dani smiled, a soft smile that didn't quite reach her eyes.

"I'd like that."

When Sunday rolled around, Dani knew it was time to head back to her apartment. 

She missed it, missed George, and honestly even missed attending classes. It had become apparent that they were doing nothing more than playing a waiting game and her life could not continue to stand still with graduation fast approaching.

She kissed her moms on the cheeks and set off back to the city, happy to nestle in on the first night with a movie and her best friend showing up with popcorn.

Getting back to class was nice, but it was also nice to enjoy a night out here and there. 

By Thursday, Dani needed a drink.

After class, she shot a text to George that she was going to the gym and suggested they should meet at their favorite bar after for a cocktail or two. George's agreement was easy, but as fate would have it, those were not Dani's plans for the evening.

She realized as much when, as she was briskly walking down the sidewalk with her head tucked an eyes on her phone, she ran directly into someone.

Immediately, she was panicking; it was completely her fault for not paying attention. She needed to focus more, even if it felt impossible.

It felt even more impossible when her eyes lifted to the face of her unintended victim and her blood ran cold in her veins.

There, standing a foot in front of her, was her brother.

Nick. Nicky. Nikolai. Nicholas. Nik.

It didn't matter what his name was.

He was right there.

When their eyes met and time stood still around them, there was an eternal silence that dropped over them like an insulated blanket. It sealed them away, locked them in a pocket of time where nothing else existed.

Then, he spoke.

"Dani?"

 

Chapter End Notes

thank you for all the love. you are all so appreciated by me.

Chapter 12: Square One Instead

Chapter Notes

You've all waited for it...

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Nick.

Panic.

Immediate fucking panic.

It was all Nick could feel as it flooded every single inch of his bodily form.

He was staring down into the eyes of someone he had only seen photos of, photos with captions wishing him a happy birthday and a good year, photos of a life he never got to live. He was staring into the eyes of a woman who had quite a list of accomplishments beneath her name all before she even started college.

He was staring down into the eyes of his little sister.

A little sister he wasn't sure how to face, even with her standing directly in front of them.

And yet, he spoke anyway.

"Dani?" he asked, as if he needed absolute certainty it was her name.

It had to be. She looked too much like the girl in the photos to not be her. 

When she nodded, it felt like every bit of wind had been knocked out of him. The panic was even worse at the confirmation; he felt trapped. 

What did he do when he felt trapped?

He ran.

He tried to step to the side, as if to walk away, but was stopped when a gentle hand touched the chest of his button down. It was just supposed to be a quick trip to the bookstore and then back home. There was something he wanted to learn more about in regards to work, but right then, he hardly knew how to breathe let alone remember what his plans previously were.

"Please," she bequeathed, her tone almost pitiful. "Please don't go. Can I just... Can I just buy you a drink or something? We don't have to talk but..." Her lips twisted and she looked him in the eye again. 

Could she see his fear? Could she see him panicking? Could she see that he had no fucking idea what to say to her when his thoughts were crashing and colliding into one another?

"I just want to sit next to you. Even if you don't know what to say. And... I don't have to say anything either. We can just share a drink. No conditions."

Although she was younger than him, Nick could hear the wisdom and comfort in her voice. She spoke with the tone of an elder, of someone with a vast knowledge of what the world should look like. It made no sense; she was barely old enough to drink. Yet, there she stood with that honest look in her eyes, begging him to simply share space with her.

"I don't... It's not --"

"I mean it when I say we don't have to talk. I just want to spend time with you."

Hearing her beg was doing the impossible: it was tugging at his heart instead of being devoured by his head.

He knew he should have said no, should have gone to the bookstore to get what he needed and returned home to Gabi, but he couldn't.

How could he?

Not with his flesh and blood sister so fucking close.

"O-Okay. I... I need to text my girlfriend and I can't stay long, but... Okay."

The relief on her face was palpable. Nick could almost feel it. It broke something in him; all she wanted was a few moments of his time. She didn't want to make him listen to what she had to say, didn't want to force him to open up. She simply wanted to buy him a drink and sit next to him while they indulged in alcohol and silence.

"I know a good spot," she offered with a friendly smile and gave a nod, encouraging him to text his girlfriend. It could have come across as pushy, but it felt... warm. It felt gentle.

"Lead the way," he returned with a soft nod of his own as he fished out his phone.

Me: Hey, baby. I'm going to grab
a drink with a friend. I'll be back
home when I'm done. Promise 
to not over-do it. I love you.

He pressed send and took in a deep breath, following after the smaller dark-haired woman. As he went to stow the phone in his pocket again, her felt it vibrate.

Mi amor: Okay, baby. If you need me to 
come grab you in an uber, let me know.
I love you too.

He smiled warmly at the message and looked ahead, realizing Dani was still just a couple of steps in front of him, weaving through the early evening crowds. He couldn't help the way his chest squeezed when she looked back to make sure he was still behind her, worry in her eyes even if she didn't let it touch her face.

They walked for only a few minutes longer until she stopped in front of a small bar wedged between a bodega and a stamp shop and pulled the door open.

Nick knew that bar.

It was one he and Gabi spent a little time at with friends every now and again.

The Anchor.

Fucking ironic.

They slid onto stools with ease, the bar dimly lit by green sconced lights and neon signs. It was a tiny hole in the wall and saw little traffic; he was thankful it was the one Dani chose. It also led him to question...

How many nights had they both existed within those walls before? How many times had she been feet away and he remained clueless, probably even lamenting to his girlfriend about everything he missed out on in life? How many night had he maybe even held the door for her and not even realized?

They would never really know, and that had to be okay.

"Seven and seven for me," she requested as the bartender solicited their orders. "And whatever he wants is on me." She glanced to him as if to encourage an order.

"Jack and Coke, please."

"Wanna start a tab?" the bartender questioned, turning back to Dani. There was something about her body language, about the smile she was offering the woman next to him that almost read as... Attraction?

Dani glanced to him, her lips twitching slightly before she looked toward the woman before her. "Yeah, go ahead." 

He realized that while he had made his short stay clear, she might not be so eager to stop drinking after he left. For as out of sorts as he was and for as hard as this all felt, he knew he wasn't the only one feeling that way. It was something he'd come to realize over the days of trying to parse things out with Gabi. They were slow-going conversations, but they were still being had, just one day at a time.

He knew, after his confrontation with Wanda, he was destroying his own life. He said as much to her in his anger and truth be told, hearing it out loud made him realize how true it was.

Shutting out the woman who loved him was a terrible choice. Not trying to find a way to more forward was a terrible choice. Being too afraid to make contact with people he knew longed for his presence was also a terrible choice, but that one was a little less in his control.

After a moment of silence, the drinks were placed in front of them and he watched as Dani reached for hers and held it up without a word.

In return, he tapped the edge of his glass to her and took a slow pull from it before setting it down on the bar top before him. His eyes landed on the television mounted to the wall, but they eventually dropped to the mirror in front of them.

In the reflection, Dani was looking at a different television. He could tell in his periphery that her leg was bouncing as a result of her nerves.

He should say something.

He should soothe her.

But how?

He took a deep breath and tried anyway despite having no idea.

"It's okay," he began, leaning a little closer to her to make sure his voice carried. "I'm not going to try and fight you." The softest chuckle left him and Dani turned her head to take him in, surveying him.

"I... It's not that. I'm just..."

"It's a lot," he admitted.

"It is. And... I don't even know what to call you."

Hearing those words from her lips felt like a punch to the chest, something that cracked his sternum wide open. It was a conversation had with Wanda, and something that ran unspoken between himself and Gabi, but Dani asking him what his name should be was almost earth-shattering.

But he had an answer. He just needed to tell her.

"You can call me Nick."

She grinned, a full and wide grin that showed how happy the permission made her.

"With or without a 'c'?" she asked, though he could tell she was joking.

His little sister was joking with him.

It was the strangest feeling, but he chose to feed back into her energy.

"Does it really matter?"

She took a sip of her drink and eyed him for a moment, deciding upon her answer. "No, I guess it doesn't."

They both chuckled, but nothing else followed. They were taking turns looking from television to mirror, trying to assess the situation and how best to handle it. It was what she asked for, but the one instance he caught her studying him in the reflection, he realized something.

She told him they didn't have to talk and she meant it. But the more they didn't talk, the more he felt like he wanted to. 

He was quiet only another minute or so longer before he finally found his voice.

"Can I ask you something?" he posed before washing the taste of the question away with a pull from his glass.

"I would like it if you did."

The way she spoke, she was so articulate and so intentional with her tone. It was clear she was trying to keep herself calm and even to prevent from running him off. From the look behind the look in her eyes, he could tell walking out too soon would crush her.

"Why did you ask me to come share a drink with you if you didn't want to ask me anything?" It was not a harsh inquiry, but rather an honest one. All he wanted was to understand.

Dani tossed back some of her drink and turned to face him a little more, tilting her head at him in observation.

"Because I think I just want you to see that whatever perception of us you have, it's just that. Your perception."

For a moment, Nick simply blinked at her.

So young, so studied, and so fucking profound.

That was his little sister.

She was right. He created an idea of them in his head, that they would want more out of him than he could give or have certain expectations of who he should have become over who he was. But that wasn't a reality. The reality was he didn't know. He didn't know because he was too afraid of giving them the chance and not being what they wanted.

He was prioritizing his fear over progress.

He sighed, looking down into his glass.

"You guys probably think I'm an asshole for taking so long..." he mused. He couldn't quite bring himself to look at her. Although... He should have known what her answer would be based on her first one.

"That's your perception," she reminded him, tapping softly at her glass while she considered. She turned toward the bar again and looked at him via the reflection in an attempt to take some pressure off of him. "The truth is... We just hope it's some day. We don't care if it's tomorrow, or the day after, or next month. We just want to be in your life."

It was calm and measured, but Nick could hear just how much she meant it. She wasn't lying or making things up to try and pacify him. She was being honest, telling him not what he wanted to hear, but what he needed to hear.

"I just..." he tried but the words tasted bitter. "I don't know how yet."

It was a soft admission, but he could see it land with the woman next to him.

"It's okay. Because they'll wait. We all will. Because all we want is just a chance to know you, and we're okay with that being on your time. As long as... That's an eventual plan."

A soft chuckle left him as his head hung.

"If it wasn't, I don't think I would have agreed to this." It wasn't snappy or rude; it was little more than fact.

"That's fair," Dani returned, her voice soft and rich as she slipped right back into the act of trying to soothe him as opposed to agitate him. "I didn't mean anything by it. No push. No demand. Just... Time."

Time.

That was all he'd taken from them since he found out, wasn't it?

He'd been hiding away in his bed, hiding from everyone and everything that wasn't Gabriela, and even then, he'd kept her at bay for some time.

"The truth is," Dani started, "that they're never going to not want you. Mom has made up every single possible version of you in her head and she loves all of them. Momma looks for you in every face she sees." Dani paused and the unspoken stayed that way between them; they both knew he'd seen Agatha that day, but neither of them felt the need to say it out loud. "They just want to learn who you are, who you want to be."

"But if I take too long..." he began, but Dani was quick to gingerly wave him off.

"Time is time, Nick. It's always going to be there for however much of it you wish to take. If you want to stave it off for as long as you can, everyone gets it, even if it sucks. But if you told me right now to book train tickets to Newark, I'd do it. Because it's all up to you. But I also know that you just aren't ready and that's okay."

She was being so fucking understanding and he didn't get it. So maybe he needed to try to get it, to understand.

"Can I ask you something else?" he posed finally after a few stalled minutes of quiet.

"Yes."

"Will you tell me about them?"

The kindness in Dani's eyes as she turned to face him nearly took him under.

"I'd love to."

Dani.

There was something so... undemanding about the interaction the two of them were sharing while sitting at that bar. 

Dani wasn't pushing him; she wasn't making him answer questions or asking him to pose his own. She wasn't forcing his hand or making him do anything he wasn't ready to do. He could have turned her down when she made the offer, but he made the choice to accept instead.

He was trying.

That much was clear.

Based on what her mom disclosed over waffles, the idea of actually running into him hadn't crossed Dani's mind. He was stuck in bed, wallowing in his grief and shutting out the world as far as she knew.

But he wasn't.

He was sitting right next to her asking her to tell him about their parents.

"Well," she began, still looking at him though she traced a finger around the rim of her glass. "I don't know what you know. But momma -- Agatha -- is a neurosurgeon. One of the highest praised in the state. We were actually... We were at an awards ceremony where she was being honored when we got the news about you."

She watched him carefully as she started to reveal a little more about what he hadn't had the chance to know, trying to gauge where the stopping point might be.

"Mom -- Rio -- is a chef. Well, not professionally anymore but she used to own her own catering company. She..." Dani hesitated, her lips pressing firmly for a moment before she continued. "She sold it when I was born to stay home with me. But she still cooks all the time. And sometimes burns the pasta sauce. Which... Momma says Panera is a lifesaver on those nights."

The gentlest laughter fell between them at the admission; it truly was funny, but it would have been funnier if he had a better idea of who Rio and Agatha were.

"They got married a few years before you were born and have obviously been together ever since. They've had the same house for thirty years almost and have done too many renovations to count, but it'll always be home." She took a soft breath, tilting her head as she watched him. She was careful as she chose her next words, still of the mind she did not want to spook him.

"There's always a place for you there."

She could see the impact it had on him; for a moment, his expression wavered and a struck gleam crossed over his eyes. He clearly hadn't been expecting the offer, but Dani knew he severely underestimated how badly they all ached to be present in his life. For her, it was a goal she'd had since she was little.

For her -- their -- parents, it was something they'd held out hope for for decades. It wasn't like they decorated it or filled it with things they thought he would like, but there was still a room with navy walls and a queen sized bed inside. It bore no photos or art, nothing to make it stand out. It was simply a spare room most of the time, but Dani knew what it really was.

It was a place for him to come home to, if ever the opportunity presented itself.

"I don't want to keep disappointing them," he voiced, looking into his drink. For some reason he did not quite understand, it hurt to look at her when he made such loaded admissions. "But I'm not ready. I don't know what to say. I don't know how to act... I just... Don't know."

Dani could feel his words in her chest; he was so fucking scared and she had no idea how to properly ease his fears. She could sit there all night telling him anything he asked to hear, but she knew his time was likely up as soon as his drink was finished.

Then, it was as he tossed the rest of it back.

"I know this might sound like ridiculous cliche bullshit, but I'll be real with you. Just be yourself. That's all anyone in this situation hopes to get from you."

That was the wrong thing to say.

"How am I supposed to do that when who I am is so tied into the biggest lie of the century?"

Okay, so that was a little dramatic. He got that from Agatha.

Having any kind of knee-jerk reaction to his statement wasn't going to help either of them. She knew the likely outcome here was that he would go home, maybe take her number, and hopefully text her within the coming weeks to say he'd finally gotten himself where he needed to be. Still, she was there for whatever he needed in the moment.

"I can't tell you how to feel, Nick. I can only tell you that we've celebrated your birthday every year since I was little. I can tell you that momma still carries around your laminated baby photo in her wallet. I can tell you that every Christmas, we light a candle for you. I can tell you that when I was younger, you were my imaginary friend. I can tell you literally anything in the world, but it's not up to me. And it's okay if you're not there yet."

When he winced at the part where she talked about having him as an imaginary friend, she was afraid she might have pushed too hard. Would he get up and leave? Would he call her a liar and tell her she was making it up to somehow gain favor with him?

Looking over to her, he did not a single one of those things.

Instead, he asked a question that nearly stopped her heart in her chest.

"But what if I am?"

Was he fucking with her? Was he giving her false hope for... whatever reason?

"'What if you are' what?" she asked dumbly, blinking at him.

His nervous hazel eyes darted over her face, trying to find... something, but she couldn't tell what it was. Was it possible he changed his mind so quickly? What was the reasoning? Why was he suddenly on board with moving forward when she'd nearly begged him to join her for a drink?

"What if I'm there?"

Holy shit, he was being serious.

"Like... How there?" she questioned, tucking her bottom lip between her teeth to chew on it nervously.

"Is your offer to grab train tickets still on the table?"

HOLY FUCKING SHIT. 

WHAT?!

"I... I mean --" she fumbled, completely stunned by the idea that he was ready to take it all on, to go to Newark and meet their parents. It was such a one-eighty that it was giving her whiplash, but she didn't care. She knew she could not waste too much time balking or he might backtrack.
