She couldn't have that when so much progress was instantaneously being made. "You're serious?"

It wasn't so much Dani doubting him as it was her wanting to make absolutely sure before she booked tickets and double checked their parents were home.

"What's the point in continuing to wait? If it goes half as well as... this," he indicated by waving a hand between them, "then what do I have to lose?"

It moved her, truly, to hear him speak so honestly. She knew he was scared, knew he might still snap and be defensive when it came to sensitive subjects, but he was trying so fucking hard.

"Then yes, my offer is still on the table."

Nick's lips lifted in the first genuine smile Dani had witnessed from him that night.

"Can you book three? I'd like to bring my girlfriend, too."

"Of course."

Rio.

The days came to pass after her meeting with Gabi and while she'd been gifted with so much to hold onto, Rio's hopes that Nicky was going to come around started dwindling once more. It wasn't that she was hopeless but she was coming to the realization that time was the be all end all. 

They were going through something that couldn't be forced, something that just had to happen naturally without any undue pressure. It was hard to stomach, especially with every day that ticked by, but it was their reality and Rio understood as much all too well.

That night in particular, she prepared chicken cordon bleu for dinner and knew Agatha was going to be late, timing it roughly to when she would arrive. When her phone dinged from the kitchen table, she was certain it was her wife; although she already announced she was on her way home, surely something came up that would delay her.

When she scooped it up off the table and swiped it open, Rio was rather surprised to see an awaiting message from Dani.

It wasn't so much she didn't expect to hear from Dani as it was the contents of the message itself.

Boogerbutt: Hey are you and momma
home?

Rio's brow wrinkled slightly as she typed her response.

Me: I am home and momma is on 
her way. Is everything okay?

Dani's return was lightning quick.

Boogerbutt: Yes. I'm coming home.
I just wanted to make sure you
were both there.

Me: For what purpose? Are you
bringing George with you?

Boogerbutt: No George tonight.
But you'll both be there in
maybe an hour?

Me: Yes. Should I leave dinner out
for you?

Boogerbutt: No, I've been drinking 
a little. Not hungry. But I will there 
asap! I love you!

Okay... What was she up to? With her brow still creased, Rio fired off a text message to her wife.

Me: Are you close to home? I just
got a series of very strange
text messages from our 
daughter. She's coming home
tonight.

There was a delay as Agatha surely waited until she was stopped to respond.

LOML: I just stopped for a bottle of
white to go with dinner. I should be 
there in about fifteen. What makes
the messages so strange?

Me: Well... She said she's coming
home, she didn't want to eat 
because she's been drinking and
she was adamant about making
sure both of us would be here.

LOML: Well... Why is that weird?
Seems pretty normal for her.

Me: I don't know. I guess it just
felt a little off. But I'm sure 
everything is fine and I'm just
being annoying mom.

LOML: My love, I'm *definitely* 
the annoying mom. I promise.

Rio laughed softly, giving a shrug to no audience. Agatha wasn't wrong.

Me: If you ask Dani, maybe. Come
home to me, baby. See you soon.
I love you.

LOML: I love you too, Rio. See 
you in 5.

As promised, Agatha arrived five minutes later to a prepped dinner and awaiting wine glasses. They sat at the dining room table and savored the meal along with the wine, lightly discussing the potential outcomes of what their daughter was up to.

She could be wily, that was for certain, but Rio felt as though there was more to it. It felt like Dani was being cagey in her text messages, like there was something important on her mind that she simply wouldn't say outright. It was mildly frustrating, but Rio knew if they were patient, they would surely get answers.

She wasn't on a bender.
She wasn't injured.
She seemed sane enough.

So what could possibly be so urgent she had to come home in the middle of the week with little warning?

With a refill to their wine glasses, the hour mark passed since the last message Dani sent. The two of them migrated to the living room, but Agatha was quick to announce she wanted a change of clothes. With a soft kiss and a lightly playful tap to her hip, Rio ushered her on and suggested throwing on a movie. With an easy agreement, Agatha disappeared up the stairs.

Not a minute later, there was a soft rattling of the deadbolt on the front door and it swung open, drawing Rio's attention in spite of knowing already who it was.

Or, she thought she knew who it was.

Seeing Dani made sense, but when she spoke, that did not make sense.

"I brought a couple of friends with me," she offered, though it barely made sense as it spilled between grinning teeth. When she stepped aside as Rio climbed to her feet, she stopped dead in her tracks as her daughter's guests came through the door.

There stood one familiar face and one semi-familiar face. 

Gabi and Nicky.

Her son and his girlfriend.

The same girlfriend who gave her hope less than a week before.

She couldn't have known back then how honest she was being, but Rio had. She just didn't think things would happen so quickly.

"What... How...?" Rio managed, but it didn't matter.

She didn't actually care.

Not when her son was standing in her foyer.

She was cautious in her approach as she stepped toward him, unsure what move was the best first move to make.

So she asked.

"Can... Can I hug you?" she asked him quietly; her eyes were filled with tears but she was trying desperately not to cry them.

So was he as he nodded his head.

Her arms wrapped around his built frame, fighting herself on her urge to cling to him for dear life. She wanted to squeeze him until her arms grew tired, to hold him and tell him she was so happy to meet him, but nothing was actually coming out. Well, nothing aside from the rivers of tears flowing down her cheeks. They only worsened when, over his shoulder, Rio caught Gabi's eye.

Her smile was genuine, but the way she nodded her head told Rio they'd finally got what they wanted: It was his idea, and they finally had him back.

Just as she moved to let him go, she heard a soft squeak of the stairs behind her and the quietest gasp of disbelief.

Rio released him and stepped back to behold the look on Agatha's face; it was little more than pure shock and lacked almost any color. As she came down the last few steps and paced her way forward, Rio could see the battle she was in to not completely crumble. Her arms opened slowly in question and much like he'd done with Rio, Nick simply folded into her.

"Oh, my boy," Agatha breathed, tucking her face into the side of his head. 

"Welcome home."

 

Chapter End Notes

...here it is.

reunited at last!
thank you again for all the love and kudos and comments
this humble writer appreciates you
now the real healing begins

Chapter 13: Saw It So Clear

Chapter Notes

life be lifing and the ao3 curse struck me in regards to health so im only able to work on stuff when my brain is working correctly. SO I PROMISE THIS ISNT DONE YET it just might take me a little longer to update. thank you all for your patience and understanding. i truly appreciate each and every one of you.

Nick.

It was just a conversation. It was just an agreement to share a drink with a woman that had a biological relation to him.

So how was he standing in the middle of his parents' home, meeting them for the first time?

The moment Dani stepped aside and Rio was on the other side of her, something in him broke. Her expression was so calm and gentle, so deliberately unnerving, but he could see the truth in her eyes. The truth was that she was truly seeing him for the first time in twenty-five years that he imagined had to have been unbearably long for her. He did not have it in him to ask where Agatha was, especially not when the woman before him asked if she could hug him.

He'd come that far; who would he have been to deny her? Who would he have been to tell her no after turning up at her doorstep?

Some part of Nick still didn't fully understand. He knew what was happening, but in his mind he was still sitting at that bar listening to Dani give him every reason he needed to stop waiting. He was staving off the unknown, sure, but at what cost? He was torturing himself, torturing his girlfriend, and he was torturing a family who only wanted to know him so they could earn the right to love him.

Love.

Aside from Gabi, was any form of love in his life real?

The short answer was that little existed outside of Gabi, and what did exist outside of Gabi was... Well, Wanda.

Of course he had his friends, their friends, but Wanda told him countless times that she loved him.

Did she?

Did she really?

How could she when their entire existence was nothing more than a fabrication of her making?

The moment he felt Rio's strong arms lock around him, something in him shifted.

She didn't need to say it. She didn't need to tell him. Right then, as she hugged him -- albeit him being a few inches taller than her -- to her chest and clung to him for dear life, he could feel it: She didn't need a conversation with him or to know anything about him at all to just... love him.

That embrace could have lasted thirty seconds or thirty years (Nick wasn't entirely sure which), but the sound of the stairs creaking broke them out of the moment. The mother in his arms broke her firm hold to step away, revealing the mother he'd seen before.

There had been that moment, that very brief moment in the jail when she walked right by him. Their eyes met then and she saw him for all he was; she saw him as the scared little boy who was just looking for answers. Back then, she had a choice. She could have upended his life, tried to push her way in, but she didn't. No, she chose to walk away, to give him space and breathing room. She walked right out of that jail and did not come back and for him, he had to believe it was because she respected him and his right to process.

Whether it was the truth was neither here nor there, but it made the moment they locked eyes across the living room a little more weightless.

Nick had been so scared to face them, so afraid of not being what they wanted... Right then, he could see that all they actually really wanted was him and only him, no matter the form he came in. 

He was stalk still as he watched Agatha's approach, not entirely sure what to do. The moment her arms opened in silent question, he had his answer. He took no more than two steps forward and folded into her like a wet blanket, her arms wrapping around her tightly. 

"Welcome home." 

She said it so easily and yet, it hit him with far more force than anyone could have guessed, and it showed in the choked but soft sob that escaped him. He was trying to keep his composure and brave his way through it, but there was something about the weight of their predicament that finally careened straight into him.

These women, Dani included, just wanted to love him. The only person who was stopping it from happening was... him.

Maybe he didn't know what to call them yet, and maybe he didn't know much about them, but he had learned enough from Dani in the bar to know that they were good people and they'd done an immaculate job in raising her. She was a little messy in her delivery and did not have the softest of hands when it came to being sensitive, but she got her point across to make him want to stop the bullshit.

Sure, maybe it was self-satisfying to cave to the depression, but it only hurt everyone else, including the person he loved most.

But this?

This was the payoff.

For every moment he'd spent scared and stuck, it was a moment wasted where he could have known what the true hug of a mother felt like. Because Wanda... Well, she wasn't the hugging type and never had been. She didn't squeeze him tight and tell him she was proud of him; it was always a head pat or a light rub of the shoulder. She didn't wrap him in her arms when he was hurt or upset and tell him everything would be okay: it was always a 'sleep it off, tomorrow will be better' and nothing more.

Right then, not having done a thing to earn it, his mothers were choosing to hug him, to hold him and let him feel the way they loved him and had loved him his entire life. He didn't need to be present for them to keep doing it.

It took him more than a minute of feeling Agatha's embrace to finally find his voice. 

"I'm sorry," he breathed quietly into her shoulder.

Her response?

It was the softest laugh as she pulled back to look up at him.

"Why are you sorry?" she asked kindly. She started to raise her hand as if to cup his face, but stopped herself and let it settle on his shoulder instead. It might have been too much too soon, but Nick found warmth and comfort in even what she offered.

It was a good question, one that had many answers.

There was one thing he was most sorry for, though.

"I'm... I'm sorry I didn't say anything... When I saw you that day... I..."

"N-- Hey," she corrected quickly, not having any real idea what it was he wanted to be called. "It's okay. I didn't say anything either. Because I... Didn't want to make things harder on you. I just hoped that by giving you space... You'd make it here eventually. And I was right."

Her blue eyes, her pink cheeks, that sweet curl of her lips were all soothing in the most astounding ways. Arguably, he did not know this woman, but he knew that she carried him for nine months and then fought to bring him home for twenty-five years. No matter who he was, what he'd become... he was still her son. He was their son.

And he was home.

For a moment as she looked down at him, he could see the initial panic in her gaze; now that he was there, what did they do?

"Would you all like some wine? We can relax in the living room with a glass," came Rio's soft suggestion from behind him.

Truthfully, Nick didn't want to drink anymore. He wasn't drunk, but he didn't want to get there and risk losing any piece of the memory they would be building that night. He was still of clear mind enough that he wanted it to stay that way; he needed to be present.

"Water for me," he offered, glancing back at her as Agatha finally lifted her hand from his shoulder.

"Me too," Dani chimed softly from her place next to Gabi at the far side of the room.

"Wine sounds great," came Gabi next, though there was something in her eyes as she looked to Rio that Nick did not quite understand. It was soft, questioning. It didn't feel significant, just... different. "Would you like some help?"

"I'd like that," Rio affirmed with a nod before glancing back to Agatha. "And you my love?"

"A glass of red would be nice, thank you."

There was a stilled moment of silence where three things were happening at once:

1) Rio and Agatha were looking at each other and fighting for their lives to not burst into tears at finally having their dreams realized.
2) Nick and Gabi were locked eye-to-eye across the room with hope written on their faces.
3) Dani was beholding the entire scene before her with a sense of gratefulness and genuine reverie. 

This was it. It finally happened.

Could it be said that the only place to go was up?

Nick wasn't sure, but in that moment, it sure felt like it.

Breaking from their respective bonds, both Rio and Gabi looked to one another and gave a nod, heading toward the kitchen to prepare drinks. When Nick turned around to face Agatha once more, she was already holding out an indicatory hand toward the living room. 

"Please, make yourself comfortable."

It was so soft, so warm, but Nick could hear something more.

She was nervous.

Well... 

So was he.

Slowly he shuffled forward, placing himself on one side of a loveseat while Agatha took her place in the middle of the couch. Even before Dani moved to take a spot on one side of her, Nick realized it was because she needed to be surrounded by the familiar to ground her in reality. It was the same reason he chose the loveseat and not the chair; when she returned, he needed Gabi by his side.

"And how did this come to be, I wonder," Agatha mused aloud, though as Nick looked up, it was to the sight of her looking over at Dani while lightly digging an elbow in her shoulder.

A pair of startlingly blue eyes raised to him and Dani simply smiled.

"You run into the people you're meant to run into, I guess," she answered honestly, but Nick saw it as something else.

It was his chance, the first chance to show his mother a piece of who he truly was.

"Quite literally, when you're both not paying attention." His voice was a little unsteady, but he sold the joke all the same the moment Agatha began to laugh.

It was a bright but gentle sound, one that caused Nick's heart to squeeze in his chest.

"Wait, you actually physically ran into each other?" she asked looking from Dani to Nick and back again.

"I was texting George," Dani replied sheepishly with a gentle shrug.

"And I just... Wasn't paying attention. Might have been doing that a lot lately," he offered with a light chuckle. "But... She offered me silence and a drink. But the more we sat there without saying anything... The more I realized I didn't want to do that."

Agatha's smile was kind, but it was sincere. "That's the thing about her... She gets us to do things we don't want to do by telling us we don't have to do them."

She was clearly speaking about herself and Rio, but the smallest part of Nick's heart warmed about the possibility that he could now be a part of that 'us' too.

"That's not --! Okay... yeah. That is what I do, isn't it?" Dani tried to refute, but she folded in the middle of her own argument as she leaned into her mother.

Their mother.

Agatha.

Mom? Momma?

He didn't know yet, and that was okay.

"Alright!" came a call from his left as Rio emerged with two wine glasses pinched in her fingers on one hand and a glass of water in her other. Right behind her was Gabi with a glass of red for herself and a large glass of water for him.

"Thank you," he told her softly as she placed herself next to him and handed it over. To punctuate his statement with a newfound sense of bravery, he pressed his lips to her cheek, smiling softly as he pulled away.

As everyone settled, so did something else: the silence.

For just a moment, all that was truly needed was appreciation of where they found themselves and how they'd gotten there.

Rio.

As Rio settled into Agatha's side, her timed and tapered interaction with Gabriela was still replaying over and over in her mind, stuck on a loop.

"How did this happen?" Rio asked in hushed tones as she pulled glasses and cups down from the cabinet. She was fighting tears, but only the happiest ones.

"I truly only have bits and pieces," Gabi admitted as she grabbed a cup to fill it with ice and water from the door of the refrigerator. "I guess they bumped into each other... She offered to buy him a drink. Two hours later he's calling me that he's on the way to pick me up. When he walked in, Dani was right behind him. I... Hardly believed my own eyes when I saw her."

She set the filled cup on the counter and began to repeat the process with the other as Rio uncorked the wine behind her.

"When he told me we were catching the next train to Newark, I... I knew what it meant. But I..."

"You haven't tole him," Rio deduced.

Gabi solemnly shook her head.

"I didn't have time."

For a moment, Rio considered as she began to fill the first of the three glasses.

"I know you don't really need me to say it, but that's probably a conversation better suited for sooner rather than later." She paused for a moment as she moved on to the second glass. "And hopefully... Tonight goes well enough that he's able to understand."

"Hopefully," Gabi agreed, placing herself at Rio's side and setting the second cup on the counter. Her hand detached from it but was only empty for a moment before Rio filled it with her own.

"You were right," she said softly. "The hope was still there. What we needed was a little more time."

"And for your spitfire of a daughter to talk some sense into him."

Rio laughed gently.

"Yeah, she's good for that most of the time."

Sitting next to her wife with Dani on the other side of Agatha, she knew it had to feel like a lot for him. Sure, he was ultimately the one to make the decision, but there was still an emotional anvil attached to the situation.

It was obvious when no one spoke.

It was because no one knew what to say. So Rio took the lead.

"What bar did you guys end up at?"

It was an easy question, one she hoped might break through the tension a little bit.

"The Anchor," Dani answered, her eyes catching his as she brandished a warm smile across her lips.

Rio caught the interaction, but it didn't seem like much until he spoke.

"We've actually been there quite a few times," he admitted, glancing down into his water. It was clear he was overwhelmed by the idea of not knowing who to look at, so he was simply trying to calibrate and get himself there.

Rio could admire that.

"Like for Halloween last year," Gabi added, giving his knee a soft squeeze.

"No way!" Dani all but shrieked. "What were you guys dressed up as?!"

Rio watched as Nick lifted his head and found his sister on the couch, a genuine grin filling his face.

"Eustice and Muriel from Courage the Cowardly Dog."

"Oh my GOD! I was the Louise who almost got kicked out for being too loud," she explained. While Rio had only half a clue what they were talking about, she realized something very important.

Their children had shared space before.

Agatha was right to be upset over how close he'd been for so long when they had no clue. They were so clueless, apparently, that Dani had been in the same bar on the same night and even saw the two of them, she just hadn't known it.

Nick's gaze scanned down the line of them as he spoke, a tender warmth laying gingerly over his tones.

"All this time, you've been so close... So close and... None of us ever knew..."

It was almost heartbreaking, honestly, to hear him be the one to point it out. Sure, not a one of them would have ever known or made the connection, but he'd been in the same tiny bar as a sister he always wanted but did not know existed and it was clearly hitting him just what it all meant.

It was hard; all of it was hard. He was taken from them, hidden away in too many corners of the world, and everyone was a little worse for wear because of it.

They all had their own struggles over it, but Rio could slowly feel in her wife's form pressed to her side that she was slowly coming to terms with it. Her muscles were easing, even if the grip she had on Rio's thigh was not. She was accepting that while their reality had been two and a half decades of pain and heartbreak and not knowing, this was their new reality; it was a reality where they got to sit together in their living room and try to hold light conversation.

"But now we do," Dani announced. "And we can do whatever we want to do with that. But I think this is a good start." 

Rio's eyes darted from her daughter to her son, truly hit by the similarities suddenly so visible due to their close proximity. Sure, Dani's face shape was drawn from her own whereas Nick's came from Agatha's pointed nose and cheekbones, and their eyes were completely different colors, but it was too apparent that they were blood related.

Her children.

Her sweet, similarly looking children.

Right there with her and Agatha, the way it should have always been.

"You're right," Nick agreed softly, his gaze landing on his mothers. "And I just... Hope it's okay to try and understand what that might be. I mean... I'm not going to run home to never be heard from again, but... This is..."

"Weird?" came Agatha's gentle question from beside her.

Something happened.

Something beautiful, something magical.

They all laughed.

All five of them.

It wasn't raucous or boisterous but fell more along the lines of a chorus of chuckles that all agreed upon the same thing. It was a sweet and treasured sound the moment it hit Rio's ears and judging by the look on her son's face, he had to be feeling close to the same.

"Yeah, weird. It's like... Where do we even start?" His voice sounded far less nervous than when he initially arrived, but Rio had a feeling it had something to do with the way his fingers were twisting mindlessly -- and perhaps a bit anxiously -- around Gabi's where they rested on his thigh. "It's... What do I ask? What do you ask? It's just..."

"It's a lot."

This time, Dani was the one to finish his sentence. "So what if you just tell us what you want us to know?"

For a moment, Rio felt like she was melting. Neither herself nor Agatha wanted to place any undue pressure on him, but Dani wasted no time in trying to be the voice of reason when both parties seemed so uncertain. She had been the glue holding their family together for a very long time, and now, she was continuing to prove that it was something she was more than happy to do, even with two new additions.

Her offer seemed to settle the young man, his posture allowing him to sink a little more into the loveseat and a little more into his girlfriend. His eyes were still moving, jumping from woman to woman, but he finally settled on Rio when he found his words.

"I work at a physical therapy clinic in the city and spend most of my time not at work with her. We go to raves, but we like concerts too. We don't have a dog but want one when we move out of the city because we don't want kids. And I..." He paused, his gaze casting down the line of them and back up again as he cleared his throat. "And I researched you all. Enough to know that... That you've celebrated my birthday every single year. And that all you've wanted is for me to be happy."

A rock leapt into Rio's throat, staunching her airflow exponentially. She was already emotional, but when he continued, she was in an active battle to not let herself burst into tears.

"So what I want you to know is that... All of this aside... I'm happy. I have a good life because I -- we -- and built it for ourselves. Not because of... her, or anything she ever did for me. But because I wanted it for myself. And I'm happy with that."

Hearing him be so honest, it moved something in Rio. He was clearly a successful young man, had a good job and a good home life. They'd spent years on end thinking about him, wondering about him, worrying about him... And all he needed them to know was that despite everything, he was happy. 

"That's all we've ever hoped for," Agatha told him, her voice low but her words sincere. "No matter where you were, we just wanted you to be happy."

For a moment, Nick just looked at her. But then again, he wasn't just looking at her. He was seeing her, assessing her, trying to figure her out. She was being so calm and kind and he was trying to figure out how to respond in kind.

"Being a kid was hard," he admitted, his stare never wavering from the woman at Rio's side. "But it has to be okay now because this is who I turned out to be. And... I was scared that you wouldn't like this version of me because it's not the one you might have imagined... But..." Finally, he tore his gaze away to look at his sister, a small smile on his lips. "Someone very wise once said... 'Every version of you is a version that is loved...' or something like that."

"You mean to tell me Dani said that?" Agatha teased, lightly poking their daughter in the ribs, eliciting a giggle at the same time.

"She's... very smart. And very wise for being so young."

"I got it from them," she managed through her giggles as she leaned into Agatha's side. 

"Well, maybe I have some things to learn yet."

Agatha.

For almost two hours -- until nearly eleven at night --- the five of them sat in their living room, drinking water and wine, as they simply held the lightest of conversations. They learned small things, like how Nick preferred pie to cake, how he sometimes got anxious in public places, how he loved eating dry cereal.

In return, he learned a little about Dani's time at Julliard and Rio's passion for cooking. He learned about Agatha's prolific career as a surgeon and smaller dynamics of their family. He asked the gentlest questions, still so timid about crossing any perceived lines.

There were no lines. There could be none. Not when he was their son and simply wanted to know them.

As exhaustion seemed to settle over them, the end of the night was drawing to a close.

"Do you think..." Nick began as he and Gabi -- hand in hand -- got to their feet, "that maybe we can come back again soon?"

For as much progress as they'd been making that night, Agatha was genuinely caught off guard by such a blatant ask. She, however, did not waste a single second in giving her response as the three of them stood as well.

"I think if you'd like to, you should come over this weekend. We were thinking about inviting Dani and her best friend over for a little cook out. We'd love it if you both joined us as well."

She said it without thought; they hadn't even brought it up to Dani yet, but she couldn't stop herself from extending the invitation. It was out of fear that if she didn't, he simply wouldn't come back even though he was asking if he could. It was irrational, but she needed to see him again. They all did. They all deserved a chance to have him in their lives.

There was a glance to his side that was met with an encouraging nod from Gabi, her agreement easy and fast. 

"We would really like that," he voiced, finally releasing Gabi's hand to step forward. That time, he was the one to open his arms up for a hug.

"Then Saturday it is," Agatha agreed, stepping into his hold as she embraced him with strong arms. Next to her, Gabi offered a strong hug to Rio. She did not hear the soft exchange between them, the one where she whispered "I will tell him," right into Rio's ear, but she could feel the warmth emanating from them even as Gabi turned to hug Dani as well.

The five of them shuffled toward the door, exchanging in one last round of embraces before Nick looked her in the eyes one last time.

"Thank you... All of you... For just..." His lips pressed as he clearly battled the tide of emotion swelling inside of him. "Thank you for accepting me."

"Oh, son," Agatha breathed at him, this time losing her battle in reaching up to lightly cup his cheek in her palm. "You never have to thank us for that. We will always accept you for who you are."

Although she was convinced the embraces were done for the night, Agatha was genuinely surprised when Nick launched at her, wrapping his arms tightly around her neck. The quickness was enough to throw her off balance, but he did not let her go far. The moment she realized he was not letting go, she had to force herself to blink back the tears at the sudden show of emotion. 

Her son loved her. He didn't have to say it, didn't have to put it into words. She could feel it.

"Go home," she soothed a moment later, finally able to force movement to lightly rub at his back. "Get some rest and let things process a little. We'll see you this weekend, hm?"

Slowly, he released his hold on her and pulled away, looking down as he offered a soft nod in return. "This weekend. And... Thank you again."

"You're always welcome," Rio voiced as she sidled up beneath Agatha's arm.

"Goodnight, everyone."

"Goodnight," Gabi added, offering a small wave as they let themselves out.

Agatha's head turned, her curious blue gaze pinning her daughter. "Are you not going back with them?" she questioned as she raised a brow to punctuate.

In answer, Dani slid beneath her other arm and laid her head on Agatha's shoulder. "I was thinking I'd stay here tonight and catch the morning train for late morning class. If that's okay."

Agatha kissed the top of her head, giving her a gentle squeeze at the same time. 

"Permission granted. You seemed to do us a solid tonight, huh?"

Rio shifted at her side, swinging around so they were better able to wrap Dani up in their arms, holding her between them like the precious gem she was.

"How do you do it?" Rio questioned in a murmur as she tucked her face into their daughter's shoulder. "How do you fix things without even trying?"

"I guess I'm just charming," Dani returned through soft giggles. "Or I just have a really trustworthy face. Considering I look like you, I'm gonna go with that."

Between the two of them, they peppered her head in at least a dozen kissed, leaving her to try and fight them off through a bout of giggles she could not control. By the time they finished, her cheeks were pink and that soft sound of her laughter began to wane.

"I'm going to go shower and then I wanna come lay with you guys for a little before bed. Is that okay?"

Realistically, Agatha knew they all had a lot to talk about and while that was probably partially where Dani's request came from, Agatha was not sure she was quite ready. She needed time to think, time to process and understand all the things they'd learned that night. 

"Yes, of course," she offered softly, brushing Dani's cheek lightly with her knuckles. "But give us a little. I'd say midnight would be good. Then we're all yours." It might not have made sense to Dani, but Agatha just... needed to breathe and did not want to have to explain as much aloud. When Dani met her blue eyes with a mirror pair, she just seemed to... get it.

"You got it, captain. See you shortly." She placed a quick peck to Agatha's cheek first and then Rio before she dramatically wiggled her way out from between them and scampered off toward the stairs and her impending shower.

Left alone for the first time that night, there was really only one thing to do.

Agatha simply folded into Rio, her face crumpling as her body began to tremble with soft sobs that she tried her hardest to choke back. The moment she felt Rio's lips on her ear and her hand smoothing over her back, it felt absolutely pointless.

"It's okay, my love," she soothed, holding Agatha a little closer. "You can cry all you need, but maybe you'd feel better if we laid down, hm?" 

Rio was right. She was always right. Agatha didn't exactly want to be having a breakdown in the middle of their home, but it was all hitting her at once just exactly what they'd experienced that night.

They had him.

He was in their lives now.

He wanted to be in their lives.

And some part of Agatha did not know what to do with that.

She sniffed softly and lifted her head from Rio's shoulder, reaching down to take one of her hands as she left her wife lead her toward the stairs and up to their room. They were both quiet and silent as they climbed into bed and Agatha found herself fastened to Rio's side, her head resting on her chest as the tears began to flow freely.

"I never thought it would happen," she admitted in the smallest whisper. Rio's fingers traced light lines along her upper arm as she pulled her closer, held her tighter.

"But it has. And will again." Rio's words were reassuring, of course, but there was something more to be said. "Because he knows. He knows we love him. And I think... I think he's going to love us, too."

Agatha wanted to argue, wanted to say Rio couldn't possibly know that, but she didn't.

She managed something else instead.

"I really hope you're right."
